1 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State v. Nunez


Docket No. 23,796A


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


129 N.M. 63; 2000-NMSC-013; 2 P.3d 264; 1999 N.M. LEXIS 388; 39 N.M. St. B. Bull. 21



December 30, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected June 8, 2000. Motions for Rehearing Denied May 10, 2000. Released for Publication May 10, 2000. As Corrected June 9, 2000.


PRIOR HISTORY: CERTIFICATIONS FROM THE NEW MEXICO COURT OF APPEALS. James L. Shuler, Frank H. Allen, Robert M. Doughty, II and Sandra A. Grisham, District Judges.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Upon certification from the New Mexico Court of Appeals, appellants, State and defendants already subjected to civil forfeiture under Controlled Substances Act, N.M. Stat. Ann. §§ 30-31-1 to -41, challenged judgments, alleging double jeopardy violations under N.M. Const. art. II, § 15, and N.M. Stat. Ann. 1978, § 30-1-10.


OVERVIEW: In five consolidated appeals, criminal defendants filed motions to dismiss criminal drug charges against them, based upon attachment of their right against double jeopardy under N.M. Const. art. II, § 15, and N.M. Stat. Ann. § 30-1-10 (1978), alleging that civil forfeiture under the Controlled Substances Act (Act), N.M. Stat. Ann. §§ 30-31-1 to -41, was penal in nature and thus, since the State had elected to obtain forfeiture before seeking criminal punishment, the State could not seek a second punishment in a criminal proceeding. In two cases, defendants' motions were granted and the State appealed. In three other cases, defendants' motions were denied, and defendants were convicted of narcotics charges. Upon certification, the Supreme Court of New Mexico reversed the convictions and affirmed the dismissals of the charges, holding that, unlike federal jurisprudence, civil forfeiture under the Act was punishment for purposes of New Mexico's protections against double jeopardy.


OUTCOME: Three convictions were reversed, and dismissals of criminal charges were affirmed, because civil forfeiture of property, such as vehicles and currency allegedly associated with the crime, was punishment and was limited by the protections against double jeopardy guaranteed by the New Mexico Constitution and the state's double-jeopardy statute.

 

2 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State v. Allen


Docket No. 23,493


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


128 N.M. 482; 2000-NMSC-002; 994 P.2d 728; 1999 N.M. LEXIS 378; 39 N.M. St. B. Bull. 3



December 1, 1999 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Motion for Rehearing Denied January 6, 2000. Released for Publication January 6, 2000. As Corrected January 29, 2000. Certiorari Denied June 5, 2000, Reported at: 2000 U.S. LEXIS 3878.
Writ of certiorari denied Allen v. New Mexico, 530 U.S. 1218, 120 S. Ct. 2225, 147 L. Ed. 2d 256, 2000 U.S. LEXIS 3878 (2000)
Habeas corpus proceeding at, Remanded by Allen v. Lemaster, 2012 NMSC 1, 2011 N.M. LEXIS 549 (N.M., 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF SAN JUAN COUNTY. W. Byron Caton, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed Defendant's sentence and his convictions for first degree murder, kidnapping, and attempted CSP.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment of the District Court of San Juan County (New Mexico) convicting him of first degree murder, first degree kidnapping, and attempted criminal sexual penetration, and sentencing him to death under the Capital Felony Sentencing Act, N.M. Stat. Ann. §§ 31-20A-1 to 31-20A-6.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was sentenced to death under the Capital Felony Sentencing Act, N.M. Stat. Ann. §§ 31-20A-1 to 31-20A-6, after he tied up a 17-year-old girl, attempted to rape her, and killed her. Defendant argued, among other things, that there was insufficient evidence to prove the charge and aggravating circumstances against him, and that the trial court erred in instructing the jury and in sentencing him. The court found sufficient evidence to sustain the charge, because the force used to kidnap was not typical of attempted rape, and additional force was used to kill the girl. The court found that the jury had been properly instructed, and a death sentence was proper, because the aggravating circumstances, murder in the commission of a kidnapping and murder of a witness, had been properly weighed against the mitigating circumstances of defendant's remorse and his age.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment, holding that sufficient evidence existed to convict, that trial court did not err in sentencing defendant to death where it properly weighed aggravating and mitigating circumstances, and properly instructed the jury. Defendant's remaining claims were meritless.

 

3 of 795 DOCUMENTS


ACLU v. City of Albuquerque


Docket No. 24,763


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


128 N.M. 315; 1999-NMSC-044; 992 P.2d 866; 1999 N.M. LEXIS 342



November 17, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication December 7, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: CERTIFICATION FROM THE NEW MEXICO COURT OF APPEALS. Robert L. Thompson, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: District court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant city appealed from the order of the district court (New Mexico) granting plaintiff's motion for summary judgment holding that city curfew ordinance violated state constitution and was preempted by state law; plaintiffs cross-appealed denials on other asserted grounds and of attorney fees and expenses.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs filed for relief from defendant's curfew that curtailed late-night activities of juveniles. Because none of the plaintiffs were stopped, arrested, cited, or prosecuted for violation of the curfew, defendant claimed that they lacked standing to challenge the ordinance. On appeal the court held that one need not first expose oneself to actual arrest or prosecution to challenge a criminal statute's constitutionality. The Children's Code, N.M. Stat. Ann. § 32A-1-1 et seq., and the Delinquency Act, N.M. Stat. Ann. § 32A-2-1 et seq., preempted defendant's curfew because it established criminal sanctions of incarceration and fines for juvenile activity which was not unlawful when committed by adults. The enforcement program was likewise invalid which authorized police to take children into custody without either a court order or a fact-specific showing to meet the conditions of N.M. Stat. Ann. § 32A-3B-3(A)(4). The court was unwilling to expand the award of attorney fees.


OUTCOME: Summary judgment affirmed because state law preempted defendant's curfew ordinance that established criminal sanctions for juvenile activity that was not unlawful when committed by adults; defendant's enforcement program was likewise invalid that did not follow statutory procedures; and court was unwilling to expand award of attorney fees.

 

4 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State v. Clark


Docket No. 23,832


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


128 N.M. 119; 1999-NMSC-035; 990 P.2d 793; 1999 N.M. LEXIS 278; 38 N.M. St. B. Bull. 40



July 8, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected October 26, 1999. Motion for Rehearing Denied September 22, 1999. Released for Publication September 22, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF GRANT COUNTY. David W. Bonem, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: Clark's sentence affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his death sentence and conviction for the murder of a nine year old girl pursuant to N.M. Stat. Ann. § 31-20A-4(A) from the District Court of Grant County (New Mexico).


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his death sentence and conviction for the murder of a nine year old girl pursuant to N.M. Stat. Ann. § 31-20A-4(A). Many issues were raised on appeal, including an allegation that the trial court erred in striking potential jurors based on opposition to the death penalty, that the trial court erred in restricting presentation of mitigating evidence and in admitting evidence of the circumstances of the crime including victim impact testimony, and that his sentence was disproportionate. The court rejected defendant's contentions and affirmed. Absent a manifest abuse of discretion, which was not present, the court refused to disturb the trial court's decision to exclude jurors based on their opposition to the death penalty. Also, the trial court's jury instructions did not unduly limit the jury's review of mitigating evidence. The trial court properly excluded evidence directly related to proportionality when that issue was to be left to the court on appeal. The trial court's admission of victim impact evidence and the crime's circumstances were consistent with the Capital Felony Sentencing Act, and defendant's sentence was neither excessive nor disproportionate.


OUTCOME: Defendant's death sentence upon a conviction of murder was affirmed. The trial court did not err in excluding jurors based on their opposition to the death penalty, nor did its jury instructions unduly limit review of mitigating evidence. In addition, evidence directed related to proportionality was properly excluded, and the admission of victim impact evidence and the crime's circumstances were consistent with the Capital Felony Sentencing Act.

 

5 of 795 DOCUMENTS


N.M. Right to Choose/NARAL v. Johnson


Docket No. 23,239


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


127 N.M. 654; 1999-NMSC-028; 986 P.2d 450; 1999 N.M. LEXIS 212; 38 N.M. St. B. Bull. 30



June 23, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected June 25, 1999. Released for Publication July 19, 1999. As Corrected December 1, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: CERTIFICATION FROM THE NEW MEXICO COURT OF APPEALS. Steve Herrera, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs cross-appealed from the New Mexico Court of Appeals, which denied their request for attorney fees, in its action for injunctive relief against defendant, the Secretary of the Human Services Department. Plaintiffs sought to enjoin defendant from enforcing new rules for its medical assistance program. Plaintiffs also moved for an award of costs on appeal.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs sought injunctive relief against defendant, the Secretary of the Human Services Department. Plaintiffs alleged that the defendant adopted new rules for its medical assistance program that violated their constitutional rights. The court enjoined defendant from enforcing its new rules and awarded plaintiffs costs, but denied attorney fees. Defendant, joined by intervenors, appealed the ruling. Plaintiffs cross-appealed the district court's decision denying them attorney fees. Plaintiffs also moved for an award of costs on appeal. The court found that plaintiffs were not entitled to an award of attorney fees or costs on appeal and affirmed the decision that plaintiffs' constitutional rights were violated. The court found that the district court did not err in declining to award attorney fees and rejected plaintiffs' argument that the private attorney general doctrine applied. Plaintiffs did not justify a departure from established state precedent of applying the American Rule to attorney fee awards. The court found that neither party was entitled to recover costs because the court ruled in favor of each party on one issue in the cross-appeal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision to deny plaintiffs' request for attorney fees, finding that a departure from the American Rule was not justified. The court also found that neither party was entitled to recover costs.

 

6 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Sandel v. N.M. PUC


Docket No. 25,523


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


127 N.M. 272; 1999-NMSC-019; 980 P.2d 55; 1999 N.M. LEXIS 126; 38 N.M. St. B. Bull. 18



March 15, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication April 27, 1999. As Corrected September 9, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE NEW MEXICO PUBLIC UTILITY COMMISSION.



DISPOSITION: Writ of mandamus vacating the REI order issued.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners sought a writ of mandamus vacating an order issued by respondent commission that in part granted intervenor corporation's request to charge retail consumers a market-based rate for electricity and granted a certificate of public convenience and necessity that allowed intervenor corporation to own and operate transmission and distribution facilities in certain areas.


OVERVIEW: Respondent commission approved a request by intervenor corporation to charge retail consumers a market-based rate for electricity and granted a certificate of public convenience and necessity, allowing intervenor corporation to own and operate transmission and distribution facilities. As a result, petitioner individuals, including members of the state legislature, union representatives, and utility shareholders, sought a writ of mandamus vacating respondent commission's order. Petitioners argued that the order violated the requirement of separation of powers contained in N.M. Const. art. III, § 1 because it brought about the deregulation of the retail electric power industry in the state without authorization from the state legislature. The court issued the writ of mandamus vacating respondent commission's order because the end result of the order was to deregulate the retail side of the electric power industry in the state in a manner inconsistent with the regulatory scheme that respondent commission was charged with administering, and, thus, respondent commission unlawfully intruded on the province of the state legislature.


OUTCOME: The court issued a writ of mandamus vacating respondent commission's order because respondent commission violated the state constitution by undertaking to deregulate the electric power industry in the state in a manner beyond the scope of the authority granted to defendant commission by the state legislature.

 

7 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State v. House


Docket No. 24,861


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


127 N.M. 151; 1999-NMSC-014; 978 P.2d 967; 1999 N.M. LEXIS 61; 38 N.M. St. B. Bull. 13



February 24, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: ORIGINAL PROCEEDING ON CERTIORARI.



DISPOSITION: Reversed the Court of Appeals and affirmed the trial court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed a judgment of the Court of Appeals (New Mexico), reversing defendant's conviction for vehicular homicide and various other charges based on a finding that the trial court abused its discretion in changing the venue of the trial.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of vehicular homicide and other charges. Defendant's conviction was reversed after an appellate court concluded that the trial court abused its discretion in changing the trial's venue. The state appealed, arguing that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in concluding that a fair trial could not be guaranteed in the county where the crime was committed and that the county where the trial was held was more likely to be free from exception. The court ruled that when moving for a venue change over defendant's objection from the district in which the crime allegedly occurred, the prosecution must prove with clear and convincing evidence that a fair trial in that district was a practical impossibility. Further, the court held that the trial court must apply a reasonable-probability standard of proof when balancing conflicting claims regarding the likelihood of a fair trial in a venue. The court reversed the judgment, concluding that it was reasonably probable that the publicity surrounding the case tended to solidify the opinions of so many residents of the county where the crime took place that the trial's fairness in that community was questionable.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversing defendant's conviction was reversed, and the judgment convicting defendant was affirmed, where substantial evidence supported the reasonable probability that a fair trial could not be obtained in the county where the crime took place, the trial court did not abuse its discretion by ordering a venue transfer to the county where the trial was held, and defendant failed to present evidence that the trial jury was biased.

 

8 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Allsup's Convenience Stores, Inc. v. N. River Ins. Co.


Docket No. 22,621


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


127 N.M. 1; 1999-NMSC-006; 976 P.2d 1; 1998 N.M. LEXIS 465; 38 N.M. St. B. Bull. 6



December 3, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Second Correction July 9, 1999. As Corrected February 20, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF BERNALILLO COUNTY. Susan M. Conway, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.



CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant insureds challenged the decision of the District Court of Bernalillo County (New Mexico), which ordered remittitur of the jury's verdict against appellee insurer in appellants' action for inadequate claims handling.


OVERVIEW: Appellant insureds and appellee insurer entered into a series of agreements for retrospective premium insurance. Judgment was entered on the jury verdict of $ 540,000 in compensatory damages for appellants and against appellee for inadequate claims handling, and for $ 4,792 in compensatory damages for the wrongful drawdown of the letter of credit. The jury also assessed punitive damages against appellee. By directed verdict, the trial court awarded appellee $ 1,645,708 on its counterclaim for unpaid premiums by appellant. The trial court granted appellee's motion for remittitur. On appeal, the court held that, when a trial court granted a motion for remittitur or new trial in the alternative, a party could accept the remittitur under protest and appeal directly, with certain requirements set by the trial judge. The covenant of good faith and fair dealing could be enforced for a failure to disclose. The jury award of punitive damages in the amount of $ 4,500,000 was not unconstitutional or otherwise excessive. The court reversed the order of remittitur, reinstated the jury verdict, and affirmed on all other issues.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order of remittitur and reinstated the jury verdict in favor of appellant insureds in their action for inadequate claims handling against appellee insurer. The court affirmed all other issues.

N.M. Right to Choose/Naral, Abortion & Reprod. Health Servs., Planned Parenthood of the Rio Grande v. Johnson


Docket No. 23,239


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


126 N.M. 788; 1999-NMSC-005; 975 P.2d 841; 1998 N.M. LEXIS 466; 38 N.M. St. B. Bull. 6



November 25, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected February 20, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: CERTIFICATION FROM THE NEW MEXICO COURT OF APPEALS. Steve Herrera, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: Deferred ruling on issue of attorney fees and the award of costs on appeal until further order of this Court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, human services department secretary and taxpayers, sought review of the district court's permanent injunction against enforcement of Rule 766, which prohibited the use of state funds for most abortions. Appellees, physicians and nonprofit organizations, alleged the rule violated N.M. Const. art. II, § 18. The New Mexico Court of Appeals certified the issue to the court.


OVERVIEW: Appellees, physicians and nonprofit organizations, filed an action against appellant, human services department secretary, challenging the constitutionality of Rule 766, which prohibited the use of state funds for abortions for Medicaid-eligible women except when necessary to save the life of the mother, to end an ectopic pregnancy, or when the pregnancy resulted from rape or incest. The district court allowed appellant taxpayers to intervene as of right. The district court permanently enjoined enforcement of the rule. Appellants challenged the order, and the intermediate appellate court certified the issue to the court. The court concluded that the rule violated N.M. Const., art. II, § 18, because it did not apply the same standard of medical necessity to men and women and there was no compelling justification for such disparate treatment. The court determined that appellees had standing and that appellant taxpayers' intervention was premised on a misapprehension of the law. The court reversed the intervention but affirmed the remainder of the district court's orders.


OUTCOME: On certification from the appellate court, the court affirmed the district court's orders granting appellees' motion for summary judgment, permanently enjoining appellant human services department secretary from enforcing its revision of the rule prohibiting the use of state funds for most abortions, and awarding costs to appellees. The court reversed the district court's orders granting appellant taxpayers' motion to intervene.

 

10 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Haragan v. Harris


Docket No. 24,365


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


126 N.M. 310; 1998-NMSC-043; 968 P.2d 1173; 1998 N.M. LEXIS 407; 37 N.M. St. B. Bull. 52



October 21, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected January 7, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: CERTIFICATION FROM THE NEW MEXICO COURT OF APPEALS. Robert M. Doughty, II, District Judge, Twelfth Judicial District.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded with instructions to dismiss complaint with prejudice.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The district court (New Mexico) entered a judgment in petitioner elected officials' favor in their declaratory judgment action against respondent state, in which the elected officials sought a writ of mandamus that ordered the state to approve the county budgets that granted salary increases to the elected officials. The state appealed.


OVERVIEW: The district court entered a judgment in the elected officials' favor in their declaratory judgment action that sought to compel the state to approve the county budgets that granted salary increases to the elected officials. The court reversed that judgment on appeal and remanded the case with instructions to dismiss the complaint with prejudice. The court held that the midterm increases violated N.M. Const. art. IV, § 27, which precluded altering public officers' compensation during their terms in office unless provided for in the state constitution, and that the elected officers were public officials. The court also opined that the language in N.M. Const. art. X, § 1 that granted the legislature the power to set county officers' salaries did not provide for an exception to N.M. Const. art. IV, § 27. The court further determined that it was unlikely that the framers intended N.M. Const. art. X, § 1 to allow the legislature to cause precisely the kind of variations in compensation for county officers that abolishing the fee-based system of compensation was designed to eliminate.


OUTCOME: The court reversed a judgment in the elected officials' favor in their declaratory judgment action that sought a writ of mandamus to compel the state to approve the county budgets that granted salary increases to the elected officials and remanded the case with instructions to dismiss the complaint with prejudice.

 

11 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Trujillo v. City of Albuquerque


Docket No. 18,296 consolidated with: Docket No. 19,118


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


125 N.M. 721; 1998-NMSC-031; 965 P.2d 305; 1998 N.M. LEXIS 338



September 8, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Amended December 29, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF BERNALILLO COUNTY. Frank H. Allen, Jr., District Judge.



DISPOSITION: Court upholds the finding of the district court, invalidating the TCA cap and permitting recovery of the Plaintiffs' full damages, but disallowing Plaintiffs' claim for post-judgment interest.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In two consolidated cases, plaintiff injured persons brought separate tort claims against defendant city pursuant to the New Mexico Tort Claims Act (TCA), N.M. Stat. Ann. § 41-4-1 to 4-27 (1996). The District Court of Bernalillo County (New Mexico) invalidated the TCA cap and permitted recovery of the injured persons' full damages. The district court disallowed the injured persons' claim for post-judgment interest. All parties appealed.


OVERVIEW: In both cases, the injured persons were awarded amounts exceeding the caps under the TCA. The injured persons challenged the constitutionality of the damages limitation in N.M. Stat. Ann. § 41-4-19(A), arguing that the cap violated their rights of equal protection under the New Mexico and United States Constitutions. The court held that the court previously should not have adopted intermediate scrutiny for the analysis of the claims. Instead, the court held that the rational basis analysis should have been applied, and such analysis was to have applied to such cases in the future. However, the law-of-the-case doctrine and principles of equity required application of intermediate scrutiny to the case because that standard was posited in the court's previous orders in the case. The court concluded that the city failed to meet its burden of proving a substantial relationship between the cap and an important government interest. The TCA cap did not implicate the right of access to the courts. Rational basis scrutiny was the appropriate equal protection analysis to be employed. Equal protection rights were not affected so substantially that intermediate scrutiny was warranted.


OUTCOME: The court upheld the finding of the district court, invalidating the TCA cap and permitting recovery of the injured persons' full damages, but disallowing their claim for post-judgment interest.

 

12 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State v. Arellano


Docket No. 24,354


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


125 N.M. 709; 1998-NMSC-026; 965 P.2d 293; 1998 N.M. LEXIS 304



August 14, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Amended December 29, 1998.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Pursuant to N.M. R. App. P. 12-102, the state appealed an order of the New Mexico Court of Appeals which reversed the trial court's denial of defendant's motion for a new trial based upon the trial court's failure to administer the jury's oath found in N.M. Unif. Jury Instructions-Crim. 14-123 to the jury before it delivered its verdict. The court granted certiorari.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with vehicular homicide. A jury was impaneled, then dismissed without being sworn. The trial court conducted the trial a few weeks later and did not administer the jury's oath at that time; however, the trial court gave a pretrial instruction regarding the jury's duty to decide the case on all the evidence and to follow the law as fair and impartial jurors. After defendant was convicted and sentenced, defendant's counsel advised the trial court that the jury had never been sworn and filed a motion for a new trial. The trial court denied the motion after administering the oath and then questioning the jurors on their verdict. Defendant's counsel admitted that he was aware, during the trial, that the jury had not been sworn, stating that his failure to advise the trial court was a tactical move. The appellate court reversed, holding that the failure to swear in the jury was reversible error and could not have been waived by defendant. The court reversed, holding that defendant knowingly waived the jury oath and that the jury had complied with the oath that would have been given. Because defendant perpetuated the error, the conviction was not a nullity.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the appellate court's order reversing the trial court's denial of defendant's motion for a new trial and affirmed the trial court.

 

13 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Srader v. Verant


Docket No. 24,136 consolidated with Docket No. 24,235


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


125 N.M. 521; 1998-NMSC-025; 964 P.2d 82; 1998 N.M. LEXIS 303; 37 N.M. St. B. Bull. 39



July 20, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Motion for Rehearing Denied August 31, 1998. Released for Publication September 1, 1998. As Amended September 30, 1998. As Corrected October 5, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: CERTIFICATION FROM THE NEW MEXICO COURT OF APPEALS. Robert L. Thompson, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: All claims in this suit dismissed under Rule 1-019 with respect to all Defendants.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff gamblers sought review from the New Mexico Court of Appeals, which certified this case to the court, in which the district court granted dismissal to defendant financial entities on the grounds that the Indian gaming tribes were indispensable parties and that plaintiffs did not state a claim for which relief could be granted. Defendant government entities sought dismissal on the same grounds plus federal preemption.


OVERVIEW: After consolidating plaintiff gamblers' two cases, the court held that the Indian Gaming Regulatory Act, 18 U.S.C.S. § 1166, did not preempt state law claims because defendant government entities did not overcome a presumption favoring state police power due to the fact that during the relevant time, Indian gaming was illegal both on and off the reservation, as no valid gaming compact was in effect. The court asserted that within reservations the federal government was responsible for dealing with gaming violations and outside the reservations defendant government entities were responsible. The court held that the Indian gaming tribes were indispensable parties, but because of sovereign immunity they could not be joined, so the court reversed the trial court's failure to dismiss plaintiffs' claims against defendant government entities and affirmed the dismissal of defendant financial entities. The court concluded that because the requested relief would stop all Indian gaming funding and there were no protective provisions to insulate the tribes from an adverse judgment's effects, litigation could not continue. All claims were dismissed under N.M. R. Civ. P. Dist. Ct. 1-019.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed all of plaintiff gamblers' claims with respect to both defendant government entities and defendant financial entities, affirming the trial court's dismissal of defendant financial entities and reversing the trial court's failure to dismiss defendant government entities. The Indian gaming tribes could not be joined because of sovereign immunity, so because they were indispensable parties, the cases were dismissed.

 

14 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Regents of the Univ. of N.M. v. N.M. Fed'n of Teachers


Docket No. 24,716


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


125 N.M. 401; 1998-NMSC-020; 962 P.2d 1236; 1998 N.M. LEXIS 246; 37 N.M. St. B. Bull. 31; 159 L.R.R.M. 2535



June 23, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected August 3, 1998. Released for Publication July 13, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: CERTIFICATION FROM THE NEW MEXICO COURT OF APPEALS. Petra Jimenez Maes, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The New Mexico Court of Appeals certified an issue to the court pursuant to N.M. Stat. Ann. § 34-514(C)(2) (1972), regarding whether plaintiff state educational institution's labor policy violated the Public Employee Bargaining Act (PEBA), N.M. Stat. Ann. §§ 10-7D-1 to -26, as asserted by defendant unions.


OVERVIEW: The PEBA opened the collective bargaining process to several categories of public employees that were explicitly excluded by the educational institution's pre-existing labor relations policy. The unions filed prohibited practices complaints against the institution, alleging violations of PEBA. The court held that 1) the PEBA regulated public employees, 2) the institution would suffer no hardship nor injustice were it required to open the collective bargaining process to additional employees, 3) the grandfather clause of PEBA did not apply to the relevant portion of the institution's policy because it did not extend the right to all employees who were afforded that right under the PEBA, and 4) the collective bargaining requirements did not violate N.M. Const. art. XII, § 13, by infringing upon the autonomy of the institution's board of regents.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the district court's affirmance of the decision and order of the agency, invalidating the educational institution's policy insofar as it denied collective bargaining right to all public employees as defined in the state public employees' bargaining statute.

 

15 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Wilson v. Denver


Docket No. 23,667


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


125 N.M. 308; 1998-NMSC-016; 961 P.2d 153; 1998 N.M. LEXIS 234; 37 N.M. St. B. Bull. 35



May 29, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication June 16, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TAOS COUNTY. Jay G. Harris, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant election contestees sought interlocutory review of a judgment of the district court of Taos County (New Mexico) that entered summary judgment for appellee election contestants on their consolidated actions that contested two separate elections of several individuals to the seats of commissioner and mayordomo for an irrigation ditch association.


OVERVIEW: Appellee election contestants pursued a consolidated action contesting 1994 and 1995 elections of several individuals as officers for a local ditch association. The district court granted summary judgment in favor of appellees, and appellant election contestees sought interlocutory appeal. Because appellees failed to file a notice of election contest within the statutory mandate of N.M. Stat. Ann. § 12-2-2(G), the court remanded the 1994 election contest for dismissal. Appellees' 1995 contest was timely, so the court when on to evaluate whether appellees were entitled to relief relative that election. The court noted that the plain language of the relevant statute N.M. Stat. Ann. § 73-3-3 provided that voting in ditch elections could be conducted based proportionately on interested persons' water rights, based proportionately on ditch ownership, or based on a majority of those using the ditch for the distribution of water. The parties disputed the manner in which the ditch association had chosen historically to conduct elections. In view of this genuine issue of fact, the court reversed the grant of summary judgment of the 1995 election and remanded the matter.


OUTCOME: The district court's grant of summary judgment on appellee election contestants' ditch election contest action was reversed and the matter remanded for a grant of summary judgment and remanded for further proceedings. The district court lacks jurisdiction over the 1994 election, so only the 1995 election was remanded for a determination as to whether the subject election administered in accordance with historical practice.

 

16 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Taylor v. Johnson


Docket No. 24,547


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


125 N.M. 343; 1998-NMSC-015; 961 P.2d 768; 1998 N.M. LEXIS 235



May 29, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected, October 22, 1998.



DISPOSITION: Respondents found in indirect civil contempt.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner state legislators filed a motion to hold respondent governor and respondent Secretary of the New Mexico Human Services Department in contempt of court, alleging that the governor and secretary were continuing to implement their public assistance changes despite a writ prohibiting such practice. The court required the governor and the secretary to show cause why they should not be held in contempt.


OVERVIEW: The governor and secretary continued to implement public assistance changes despite a writ prohibiting them from doing so. The governor and the secretary argued that their actions were necessary to prevent the loss of federal funding for the state's welfare program. The court reasoned that the governor and the secretary did not have the discretion to continue their plan, which was found to have been unconstitutional as a violation of the state constitution's separation of powers clause. Moreover, it determined that they had more than adequate notice and were advised to comply with the previously entered writ. The court found that the governor and the secretary had not complied with the writ and, therefore, held them in indirect civil contempt. The court found that the most appropriate contempt sanction was an order directing the governor and secretary to cease and desist immediately from implementing their public assistance program within seven days.


OUTCOME: A judgment finding the governor and secretary in indirect civil contempt was entered, and they were directed to immediately comply with the court's previous order.

 

17 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State v. Duffy


Docket No. 22,667


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


126 N.M. 132; 1998-NMSC-014; 967 P.2d 807; 1998 N.M. LEXIS 202; 37 N.M. St. B. Bull. 25



May 20, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected February 24, 1999. Second Correction January 11, 1999. Released for Publication June 5, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF BERNALILLO COUNTY. Ross C. Sanchez, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed Duffy's convictions for felony murder and tampering with evidence, and vacated, on double-jeopardy grounds.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the District Court of Bernalillo County (New Mexico), which convicted him of first-degree felony murder, robbery with an old-age enhancement, and tampering with evidence, in violation of N.M. Stat. Ann. § 30-2-1 (1994), N.M. Stat. Ann. § 30-16-2 (1973), and N.M. Stat. Ann. § 30-22-5 (1963).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of first-degree felony murder, robbery with an old-age enhancement, and tampering with evidence, in violation of N.M. Stat. Ann. § 30-2-1 (1994), N.M. Stat. Ann. § 30-16-2 (1973), and N.M. Stat. Ann. § 30-22-5 (1963). Defendant sought review and contended that his right to be protected from double jeopardy was violated. The court held that, to determine whether multiple punishments had been imposed unconstitutionally, it was required to inquire whether the conduct underlying the offenses was unitary, and if so, it was to determined whether the legislature intended to create separately punishable offenses for the unitary conduct. The court found that, because the conduct underlying the felony-murder and the robbery charges was unitary, convictions for both was in violation of the double jeopardy clause. The court held that defendant's conviction for felony murder was correct because the killing was apart from the consideration of the underlying felony. The court affirmed the convictions for felony murder and tampering with evidence and vacated the conviction for robbery.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a part of the judgment of the trial court, which convicted defendant of first-degree felony murder and tampering with evidence. The court vacated on double jeopardy grounds a part of the judgment of the trial court, which convicted defendant of robbery with an old-age enhancement.

 

18 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State v. Mora


Docket No. 23,693


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


124 N.M. 346; 1997-NMSC-060; 950 P.2d 789; 1997 N.M. LEXIS 464; 37 N.M. St. B. Bull. 37



November 17, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected January 6, 1998.
Petition granted by Mora v. Lytle, 129 N.M. 385, 9 P.3d 68, 2000 N.M. LEXIS 278 (N.M., 2000)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF BERNALILLO COUNTY. W. John Brennan, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, vacated in part and remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The District Court of Bernalillo County (New Mexico) convicted defendant of first degree murder, criminal sexual contact in the third degree, and intentional child abuse resulting in great bodily harm or death. Defendant appealed his convictions and, alternatively, his sentencing for the convictions.


OVERVIEW: While defendant's girlfriend was in the shower, the defendant penetrated her baby's anus. He also struck the baby's head, killing her. The defendant asserted that his girlfriend killed the baby. The court held, inter alia, that 1) due to the baby's unstable health and her head injuries, a rational jury could have found that the defendant committed the crime of criminal sexual conduct of a minor under circumstances dangerous to human life, thus supporting his felony murder conviction, 2) a rational jury could infer that the baby's head injuries were intentionally inflicted where a physician testified that the fracture was caused either by striking the skull against a hard object or by shaking the child and hitting her skull against a hard object, 3) there was sufficient evidence to prove that the murder was committed during the commission of the criminal sexual contact, 4) the evidence supported the remaining convictions, 5) the trial court did not abuse its discretion in admitting autopsy photographs because they were more probative than prejudicial, and 6) the felony murder and criminal sexual contact were sufficiently distinct to warrant convictions for both.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the convictions for felony murder and criminal sexual contact in the third degree, remanded the case with directions that the conviction for intentional child abuse resulting in death be vacated, and that the judgment and sentence be amended to reflect sentences for both criminal sexual contact of a minor and felony murder.

 

19 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State v. Cooper


Docket No. 22,504


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


124 N.M. 277; 1997-NMSC-058; 949 P.2d 660; 1997 N.M. LEXIS 452; 36 N.M. St. B. Bull. 50



November 3, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication November 25, 1997.
Writ of habeas corpus denied Cooper v. LeMaster, 211 F.3d 1277, 2000 U.S. App. LEXIS 15133 (10th Cir. N.M., 2000)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Cooper v. Janecka, 2009 N.M. Unpub. LEXIS 5 (2009)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF BERNALILLO COUNTY. Frank H. Allen, Jr., District Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and remanded in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment from the District Court of Bernanillo County (New Mexico) that convicted him of felony murder, second-degree murder, armed robbery, and sentenced defendant to life plus 15 years in prison under U.S. Const. Amend. V.


OVERVIEW: After defendant stabbed victim to death, defendant was convicted of felony murder, second-degree murder, armed robbery, two counts of aggravated battery, and numerous other crimes. When the court sentenced defendant to life in prison for felony murder and merged a sentence of nine years for second-degree murder, resulting in a cumulative sentence of life plus 15 years in prison, defendant appealed under U.S. Const. Amend. V. The court vacated defendant's convictions for second-degree murder and armed robbery, and one of his convictions for aggravated battery and remanded for resentencing. Defendant's multiple convictions violated defendant's right to be protected from double jeopardy. The court affirmed his felony murder conviction. Defendant's remarks to the hostage negotiators in a suicide attempt were voluntary. The court affirmed one of his convictions for aggravated battery. A struggle was an intervening event between the initial battery and the acts that caused victim's death. The conduct that gave rise to defendant's convictions for aggravated battery and felony murder could not be characterized as unitary.


OUTCOME: The court remanded for resentencing because convictions for second-degree murder, armed robbery, and aggravated battery were unconstitutional because multiple convictions violated defendant's double jeopardy right. The court affirmed one conviction for aggravated battery because the conduct that led to convictions for aggravated battery and felony murder was not unitary.

 

20 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Reed v. State ex rel. Ortiz


Docket No. 22,749


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


124 N.M. 129; 1997-NMSC-055; 947 P.2d 86; 1997 N.M. LEXIS 409; 36 N.M. St. B. Bull. 47



September 9, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Motion for Rehearing Denied October 28, 1997. Released for Publication October 28, 1997. As Corrected December 3, 1997. Second Correction January 20, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TAOS COUNTY. Peggy J. Nelson, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent challenged a decision of the District Court of Taos County (New Mexico), which granted petitioner a writ of habeas corpus. Petitioner had challenged his extradition from New Mexico to Ohio on the grounds that the extradition documents were not in order and he was not a fugitive from justice.


OVERVIEW: While petitioner was in an Ohio prison, he incurred the animosity of prison officials by becoming a jailhouse lawyer and an advocate for the rights of Native American inmates. After he was placed on parole, he was warned by his parole officer to stop speaking out against the prison system and the parole board or his parole would be revoked. Petitioner was also told by inmates that if he was returned to prison, the prison personnel would cause him death or great bodily harm. After a minor incident, petitioner was advised by his parole officer that he would have to wait until after he was back in prison before he could present evidence of his innocence to the parole board. He then fled the State of Ohio and challenged his extradition from New Mexico. The trial court granted him a writ of habeas corpus and the court affirmed. It found that petitioner was not a fugitive from justice because the conduct of the State of Ohio forced him to flee the State under duress, as the persuasive and uncontroverted evidence reflected that petitioner left Ohio because he risked death or great bodily harm at the hands of prison officials if he had reported to be arrested by his parole officer.


OUTCOME: The court concluded that the extradition documents were in order, but found that the conduct of the State of Ohio forced petitioner to flee the State under duress, in fear of death or great bodily harm at the hands of government officials, and affirmed the trial court's decision, which granted petitioner a writ of habeas corpus.

 

21 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State v. Johnson


Docket No. 23,262


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


123 N.M. 640; 1997-NMSC-036; 944 P.2d 869; 1997 N.M. LEXIS 303; 36 N.M. St. B. Bull. 36



August 1, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication August 19, 1997. As Corrected September 4, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: ORIGINAL PROCEEDING ON CERTIORARI. H. Richard Blackhurst, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury convicted defendant of aggravated assault, criminal penetration, and false imprisonment, after the trial court precluded evidence of the victims' prior sexual conduct, pursuant to N.M. Stat. Ann. § 30-9-16, and N.M. R. Evid. 11-413. The New Mexico Court of Appeals reversed the verdict, holding the preclusion deprived the defendant of his U.S. Const. amend. VI right to confrontation, and granted him a new trial. The state appealed.


OVERVIEW: The court held that the rape shield law, codified as N.M. Stat. Ann. § 30-9-16, and the corresponding rule prevented the admission of the prior sexual conduct by the victims, because the defendant failed to show (a) that the evidence was material and relevant, and (b) that its probative value equaled or outweighed its inflammatory or prejudicial nature. The court initially agreed with the rationale of the appeals court that a defendant's right to confrontation required admission of prior sexual conduct of an alleged rape victim, thereby overruling the rape shield law, if the defendant's case were built on a premise whereby evidence of prior sexual conduct was probative of the defense. However, a bare claim that the victim was a prostitute did not satisfy the test for admission. The defendant never expressed his intention to use the prior sexual conduct evidence to expose the victims' motives to lie or as a basis for a theory of relevance other than propensity, which was insufficient to overcome the rape shield law. On that reasoning, the court held that the appeals court erred in reversing the trial court's verdict and its sentencing of the defendant for sexual assault.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the appeals court's order, reversing the defendant's conviction and sentence for aggravated sexual assault, and remanded the matter to the appeals court for determination of other issues.

 

22 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State v. Setser


Docket No. 22,983


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


122 N.M. 794; 1997-NMSC-004; 932 P.2d 484; 1996 N.M. LEXIS 472; 36 N.M. St. B. Bull. 13



December 23, 1996, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication January 8, 1997. As Corrected January 31, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF SANDOVAL COUNTY. Louis P. McDonald, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the District Court of Sandoval County (New Mexico), which convicted defendant on two counts of first degree murder, conspiracy to commit murder, aggravated robbery, unlawful taking of a motor vehicle, and tampering with evidence.


OVERVIEW: While investigating a double murder, the police were informed that defendant, a 16-year-old female with a history of mental and emotional problems, wished to confess something to them. Defendant was advised of her Miranda rights, stated that she understood them, waived her right to remain silent, and adamantly refused to have either an attorney or her mother present for her statement. In a motion to suppress, defendant claimed that her confession was inadmissible because, given her age and mental condition, she could not have voluntarily waived her Miranda rights. The court denied defendant's motion to suppress, and the jury convicted defendant on two counts of first degree murder, conspiracy to commit murder, aggravated robbery, unlawful taking of a motor vehicle, and tampering with evidence. On appeal, the court affirmed and held that defendant was not entitled to a statutory presumption of involuntary waiver because she was older than 14 years old. Further, under the totality-of-circumstances test, the state proved that defendant's confession was given voluntarily after a valid waiver of her Miranda rights.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction on two counts of first degree murder, conspiracy to commit murder, aggravated robbery, unlawful taking of a motor vehicle, and tampering with evidence because defendant was not statutorily entitled to a presumption that her confession was involuntary, and under a totality of the circumstances, it was shown that defendant waived her Miranda rights and voluntarily confessed to the crimes.

 

23 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State v. Brown


Docket No. 21,980


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


122 N.M. 724; 1996-NMSC-073; 931 P.2d 69; 1996 N.M. LEXIS 458; 36 N.M. St. B. Bull. 3



December 5, 1996, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication December 26, 1996. As Corrected January 31, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF CHAVES COUNTY. Alvin F. Jones, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Chaves County District Court (New Mexico), which convicted him of first-degree depraved mind murder under N.M. Stat. Ann. § 30-2-1(A)(3) (1994), and sentenced him to life imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: The defendant argued that the trial court erred in refusing to instruct the jury that his intoxication could be considered in determining the mental state required for conviction of depraved mind murder. The court held that a fact finder may consider evidence of extreme intoxication when determining whether defendant possessed the requisite mental state of subjective knowledge for depraved mind murder. The evidence of intoxication could be considered to reduce first degree depraved mind murder to second-degree murder, but could not be used to reduce it to lesser offenses or to completely excuse defendant from the consequences of his unlawful act. The court found that there was sufficient evidence that defendant was intoxicated to raise the question of whether he actually possessed the subjective knowledge or the requisite awareness that his acts were greatly dangerous to the lives of others. The trial court committed reversible error in refusing to give defendant's instruction on intoxication because the evidence at trial supported the giving of the instruction on his theory of the case.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the judgment of the trial court.

 

24 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Conoco, Inc. v. Taxation & Revenue Dep't


Docket Nos. 22,995, 23,045


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


122 N.M. 736; 1997-NMSC-005; 931 P.2d 730; 1996 N.M. LEXIS 476; 36 N.M. St. B. Bull. 6



November 26, 1996, Filed



DISPOSITION:  Reversed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner taxpayers sought review of a decision of the Court of Appeals (New Mexico), which held that respondent state tax department's corporate income tax scheme did not treat dividends received from foreign subsidiaries less favorably than those received from domestic subsidiaries and therefore was not violative of the Foreign Commerce Clause of the U.S. Const. art. I, § 8, cl. 3.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers sought a refund of corporate income taxes paid to the state tax department (department) on dividends received from the taxpayer's foreign subsidiaries. The department's hearing officer denied the refunds and upheld an assessment for underpaid taxes. The court of appeals upheld the constitutionality of New Mexico's formulaic corporate tax scheme. The department argued that the application of the formula remedied the differential treatment of domestic and foreign commerce under the New Mexico tax scheme by thus reducing the taxable income base. On appeal, the court reversed the judgment because the department's tax scheme violated the Foreign Commerce Clause of the U. S. Constitution. The court found that dividends received by the taxpayers, parent corporations, from their foreign subsidiaries were taxed; however, dividends received from domestic subsidiaries were excluded entirely from the parent's tax base. The court noted that none of the taxpayer's foreign subsidiaries conducted business in New Mexico and both taxpayers filed state corporate income tax returns as separate corporate entities.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the court of appeals decision and found that the department's corporate income tax scheme on the dividends received by the taxpayers from foreign subsidiaries was unconstitutional. The court allowed the taxpayers' refunds and abated the department's assessments.

 

25 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Madrid v. St. Joseph Hosp.


Docket No. 23,226


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


122 N.M. 524; 1996-NMSC-064; 928 P.2d 250; 1996 N.M. LEXIS 431; 35 N.M. St. B. Bull. 49



July 22, 1996, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Motions for Rehearing Denied December 2, 1996. Released for Publication December 2, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: CERTIFICATION FROM THE NEW MEXICO COURT OF APPEALS. Gregory D. Griego, Workers' Compensation Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a consolidated appeal, by certification from the New Mexico Court of Appeals, pursuant to N.M. Stat. Ann. § 34-5-14(B)(3) and (4) (1990), appellant workers challenged the constitutionality of the New Mexico Workers' Compensation Act of 1978, N.M. Stat. Ann. §§ 52-1-1 to -70 (1991) (Act), under which each was denied the level of permanent partial disability benefits (PPD) sought.


OVERVIEW: The workers contended that there was insufficient evidence to support the workers' compensation judge's finding regarding the date on which they reached maximum medical improvement (MMI), and the value assigned to them for residual physical capacity. One worker was employed as a staff nurse by appellee hospital when she sustained an injury to her back. She received an impairment rating of zero percent from her medical care provider, which rendered her ineligible for further workers' compensation benefits. The second worker suffered from pain in her arm, shoulder, and back, which impaired her capacity to work. Her treating physician established that she had reached MMI with an impairment rating of five percent. The workers contested the mandatory use of the American Medical Association Guides to the Evaluation of Permanent Impairment (AMA Guide), alleging that the AMA Guide was not developed to determine the impact of an individual's impairment on his capacity to work. The court held that the mandatory application of the AMA Guide did not violate equal protection and that the workers' compensation judge's findings were supported by substantial evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the worker's compensation judges' determination of the proper level of benefits available to both workers, concluding that all challenged portions of the New Mexico Workers' Compensation Act were constitutional and the judge's determinations were supported by substantial evidence.

 

26 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Cummings v. X-Ray Assocs. of N.M., P.C.


Docket No. 22,246


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


121 N.M. 821; 1996-NMSC-035; 918 P.2d 1321; 1996 N.M. LEXIS 210; 35 N.M. St. B. Bull. 27



May 31, 1996, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Motion for Rehearing Denied June 20, 1996. Released for Publication June 20, 1996. As Corrected July 9, 1996. Second Correction August 29, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: CERTIFICATION FROM THE NEW MEXICO COURT OF APPEALS. Susan Conway, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff patient filed a malpractice claim against defendant radiologists for failing to properly diagnose a cancerous mass in her lung. A state district court of New Mexico dismissed her complaint as barred by § 41-5-13, the three-year statute of limitations of the Medical Malpractice Act, N.M. Stat. Ann. §§ 41-5-1 to -29 (1978). The New Mexico Court of Appeals certified the patient's appeal.


OVERVIEW: The patient asserted that her cause of action did not accrue until she learned that the cancer had metastasized and that § 41-5-13 barred her action before it had accrued. She alleged that it violated equal protection and her due process right of access to the courts as found in U.S. Const. amends. V and XIV, § 1 and N.M. Const. art. II, § 18. On appeal, the court affirmed and held that the patient's claim was barred by § 41-5-13. The section violated neither the Equal Protection nor the Due Process Clauses. Under the rational-basis test, it was reasonably drafted to further a legitimate government interest. Also, the three-year time limit established a reasonable termination point for medical malpractice claims. The section operated as a statute of repose and was reasonably related to important governmental interests. The plain language of the section demonstrated that it was an occurrence rule, and the cause of action ran from the date of the act of malpractice. Thus, the patient's cause of action did not accrue when the metastasis was discovered. Moreover, she did not exercise diligence when she first learned that she had been misinformed about the mass in her lung.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of the patient's medical malpractice claim as barred by the statute of limitations.

 

27 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State v. Rotherham


Docket No. 22,059, Docket No. 22,462, Docket No. 22,497, Docket No. 22,608, Docket No. 22,650


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


122 N.M. 246; 1996-NMSC-048; 923 P.2d 1131; 1996 N.M. LEXIS 267; 35 N.M. St. B. Bull. 34



May 31, 1996, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected September 9, 1996. Second Correction November 26, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF BERNALILLO COUNTY. W. C. "Woody" Smith, District Judge (Docket No. 22,059). APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF BERNALILLO COUNTY. James F. Blackmer, District Judge (Docket No. 22,462). APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF CHAVES COUNTY. W. J. Schnedar, District Judge (Docket No. 22,497). CERTIFICATION FROM THE NEW MEXICO COURT OF APPEALS. Frank H. Allen, Jr., District Judge (Docket No. 22,608). CERTIFICATION FROM THE NEW MEXICO COURT OF APPEALS. Albert "Pat" Murdoch, District Judge (Docket No. 22,650).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The District Court of Bernalillo County (New Mexico) and the District Court of Chaves County (New Mexico) found defendants were incompetent to stand trial. Both defendants and the state appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendants contended that New Mexico's Mental Illness and Competency Code (NMMIC), specifically N.M. Stat. Ann. §§ 31-9-1 to -1.5 (1995), was unconstitutional. The state, appealing the dismissal of criminal commitment proceedings under N.M. Stat. Ann. § 31-9-1.5 against one defendant, contended that the NMMIC was constitutional. The court held that the NMMIC was not unconstitutional. The court also held that any alleged deficiency in the treatment rendered to incompetent criminal defendants was not due to alleged unconstitutionality of the NMMIC. Rather, without defining the particular treatment for each defendant, the NMMIC properly required treatment to be administered by qualified professionals. Thus, any claim that treatment was insufficient would have been properly directed to those responsible for its specific design and administration. The court noted that it also had considered specific arguments made on behalf of individual defendants and the court concluded that its disposition of the common constitutional arguments made it unnecessary to address any of the specific arguments unique to any particular defendant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the district court as one defendant. The court remanded the cases of two defendants for further proceedings as required under the state statute.

State v. Campos


Docket No. 21,429


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


122 N.M. 148; 1996-NMSC-043; 921 P.2d 1266; 1996 N.M. LEXIS 247; 35 N.M. St. B. Bull. 32



May 30, 1996, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Motion for Rehearing Denied July 24, 1996. Released for Publication July 25, 1996. As Corrected August 22, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF CHAVEZ COUNTY. William J. Schnedar, District Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his convictions in the District Court of Chavez County (New Mexico) for first-degree criminal sexual penetration (CSP) and first-degree felony murder.


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for first-degree felony murder, N.M. Stat. Ann. § 30-2-1(A)(2) and reversed and remanded. The conviction and sentencing for both felony murder and the underlying felony violated defendant's constitutional protections against double jeopardy. The conduct underlying the CSP and the murder was unitary, and the legislature did not intend to punish defendant twice for the same killing. As the state conceded, the case needed to be remanded for resentencing with instructions to vacate defendant's CSP conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for first-degree felony murder, reversed his conviction for first-degree criminal sexual penetration, and remanded for resentencing in conformity with its opinion.

 

29 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Twohig v. Blackmer


No. 22,704


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


121 N.M. 746; 1996-NMSC-023; 918 P.2d 332; 1996 N.M. LEXIS 174; 35 N.M. St. B. Bull. 23



May 20, 1996, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication May 20, 1996. As Corrected June 4, 1996.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner attorney sought a writ of superintending control to vacate a gag order imposed by the trial court in his client's third trial on the grounds that the gag order impermissibly restricted his rights of free speech in violation of N.M. Const. art. III, § 17, and N.M. R. Prof. Conduct 16-306.


OVERVIEW: The trial court issued an order prohibiting all trial participants from communicating with the media about the third trial of the attorney's client. The gag order prohibited counsel for both parties from making any extrajudicial oral or written statement, comment, opinion, press release, letter or other communication to or through any media or public fora, on any substantive matters or substantive issues of the case and directed counsel to refrain from releasing motions and pleadings to the press without the court's prior approval. The court held that: (1) the imposition of a gag order was not warranted because the trial court had not laid out the factual foundation for finding a substantial likelihood of prejudice or clear and present danger to a fair and impartial jury; (2) the order did not contain any analysis of the facts supporting the trial court's conclusion that the gag order was necessary; and (3) the order did not indicate the trial court considered alternatives less restrictive of free speech rights than an outright ban on all communication with the media.


OUTCOME: The court granted the attorney's petition for a writ of superintending control and issued a writ vacating the trial court's gag order.

In re Eastburn


Docket No. 23,018


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


121 N.M. 531; 1996-NMSC-011; 914 P.2d 1028; 1996 N.M. LEXIS 119



April 10, 1996, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication April 10, 1996.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The court disciplined a lower court judge for direct contempt, imposing sanctions that included suspension and probation, and prepared a formal censure of the judge.


OVERVIEW: The judge, who disagreed with the peremptory disqualification statute, N.M. Stat. Ann. § 383-9 (1978), refused to recognize litigants' disqualification requests. He also made a practice of recusing himself from cases reassigned to him following the peremptory challenge of any other judge in the district. A litigant petitioned for a writ of superintending control or, in the alternative, for a writ of mandamus requiring the judge to exercise his constitutionally and statutorily mandated judicial function to hear a reassigned case. The court issued a writ of mandamus and, upon the judge's disobedience, initiated contempt proceedings by a show cause order. The court sanctioned the judge after he admitted that he had intentionally disobeyed the mandamus order. The court observed that the judge's behavior, which included intemperate language, had seriously damaged public esteem for the judiciary in general, in violation of N.M. Code Jud'l Conduct 21-200(A).


OUTCOME: The court censured the judge by means of its opinion.

 

31 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Denish v. Johnson


No. 23,182


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


121 N.M. 280; 1996-NMSC-005; 910 P.2d 914; 1996 N.M. LEXIS 28; 35 N.M. St. B. Bull. 10



January 29, 1996, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication February 1, 1996. As Corrected March 4, 1996. Second Correction May 8, 1996.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff regents filed an emergency verified petition for writ of mandamus and request for immediate stay to prevent defendant governor from removing them from their positions as regents of New Mexico Institute of Mining and Technology and appointing their replacements. The court granted the stay and issued an alternative writ of mandamus that expired.


OVERVIEW: A group of five regents oversaw the college. These regents were chosen by the governor and confirmed by the state senate for a constitutionally mandated term of six years. Two regents were awarded five-year terms. Subsequently, prior to the end of the term, the governor sought to replace the two regents. The regents filed an emergency verified petition for writ of mandamus and request for immediate stay. The court granted the stay and issued an alternative writ of mandamus that expired. The court then denied as unnecessary the request of the regents for a peremptory writ of mandamus. The court directed that the regents would remain under the holdover provision of N.M. Const. art. XX, § 2 until the governor, with the consent of the senate, appointed their successors at the next legislative session as required by N.M. Const. art. XII, § 13. Though the opinion may be filed after the opening of the next legislative session, the court opined that they saw no reason why the governor could not, during that session, submit the names of appointees for the consent of the senate.


OUTCOME: The court denied the request of the regents for a peremptory writ of mandamus. The court directed that the regents would remain under the holdover provision of the New Mexico Constitution until the governor, with the consent of the senate, appointed their successors.

 

32 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Pierce v. State


No. 22,264


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


121 N.M. 212; 1996-NMSC-001; 910 P.2d 288; 1995 N.M. LEXIS 406; 34 N.M. St. B. Bull. 3



December 11, 1995, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication January 4, 1996. As Corrected April 2, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF SANTA FE COUNTY. Steve Herrera, District Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant retirees sought review of the order of the District Court of Santa Fe County (New Mexico) which granted summary judgment to appellee state in a class action by pension recipients under the Public Employees, the Judicial, the Magistrate, and the Educational Retirement Acts.


OVERVIEW: Retirees appealed from a summary judgment entered in favor of state which dismissed a class action lawsuit filed on behalf of retirees who received a pension prior to January 1, 1990 under the Public Employees Retirement Act, the Judicial Retirement Act, the Magistrate Retirement Act, and the Educational Retirement Act. The court affirmed because the four statutory retirement programs did not grant retirees private contractual rights; thus, no right to the repealed tax exemptions and no impairment of contract under either the New Mexico or Federal Constitution existed. The programs created a property interest in the individual contributions which vested after acquiring the minimum number of service credits, but these vested rights did not include a repealed tax exemption. Also, the admission of an affidavit with newspaper articles was proper, but award of costs was not.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part and reversed in part the judgment of the district court.

 

33 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Schwartz v. Johnson


No. 23,187


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


120 N.M. 820; 1995-NMSC-080; 907 P.2d 1001; 1995 N.M. LEXIS 393; 34 N.M. St. B. Bull. 52



December 7, 1995, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication December 7, 1995.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, state and district attorneys, and intervenor senator sought a writ of mandamus to compel respondents, governor, Secretary of the New Mexico Department of Finance and Administration, director of Budget Division, and the State Corporation Commission, to resume monthly 1/12 allotments of monies appropriated in the General Appropriations Act of 1995 and to restore funds withheld under the governor's general-fund allotment policy.


OVERVIEW: The issue before the court was whether the governor's authority to regulate the state fiscal policy was to be measured solely by the specific statutory and constitutional prohibitions against incurring liabilities without general funds to meet those liabilities. The court granted petitioners' application for a writ of mandamus. The court found that N.M. Stat. Ann. § 6-3-6 (1978) did not specify that allotments for agencies whose needs were efficiently measured as a constant throughout the fiscal year were to be made in 1/12 increments. The court reasoned that to withstand a constitutional challenge, § 6-3-6 had to be interpreted to require that periods and amounts of allotments be designed to meet the constant needs of governmental agencies to achieve the purposes of appropriations. The court noted that the governor's fiscal policy in the instant case was not related to those needs, but was instead related to the prudent maintenance of the general-fund reserves. Thus, the court concluded that § 6-3-6 standing alone was insufficient to authorize the governor's regulation of state fiscal policy.


OUTCOME: The court granted petitioners' writ of mandamus to compel the governor to resume the monthly allotments of monies.

 

34 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Udall v. Public Emples. Ret. Bd.


No. 22,279


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


120 N.M. 786; 1995-NMSC-078; 907 P.2d 190; 1995 N.M. LEXIS 392; 34 N.M. St. B. Bull. 52



November 22, 1995, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication December 8, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: ORIGINAL PROCEEDING ON CERTIORARI. Joe Cruz Castellano, District Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, legislators participating in the legislative retirement benefit plan in question, sought review by writ of certiorari from the judgment of the Court of Appeals (New Mexico), which found the plan, created under N.M. Stat. Ann. §§ 10-11-39 to 10-11-43 (1992), unconstitutional. Respondent, the state attorney general, filed suit against the legislators and the Public Employees Retirement Board, also a petitioner, attacking the plan.


OVERVIEW: N.M. Stat. Ann. §§ 10-11-42 required that a legislator contribute $ 100 per year under the plan in order to earn service credits and to receive benefits. Participation in the plan was voluntary. Yet, N.M. Const. art. IV, § 10 proscribed payment of any other compensation to legislators beyond the permitted per diem and mileage allowance. The attorney general had sought injunctive relief, among other things, barring future payments under the plan. The court of appeals held that the legislative retirement benefits constituted compensation in violation of N.M. Const. art. IV, § 10. The court reversed the judgment of the court of appeals, and opined that said court did not consider the contingent nature of retirement benefits. The court found that the legislative retirement benefits paid out under the plan were not included within the terms "compensation, allowance or perquisite," as used in N.M. Const. art. IV, § 10, because such benefits were too remote and contingent. Under the plan, a legislator must have accumulated the requisite number of years of credited service before any benefits would vest and must have remained alive until the earliest time that the benefits would vest.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the court of appeals and held that the plan did not violate the New Mexico Constitution.
