State v. Meadors


No. 22,722


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


121 N.M. 38; 1995-NMSC-073; 908 P.2d 731; 1995 N.M. LEXIS 391; 34 N.M. St. B. Bull. 50



November 6, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication November 30, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: CERTIFICATION FROM THE NEW MEXICO COURT OF APPEALS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the trial court (New Mexico), which convicted him of aggravated battery and negligent arson, arguing that the court denied him due process by instructing the jury on aggravated battery as a lesser-included offense of attempted murder.


OVERVIEW: The primary issue on appeal was whether aggravated battery was a lesser-included offense of attempted murder. Defendant argued that the trial court denied him due process by instructing the jury on aggravated battery as a lesser-included offense of attempted murder. The court affirmed because the trial court did not err in instructing the jury on aggravated battery as a lesser-included offense of attempted murder, in restricting defense counsel's cross-examination of the victim regarding certain medical problems that allegedly arose out of the victim's drug use, or in sentencing the defendant for two offenses. The Fifth Amendment's prohibition against double jeopardy was not violated because the trial court merged the offenses of negligent use of an explosive and negligent arson.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for aggravated battery and negligent arson.

 

36 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Morningstar Water Users Ass'n v. N.M. PUC


NO. 21,985


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


120 N.M. 579; 1995-NMSC-062; 904 P.2d 28; 1995 N.M. LEXIS 323



September 21, 1995, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication October 11, 1995. As Corrected October 26, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE PUBLIC UTILITY COMMISSION.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant water association (association) sought review of the decision of appellee New Mexico Public Utility Commission (commission), which held that it had no jurisdiction in the association's action against the city to restrain the city from invading the association's water supply service territory.


OVERVIEW: The association sought an order to restrain the city from invading the association's water supply service territory and the commission held that it did not have jurisdiction. The sole question before the court was whether the commission had jurisdiction to grant the order. The court concluded that the commission had no such jurisdiction. The court held that, absent a regulatory provision stating otherwise, or absent a willingness of the utility to serve an indefinite public, any utilities not expressly brought within the scope of the Public Utility Act (PUA), N.M. Stat. Ann. §§ 62-3-1 to -6-27, 62-8-1 to -13-14 (Repl. 1993 and Supp. 1995), were excluded from the commission's jurisdiction. This conclusion was supported by the fact that the commission steadfastly insisted that it had no jurisdiction over water users' associations. Additionally, the association offered no evidence to show that, as a water users' association, it was subject to the PUA.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the commission that it had no jurisdiction over the association's action against the city seeking to restrain the city from invading the association's water supply service territory.

 

37 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State v. Contreras


NO. 21,455


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


120 N.M. 486; 1995-NMSC-056; 903 P.2d 228; 1995 N.M. LEXIS 316; 34 N.M. St. B. Bull. 40



August 16, 1995, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected October 5, 1995.



DISPOSITION: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF BERNALILLO COUNTY. W.C. "Woody" Smith, District Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the decision of the District Court of Bernalillo County (New Mexico), which convicted him of felony murder under N.M. Stat. Ann. § 30-2-1(A)(2) (1994), armed robbery under N.M. Stat. Ann. § 30-16-2 (1994), tampering with evidence under N.M. Stat. Ann. § 30-22-5 (1994), and unlawful taking of a vehicle under N.M. Stat. Ann. § 66-3-504 (1994).


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his convictions for felony murder arguing that the trial court violated the constitutional prohibition against double jeopardy by sentencing him for both the felony murder conviction and the underlying predicate felony conviction. The court held that substantial evidence supported the felony murder conviction and affirmed the conviction. The court found that defendant's conduct was unitary as the armed robbery and the murder occurred simultaneously. The court found that the deadly weapon defined the quality and nature of the armed robbery, and the objects and results of the stabbing and theft clearly united. The court found that the legislature did not intend multiple punishments. The court held that defendant could not have been convicted of felony murder unless the state proved all of the elements of armed robbery; the elements of armed robbery thus were subsumed by the elements of felony murder in the course of an armed robbery. The court reversed defendant's conviction for armed robbery. The court affirmed the convictions for unlawful taking of a vehicle and tampering with evidence.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's armed robbery conviction and affirmed the convictions for felony murder, tampering with evidence, and unlawful taking of a vehicle.

State ex rel. Clark v. Johnson

SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, two state legislators and a taxpayer, filed a verified petition for writ of mandamus or writ of prohibition and declaratory judgment alleging that respondent, a state governor, entered into revenue sharing agreements on gaming with various Indian tribes, contrary to the Indian Gaming Regulatory Act, 25 U.S.C.S. §§ 2701-2721.

It held that it was necessary to join the Indian tribes as parties because the mandamus was directed to the governor.


OUTCOME: The court issued the peremptory writ and stay. It stayed all actions to enforce, implement, or enable any and all of the gaming compacts and revenue-sharing agreements executed by the governor, and directed the governor and all other state officials subject to his authority to proceed in conformity with the views of the court in the opinion.

 

39 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Daddow v. Carlsbad Mun. Sch. Dist.


No. 21,284


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


120 N.M. 97; 1995-NMSC-032; 898 P.2d 1235; 1995 N.M. LEXIS 193; 34 N.M. St. B. Bull. 28



May 2, 1995, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Motion for Rehearing denied June 14, 1995. Released for Publication June 14, 1995. As Corrected July 12, 1995. Second Correction September 11, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF EDDY COUNTY. Fred A. Watson, District Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff sought review of a judgment of the District Court of Eddy County (New Mexico), which dismissed her complaint under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 against defendants, school district and board of education (collectively district). The district sought review of the trial court's decision, which denied an award of damages to the district.


OVERVIEW: The employee sought review of the trial court's order which dismissed her action under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 against the district for wrongful termination on the basis that the district could not be sued under § 1983. The district appealed the trial court's decision, which denied damages to the district. The court held that the trial court improperly dismissed the employee's § 1983 action. The court found that local school boards were "persons" for the purposes of § 1983, and they were local governing bodies with political and fiscal autonomy. The court held that the action was not barred by any statutory governmental immunity in New Mexico. The court held that although the employee could sue the district, she could not prevail on the merits of the case because the district terminated her for cause and in a manner conforming with due process. The court held that the trial court correctly awarded costs to the district as the prevailing party. The court affirmed the trial court's denial of damages to the district because the trial court properly exercised its equitable powers to bar recovery on a finding of only negligent behavior by the employee.


OUTCOME: The court reversed in part, but affirmed the judgment of the trial court. The court concluded that the district was not absolutely immune from suit under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983. On the merits, the district showed that the employee received due process and was therefore entitled to recover its costs in defending the suit. The court found that the district could not recover damages based solely on the employee's negligent behavior.

Romero v. Sanchez


No. 21,752


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


119 N.M. 690; 1995-NMSC-028; 895 P.2d 212; 1995 N.M. LEXIS 176; 34 N.M. St. B. Bull. 22

SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication May 10, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF SAN MIGUEL COUNTY. Jay G. Harris, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: Therefore the trial court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant police officer sought a rehearing of an order from the court, which affirmed in part the officer's summary judgment motion previously granted in full by the District Court of San Miguel County (New Mexico).


OVERVIEW: The individual brought an action against the police officer under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 and the New Mexico Tort Claims Act, N.M. Stat. Ann. §§ 41-4-1 to -27 (1994), asserting several causes of action based upon an incident involving the individual's refusal to pay a towing company for a mobile home move. The district court granted the officer's motion for summary judgment. On review, the court affirmed summary judgment in part. The officer sought a rehearing. The court held that its original ruling was in error because: (1) fear of arrest was not sufficient to support an assault claim; (2) the officer had a reasonable belief upon the facts that it was necessary to separate the individual from the towing company employee precluding the false imprisonment and unlawful detention claims; (3) there was no intention by the employee to permanently deprive the individual of his property but rather the property was kept until the possessory lien was satisfied; and (4) the officer was entitled to qualified immunity as to the claims of breaking and entering, unlawful search, and violation of property rights because the facts did not show that the officer violated clearly established law.


OUTCOME: The court withdrew its original opinion and affirmed the judgment from the trial court granting the police officer's motion for summary judgment.

 

41 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Roth v. Bookert (In re J.J.B.)


NO. 21,864


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


119 N.M. 638; 1995-NMSC-026; 894 P.2d 994; 1995 N.M. LEXIS 133; 34 N.M. St. B. Bull. 21



March 30, 1995, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication April 18, 1995. As Corrected May 31, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: ORIGINAL PROCEEDING ON CERTIORARI. W. John Brennan, District Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner adoptive parents challenged the decision of the Court of Appeals (New Mexico), which reversed the decision of the trial court and voided the adoption, reasoning that respondent natural father was not unfit. Termination of his parental rights on grounds of the child's interests alone, absent a showing of parental unfitness, failed to satisfy constitutional due process.


OVERVIEW: Respondent natural father and his girlfriend had three children. His girlfriend placed their youngest child for adoption against respondent's wishes. The adoption took place over his objection. The trial court entered a final decree terminating respondent's parental rights and granting the adoption. The court of appeals reversed finding that the record did not support a finding that respondent was unfit, and that termination of his parental rights on grounds of the child's interests alone, absent a showing of parental unfitness, failed to satisfy constitutional due process. The court agreed in the decision to void the adoption, but remanded for the trial court to determine the best interests of the child. The trial court's judgment was influenced by an error of law because there was no express finding of fact indicating that respondent either intended to abandon the child or that he was an unfit parent. The evidence supported the conclusion that respondent did not bear responsibility for the disintegration of his relationship with his son. Any presumption of abandonment that arose under state law was rebutted.


OUTCOME: The judgment voiding an adoption was affirmed, but remanded to determine the best interests of the child. There was no express finding of fact indicating that respondent natural father either intended to abandon the child or that he was an unfit parent. Respondent did not bear responsibility for the disintegration of his relationship with his son. Any presumption of abandonment that arose under state law was rebutted.

Garcia ex rel. Garcia v. La Farge


No. 22,160


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


119 N.M. 532; 1995-NMSC-019; 893 P.2d 428; 1995 N.M. LEXIS 132; 34 N.M. St. B. Bull. 20



March 2, 1995, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Motion for Rehearing denied April 10, 1995. Released for Publication April 10, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: CERTIFICATION FROM THE NEW MEXICO COURT OF APPEALS. Steve Herrera, District Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, parents of incapacitated son, sought review of the decision of the district court (New Mexico), which granted summary judgment for defendant doctor in the parents' medical malpractice action after their child suffered a cardiac arrest. The New Mexico Court of Appeals certified the appeal to the court pursuant to N.M. Stat. Ann. § 34-5-14(C).


OVERVIEW: The parent's contended that the three-year statute of limitations in the Medical Malpractice Act, N.M. Stat. Ann. § 41-5-13 was a violation of due process and equal protection, and was prohibited special legislation. They also argued that the statute of limitations should be tolled because the doctor had fraudulently concealed their child's condition. The court reversed the decision finding that § 41-5-13 deprived the parent's of due process. The court found that the parent's could not demonstrate that § 41-5-13 drew a classification which discriminated against them in the exercise of their claimed interest in access to the courts because it did not discriminate against the parent's child based on his status as a medical malpractice plaintiff. Section 41-5-13 did not violate N.M. Const. art. IV, § 24 prohibition of enactment of a special law when a general law could be made applicable because it applied to all persons in a certain defined situation. The court held that a statute of repose that allowed an unreasonably short period of time to bring an accrued action violated the Due Process Clause of the New Mexico Constitution.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the summary judgment finding that the medical malpractice action had been brought within three years of the date on which the claim accrued.

Marrujo v. N.M. State Highway Transp. Dep't

DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff personal representative of decedent's estate appealed the judgment of a trial court (New Mexico), which granted summary judgment for defendant New Mexico State Highway Transportation Department (highway department) in his wrongful death action under the Tort Claims Act, N.M. Stat. Ann. § 41-4-15 (1978 & Repl. Pamp. 1989).


OVERVIEW: The decedent was in a car accident on a curved section of a state road. The decedent moved the car he occupied partially off the road to repair a wheel. Another car rounded the curve and struck the decedent. The highway department received two accident reports within a few days of the accident. The personal representative filed a wrongful death action under § 41-4-15, alleging that the highway department negligently maintained the road. The highway department filed a motion to dismiss. The court found that the accident reports did not serve as notice of the claim.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court, granting summary judgment for the highway department in the personal representative's wrongful death action.

Clark v. Tansy


No. 19,931


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


118 N.M. 486; 1994-NMSC-098; 882 P.2d 527; 1994 N.M. LEXIS 363; 33 N.M. St. B. Bull. 1317



September 7, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Motion for Rehearing Denied October 3, 1994. Released for Publication October 3, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: ORIGINAL PROCEEDING ON CERTIORARI. Stanley F. Frost, District Judge


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed a petition for a writ of certiorari after the district court denied his writ of habeas corpus after being sentenced to death for kidnapping and murder.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was sentenced to death for kidnapping and murder. Defendant filed a petition for a writ of habeas corpus in the district court, which was denied. The court granted defendant's petition for a writ of certiorari. The court held that the prosecutor specifically relied on defendant's future dangerousness in his argument for the death penalty and did not accurately explain to the jury the length of defendant's incarceration. The court found that the length of incarceration facing defendant before he could have been considered for parole, as an alternative to a death sentence, was information that must have been provided to a jury before it deliberated on the capital charge if defendant decided it was in his best interest to have the jury apprised of this information. The court found that to withhold this information after it was requested violated defendant's due process right to have accurate information presented to the jury to rebut the prosecution's case for death. The court held that the failure to provide the jury with such accurate information violated defendant's due process rights. The court vacated the death sentence and remanded the case.


OUTCOME: The court vacated defendant's death sentence and remanded the cause to the district court for resentencing.

46 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Bd. of Educ. v. Harrell


No. 20,856


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


118 N.M. 470; 1994-NMSC-096; 882 P.2d 511; 1994 N.M. LEXIS 360; 33 N.M. St. B. Bull. 1387; 9 I.E.R. Cas. (BNA) 1693



September 2, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication September 30, 1994. As Corrected December 16, 1994. As Corrected January 17, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF EDDY COUNTY. Patrick J. Francoeur, District Judge


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent school employee was terminated from employment with applicant school board pursuant to termination procedures in N.M. Stat. Ann. 22-10-17.1 (1993). The District Court of Eddy County (New Mexico) affirmed an arbitrator's award that terminated the employment. The school employee challenged the arbitration and review.


OVERVIEW: Respondent school employee was terminated from employment with applicant school board pursuant to termination procedures in N.M. Stat. Ann. 22-10-17.1 (1993). The trial court affirmed an arbitrator's award that terminated the employment. The court reversed and remanded the order because it determined that the overall statutory procedure, calling for compulsory arbitration of school employment disputes, was constitutional, but that the limitation on judicial review in N.M. Stat. Ann. § 22-10-17.1(M) (1993) was not. The court determined that the statutory arbitration process was compulsory rather than voluntary, and therefore the school employee had a right to procedural due process because there termination affected his property rights. The arbitration process was determined to be constitutionally fair, but the judicial review, restricted by N.M. Stat. Ann. § 22-10-17.1(M) (1993), did not comport to either procedural due process or separation of powers between branches of government. The court held that on remand the court was required to apply de novo review of questions of law and substantial-evidence review of findings of fact for the compulsory arbitration.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the order confirming the arbitration award in the termination by applicant school board of respondent school employee because the court determined that the statutory review for a compulsory arbitration was improper and had to be changed to a standard where the judicial review was de novo review of questions of law and substantial-evidence review of findings of fact.

 

47 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State v. Hodge


Nos. 21,305, 21,310, 21,311, 21,313 (Consolidated)


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


118 N.M. 410; 1994-NMSC-087; 882 P.2d 1; 1994 N.M. LEXIS 333; 33 N.M. St. B. Bull. 1112



August 23, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Motion for Rehearing Denied September 16, 1994. Released for Publication September 16, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: ORIGINAL PROCEEDING ON CERTIORARI


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Writ of certiorari was granted with respect to judgments from the New Mexico Court of Appeals, which affirmed defendants' convictions on charges of possession of a controlled substances on the grounds that each defendant had waived his or her challenge to the sufficiency of the evidence by pleading guilty to the charged offense.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendants argued that the general rule limiting appeals following guilty pleas to jurisdictional issues was inapplicable where they expressly had conditioned their guilty pleas by reserving the right to appeal a specific nonjurisdictional issue. As an initial matter, the court noted that the state's rules of criminal procedure neither expressly authorized nor prohibited the use of conditional guilty pleas to reserve specific issues for appeal. The court then held that an issue of sufficiency of the evidence might be reserved for appellate review, particularly where the following critical requirements for a conditional plea were met: each defendant expressed an intention to reserve a particular pretrial issue for appeal and neither the prosecution nor the trial judge opposed such a plea. The court then found that as each defendant properly preserved the sufficiency issue for appeal, each had entered a valid conditional plea and the issue was reviewable on appeal. Accordingly, the court reversed the affirmance of defendants' convictions, allowed defendants to withdraw their guilty pleas, and remanded the causes so that the convictions could be set aside.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgments of conviction, and remanded each case with instructions to vacate each defendant's conviction on the charge of possession of a controlled substance.

Coleman v. United Eng'rs & Constructors, Inc.


No. 21,683


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


118 N.M. 47; 1994-NMSC-074; 878 P.2d 996; 1994 N.M. LEXIS 264; 33 N.M. St. B. Bull. 933; CCH Prod. Liab. Rep. P14,161



July 18, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication August 3, 1994. Counsel Amended August 31, 1994. As Corrected October 19, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF EDDY COUNTY. Fred A. Watson, District Judge


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff victim sought review of an order from the District Court of Eddy County (New Mexico) that granted summary judgment in favor of defendant company with respect to the victim's action for personal injuries sustained when a conveyor-belt manlift failed to operate properly.


OVERVIEW: The victim was injured in the course of her employment when she fell from a vertical conveyor-belt manlift after its top-limit switch failed to properly stop the device. The victim brought an action against the company and others involved in the manufacture, sale, distribution, and installation of the manlift. The trial court determined that the manlift was a physical improvement to real property and that the victim's claim against the company was barred by the 10-year limitations period of N.M. Stat. Ann. § 37-1-27 (Repl. Pamp. 1990). The trial court granted summary judgment in favor of the company. The victim contended that § 37-1-27 violated her equal protection and due process rights. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's order. The court determined that rational basis scrutiny, rather than intermediate scrutiny, applied to assess the constitutionality of § 37-1-27. The court held that § 37-1-27 was constitutional. The court found that the legislature's objective in enacting § 37-1-27 was permissible and rationally related to a legitimate governmental interest. The court also ruled that § 37-1-27 was not applied retroactively to the victim's case.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court that granted summary judgment in favor of the company with respect to the victim's action for personal injuries sustained when the conveyor-belt manlift failed to operate properly.

State v. Trujillo


No. 21,771


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


117 N.M. 769; 1994-NMSC-066; 877 P.2d 575; 1994 N.M. LEXIS 229; 33 N.M. St. B. Bull. 872



June 14, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication June 30, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF OTERO COUNTY. Sandra A. Grisham, District Judge


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed a decision from the district Court of Otero County (New Mexico), which changed the conditions of defendant's probation.


OVERVIEW: Because the petition was not filed within ninety days of the rendition of the sentence, as required by N.M. R. Crim. P. Dist. Ct. 5-801(B), the trial court had no authority to modify defendant's conditions of probation under this rule. The court refused to consider whether N.M. R. Crim. P. Dist. Ct. 5-104(B)(2) could be used to extend the time for such a filing, because no extension of time had been requested. The court agreed that under N.M. Stat. Ann. § 31-21-21, the trial court had discretion to modify conditions of probation in appropriate cases. It concluded, however, that the trial court abused its discretion by changing the conditions of defendant's probation. The changed condition was part of a valid plea bargain agreement which was binding on both parties. The trial court could not amend or modify the sentence imposed pursuant to the valid plea agreement in such a way that allowed one party to renege on its part of the agreement.


OUTCOME: The court reverse the decision and remanded the matter for reinstatement of the sentence originally agreed to by the parties.

County of Dona Ana v. Bennett


No. 20,308


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


116 N.M. 778; 1994-NMSC-005; 867 P.2d 1160; 1994 N.M. LEXIS 37; 33 N.M. St. B. Bull. 180



January 10, 1994, Decided  
January 10, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication January 28, 1994. As Corrected April 6, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: CERTIFICATION FROM THE NEW MEXICO COURT OF APPEALS. Lalo Garza, District Judge


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The New Mexico Court of Appeals certified an appeal to the court under N.M. Stat. Ann. § 34-5-14(C) (1978) in order to determine the proper date for valuing property taken by plaintiff county in a condemnation proceeding after defendant property owners appealed contending that the trial court had erred in refusing testimony on the value of removed soil and in refusing to give a jury instruction on the value of the soil.


OVERVIEW: The county filed a petition in the district court to condemn the property owners' property for highway improvements. The county filed its petition under the Special Alternative Condemnation Procedure established by N.M. Stat. Ann. § 42-2-1 to -24 (1978). The county filed a petition for a preliminary order of entry, entered the property, and began work that included removing soil from the property. The property owners objected to the preliminary order of entry and requested that the proceeding be dismissed, which the district court denied. The district court entered an order making the preliminary order of entry permanent. The jury returned verdicts in favor of the property owners and the district court entered judgment on the verdicts. The property owners appealed. The appellate court certified the appeal to the court, stating that its resolution required a determination of the proper date for valuing property taken in a condemnation proceeding. The court affirmed the district court's judgment adopting the date that the preliminary order became effective as the proper valuation date in a condemnation proceeding under the Special Alternative Condemnation Procedure.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the district court, which held that the date the preliminary order became effective was the proper date to use in assessing the value of property taken under the Special Alternative Condemnation Procedure.

State v. Simpson

CASE SUMMARY:

OVERVIEW: Defendant was the driver of a vehicle involved in a traffic accident in which three of defendant's passengers were killed. Defendant stipulated that his blood alcohol content was between .07 and .13 at the time of the accident. There was also some evidence that defendant was speeding. The court also found that the trial court did not err in giving withdrawn instruction on blood alcohol level and refusing proposed instruction on speeding and that the trial court did not err in admitting results of blood alcohol tests and unidentified statements.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions.

 

52 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State v. Henderson


No. 21,127


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


116 N.M. 537; 1993-NMSC-068; 865 P.2d 1181; 1993 N.M. LEXIS 346; 32 N.M. St. B. Bull. 1160



November 10, 1993, Decided  
November 10, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication November 29, 1993. As Corrected March 15, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: ORIGINAL PROCEEDING ON CERTIORARI. Alvin F. Jones, District Judge


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed a petition for certiorari review with the court after he was convicted of two counts of contributing to the delinquency of a minor (CDM) in violation of N.M. Stat. Ann. § 30-6-3 (Supp. 1992), and two counts of false imprisonment in violation of N.M. Stat. Ann. § 30-4-3 (1984), and the convictions were affirmed. Defendant asserted several errors.


OVERVIEW: Before the court were the issues of whether the uniform jury instruction for contributing to the delinquency of a minor (CDM), in violation of N.M. Stat. Ann. § 30-6-3 (Supp. 1992), was deficient, and whether it was error for the trial court to refuse to instruct the jury on the offense of indecent exposure before a minor as a lesser included offense of CDM. The court held that the trial court's jury instruction to find defendant guilty of CDM if his acts encouraged each of the girls in question to conduct herself in a manner injurious to her morals, health, or welfare adequately reflected the CDM statute because the legislature's earlier and subsequent use of injurious conduct to define juvenile delinquency or establish juvenile court jurisdiction did not limit the use of injurious conduct for purposes of CDM. Furthermore, the court found that defendant was not entitled to an instruction on indecent exposure as a lesser included offense of CDM because indecent exposure required that the acts take place in "public view" and there was no such element in the CDM statute. As such, the court affirmed defendant's convictions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions and sentences.

 

53 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State v. Trevino


No. 19,997


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


116 N.M. 528; 1993-NMSC-067; 865 P.2d 1172; 1993 N.M. LEXIS 347; 32 N.M. St. B. Bull. 1154



November 10, 1993, Decided  
November 10, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication November 29, 1993. As Corrected December 28, 1993. Second Correction March 15, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: ORIGINAL PROCEEDING ON CERTIORARI. William J. Schnedar, District Judge


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the decision of the court of appeals (New Mexico), which affirmed his convictions on four counts of criminal sexual contact with a minor in the third degree and two counts of contributing to the delinquency of a minor.


OVERVIEW: On review, the court affirmed and held that convictions on both charges based on unitary conduct did not violate principles of double jeopardy, that the state was not required to present evidence beyond the defendant's act to support a conviction for contributing to the delinquency of a minor, and that the act of the defendant need not actually have caused delinquency. The court found that the two crimes each required proof of a fact that the other did not. The court determined that the legislature intended for the crimes to be separate crimes, punishable separately even when unitary conduct violated both statutes, thus, defendant's claim that his convictions under both statutes violated double jeopardy principles was rejected. The court also found that the state was not required to present separate evidence that the defendant's act contributed to the delinquency of a minor. The court concluded that although contributing to the delinquency of a minor required proof of a fact that was not required to prove criminal sexual contact of a minor, that did not mean that the different facts could not be proved by the same evidence.


OUTCOME: The convictions for criminal sexual contact of a minor and contributing to the delinquency of a minor were affirmed.

 

54 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State v. Gutierrez


No. 19,893


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


116 N.M. 431; 1993-NMSC-062; 863 P.2d 1052; 1993 N.M. LEXIS 342; 32 N.M. St. B. Bull. 1078; 62 U.S.L.W. 2370



October 27, 1993, Decided  
October 27, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Writ of Certiorari filed June 3, 1991, Granted June 24, 1991. Released for Publication November 18, 1993. As Corrected February 9, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF BERNALILLO COUNTY. Woody Smith, District Judge


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state filed a petition for writ of certiorari to review a judgment by the Court of Appeals (New Mexico), which affirmed the suppression of evidence obtained through unannounced entry of defendants' residence as authorized in a search warrant.


OVERVIEW: The trial court suppressed evidence obtained through unannounced entry of defendants' residence as authorized in a search warrant because it found that the search warrant was invalid. The state argued that the evidence could still be admitted under the exclusionary rule's "good faith" exception. The court held that while federal courts recognized the good-faith exception under the federal constitution, the exception was incompatible with the guarantees of N.M. Const. art. II, § 10, which prohibited unreasonable searches and seizures and mandated the issuance of search warrants only upon probable cause. The court held that the purpose and basis for the state's exclusionary rule was incompatible with any exception based on the good-faith reliance of the officer on the magistrate's determination either of probable cause or of the reasonableness of the search. Consequently, the court held that the fruits of the search conducted in this case had to be suppressed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the suppression of evidence obtained through an invalid search warrant.

 

55 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State v. Green


No. 20,251


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


116 N.M. 273; 1993-NMSC-056; 861 P.2d 954; 1993 N.M. LEXIS 301; 32 N.M. St. B. Bull. 905



September 21, 1993, Decided  
September 21, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication October 7, 1993. As Corrected December 14, 1993. Second Correction February 9, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: CERTIFICATION FROM THE NEW MEXICO COURT OF APPEALS. David W. Bonem, District Judge


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of embezzlement and attempting to traffic cocaine after he failed to return $ 250 to an undercover police officer who, as a part of a police "sting," gave defendant the money and requested that defendant purchase cocaine for him. Defendant appealed his convictions to the New Mexico Court of Appeals, which pursuant to N.M. Stat. Ann. § 34-5-14(C), certified the appeal to the court.


OVERVIEW: The court held that the jury instruction given on embezzlement given was deficient because it failed to instruct the jury on all of the essential elements required under N.M. Stat. Ann § 30-16-8. The instruction failed to include the requirement that at the time of the conversion of the property at issue, defendant entertained a specific intent to deprive the owner of the property. Although defendant failed to object to the instruction at trial, the court found that the instruction constituted fundamental error. Therefore, the court reversed the embezzlement conviction. However, the court affirmed defendant's conviction for attempting to traffic cocaine, holding that there was substantial evidence to support the conviction. Defendant's acceptance of the money to purchase cocaine was an overt act in furtherance of the goal crime of trafficking in cocaine; the crime of attempt could be established based on this act. Finally, the court rejected defendant's claim that double jeopardy principles mandated that he could not be punished both for embezzlement and attempted trafficking, noting that the same conduct was not being used to support both charges.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for attempted trafficking in cocaine, reversed his conviction for embezzlement, and remanded to the trial court for a new trial on the embezzlement charge.

Whitely v. N.M. State Pers. Bd.


No. 20662


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


115 N.M. 308; 1993-NMSC-019; 850 P.2d 1011; 1993 N.M. LEXIS 88; 32 N.M. St. B. Bull. 381



April 1, 1993, Decided  
April 1, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication April 19, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF OTERO COUNTY. Richard A. Parsons, District Judge


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, juvenile probation officers (JPOs), challenged the decision of the District Court of Otero County (New Mexico) that granted the summary judgment motion of defendant, State Personnel Board, with respect to the JPOs' allegations that the Board violated Section 47(C) of the Youth Authority Act and impaired their contract in violation of N.M. Const. art. II, § 19 when the Board did not preserve the JPOs' rate of accrued vacation leave.


OVERVIEW: The court also dismissed the JPO's illegal diminution of compensation claim for failure to state a claim upon which relief could be granted. Pursuant to the Youth Authority Act, N.M. Laws, ch. 101, § 47(c) (1988), N.M. Stat. Ann. § 9-2A-5 (Supp. 1992), the JPOs were transferred from the judicial branch of the state government to another branch. They argued that according to the act, they continued to accrue annual vacation leave at judicial rates. The court affirmed the judgment, concluding that the judicial branch rates of accrual for annual leave were not preserved by the act's grandfather clause and that no unconstitutional impairment of contracts or diminution of compensation resulted. The court, using general rules of statutory construction, concluded that the rate of accrual of annual leave was not an "accrued benefit" under the plain meaning and structure of Section 47(C). The court explained that statutes fixing the compensation or terms of public employment were presumed merely to establish public policy subject to legislative revision and not to create contractual or vested rights.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the granting of the Board's motion for summary judgment and the dismissal of the JPOs' claims.

 

57 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Swink v. Fingado


No. 20364


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


115 N.M. 275; 1993-NMSC-013; 850 P.2d 978; 1993 N.M. LEXIS 90; 32 N.M. St. B. Bull. 363



March 2, 1993, Decided  
March 2, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication April 19, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: CERTIFICATION FROM THE TENTH CIRCUIT COURT OF APPEALS. William J. Holloway, Jr., Presiding Judge


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The court considered a question of law certified by the United States Court of Appeals for the Tenth Circuit after appellant trustee sought review of an order of the trial court in favor of appellee wife authorizing the sale of joint tenancy property held by appellee and the debtor spouse in the debtor's bankruptcy action. Appellant claimed that an amendment to N.M. Stat. Ann. § 40-3-8 (1978) applied retroactively.


OVERVIEW: An involuntary bankruptcy petition was filed against debtor spouse and appellee wife. The petition was dismissed against appellee. A judgment authorizing the sale of the parties' joint tenancy property was reversed. Appellant trustee claimed that a statutory amendment allowed treatment of joint tenancy property as community property. The court found that the savings clause indicated legislative intent of retroactivity, that retroactive application did not violate the New Mexico Constitution, that community debts were satisfied from all community property including joint tenancy property, and that the state's marital property laws presumed that all property acquired during the marriage was community property. The court held that the amendments to the statute were applied retroactively to treat joint tenancy property as community property includable in debtor's bankruptcy estate.


OUTCOME: The court held that the amendment to the New Mexico community property statute characterized joint tenancy property as community property. The court ordered that the trial court's order that voided appellant trustee's sale should have been reversed because joint tenancy property was community property includable in the bankruptcy estate to satisfy appellee wife and debtor's community debts.

 

58 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Santillanes v. State


No. 20638


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


115 N.M. 215; 1993-NMSC-012; 849 P.2d 358; 1993 N.M. LEXIS 68; 32 N.M. St. B. Bull. 268



March 1, 1993, Decided  
March 1, 1993, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication March 17, 1993. As Corrected April 22, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: ORIGINAL PROCEEDING ON CERTIORARI. Frank H. Allen, Jr., District Judge


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the Court of Appeals (New Mexico), which affirmed his conviction for child abuse under N.M. Stat. Ann. § 30-6-1(C) (Repl. Pamp. 1984). Defendant contended that the provision in the statute under which he was convicted was unconstitutional because it improperly criminalized ordinary civil negligence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted under N.M. Stat. Ann. § 30-6-1(C) (Repl. Pamp. 1984) of child abuse involving no death or great bodily injury after he cut his nephew's neck with a knife during an altercation. The court of appeals affirmed the conviction. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that the statute required at least a showing of criminal negligence. Where N.M. Stat. Ann. § 30-6-1(C) (Repl. Pamp. 1984) had been interpreted to criminalize innocent conduct, although negligent in the civil sense, that interpretation was held to be erroneous. All opinions that were inconsistent in any way with that analysis regarding criminal negligence were expressly overruled. While the trial court committed error in failing to instruct the jury on a criminal negligence standard, no rational jury could have concluded that defendant cut his nephew's throat without satisfying the standard of criminal negligence. As the element of criminal negligence was established by the evidence, the error in instructing the jury on a civil negligence standard instead of a criminal negligence standard was not reversible error.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction for child abuse involving no death or great bodily injury was affirmed in the absence of reversible error. The standard of criminal negligence adopted in the opinion was ordered to govern all cases pending on direct review, provided the issue was raised and preserved, and all cases pending but in which a verdict had not been reached.

State v. Hernandez


No. 19728


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


115 N.M. 6; 1993-NMSC-007; 846 P.2d 312; 1993 N.M. LEXIS 27; 32 N.M. St. B. Bull. 124



January 14, 1993, Decided  
January 14, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication February 1, 1993. As Corrected February 25, 1993. Second Correction July 1, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF GRANT COUNTY. V. Lee Vesely, District Judge



DISPOSITION: In accordance with the foregoing discussion, the decision of the trial court is AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the District Court of Grant County (New Mexico), which convicted him of first degree felony murder, aggravated burglary, attempted robbery, and battery and sentenced him to life imprisonment for the murder conviction. Defendant claimed he was denied effective assistance of counsel in violation of U.S. Const. amend. 14 and N.M. Const. art. II § 14.


OVERVIEW: A woman was found beaten and murdered. Hairs that did not match the victim were found in her mouth and on the bed. A man contacted police and relayed defendant's story of murdering the woman. Defendant was convicted of first degree felony murder, aggravated burglary, attempted robbery, and battery and was sentenced to life imprisonment for the murder conviction. The court affirmed, holding that defendant was not denied effective assistance of counsel under U.S. Const. amend. 14 and N.M. Const. art. II § 14 when the trial court denied his motion for a continuance because he had nearly a year to prepare for trial and suffered no prejudice without showing that any of his defense theories had a reasonable probability of success. Defendant was not prejudiced by the trial court's refusal to exclude a detective from the courtroom during trial because the detective already knew what the witnesses would say from his investigation. Graphic photographs were relevant to show defendant had the requisite intent to kill. There was no evidence of pretrial publicity that prejudiced the jurors to support a change of venue. The trial court's felony murder instruction was not fundamental error.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions and sentence because the trial court did not abuse its discretion in denying defendant's request for a continuance where he had nearly one year to prepare his case and was not prejudiced by the continuance. Defendant's counsel was not ineffective by failing to obtain an expert in forensics or hair analysis. The trial court did not err by allowing expert testify regarding hairs collected from the scene.

Carrillo v. Rostro


No. 19650


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


114 N.M. 607; 1992-NMSC-054; 845 P.2d 130; 1992 N.M. LEXIS 248; 31 N.M. St. B. Bull. 978; 49 A.L.R.5th 911



August 28, 1992, Decided  
August 28, 1992, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected December 7, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF SANDOVAL COUNTY. Kenneth G. Brown, District Judge


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, board of education (board) and its members, appealed a judgment of the District Court of Sandoval County (New Mexico), which denied summary judgment to members and held that they were not entitled to qualified immunity on plaintiff principal's civil rights claims under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983.


OVERVIEW: Board contended that its members were entitled to qualified immunity from principal's suit which alleged that board had violated her First Amendment rights when it declined to renew her contract because of her criticism of board at a public meeting. The court held that the issue of board members' objective reasonableness in engaging in the challenged conduct, as measured by reference to clearly established law at the time the conduct occurred was a legal issue and that summary judgment was an appropriate means for invoking the trial court's ruling on the question. Further, denial of summary judgment conclusively determined board members' claim of right not to stand trial on the allegations and thus, under the collateral order doctrine, the denial of summary judgment was reviewable. The court held that it could not see how the decision not to rehire principal could be characterized as anything other than an infringement of her First Amendment rights and there was no evidence of any adverse effects to board from her speech. Thus, board members had to submit relevant evidence at trial on how their interest outweighed principal's interest in commenting on public matters.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of summary judgment on principal's First Amendment claim, but it reversed summary judgment insofar as it related to her Fourteenth Amendment claim.

Ryan v. Gonzales


No. 20636


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


114 N.M. 346; 1992-NMSC-052; 838 P.2d 963; 1992 N.M. LEXIS 262; 31 N.M. St. B. Bull. 951



August 28, 1992, Decided  
August 28, 1992, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected December 16, 1992. Second Correction December 29, 1992.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner state representatives sought a writ of mandamus directing respondent secretary of state to submit multiple questions rather than a single question to the voters under the 1992 Capital Projects General Obligation Bond Act, 1992 N.M. Laws, ch. 103, §§ 1-17.


OVERVIEW: The state representatives sought a writ of mandamus to direct the secretary of state to submit multiple questions to the voters for the capital projects in the 1992 Capital Projects General Obligation Bond Act, 1992 N.M. Laws, ch. 103, §§ 1-17. The state representatives argued that multiple questions were required by N.M. Const. art. IX, § 8. The court agreed and directed the secretary of state to submit multiple questions to the voters. The court noted that N.M. Const. art. IX, § 8 required that debts for specified works or objects be submitted to the voters and that this provision was intended to prevent logrolling, which was the combining of multiple projects to achieve the passage of all. Because the projects combined under the Act did not naturally relate to each other, the court concluded that they could not be considered in a single submission to the voters. The court found that there was an alternative multiple grouping of projects under the Act that had a more natural relationship to each other and that the submission of these multiple groupings to the voters would be constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court granted the mandamus relief requested by the state representatives and directed the secretary of state to submit multiple questions to the voters on various capital projects.

Timberon Water Co. v. N.M. PSC (In re Timberon Water Co.)

PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM ORDER OF THE PUBLIC SERVICE COMMISSION


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant trustee sought review of a ruling from the New Mexico Public Service Commission, which denied appellant's requested water rate increase.


OVERVIEW: Appellee commission granted a water company a certificate of public convenience and necessity authorizing the company to charge rates for water. The company's president executed a promissory note with a mortgage to a bank. The company filed for bankruptcy under chapter 11. Appellee's staff petitioned appellee to investigate the company's quality of service and the propriety of the promissory note and mortgage. Appellant trustee filed a petition for a rate increase. 63 of 795 DOCUMENTS


JMB Retail Props. Co. v. Eastburn


No. 20594


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


114 N.M. 115; 1992-NMSC-045; 835 P.2d 831; 1992 N.M. LEXIS 231; 31 N.M. St. B. Bull. 826



August 3, 1992, Decided  
August 3, 1992, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected.


PRIOR HISTORY: ORIGINAL PROCEEDING ON SUPERINTENDING CONTROL, PROHIBITION, OR MANDAMUS


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner company filed a peremptory election to excuse respondent judge of the district court (New Mexico) from presiding over the pending, wherein the company was a defendant. An order was entered denying the election to excuse and the company petitioned the court for a writ of superintending control, prohibition, or mandamus requiring the judge to recognize the election.


OVERVIEW: The company sought to have the judge excused as judge from the underlying case. The judge entered an order denying the election to excuse and the company petitioned for a writ of mandamus. The court denied the petition, holding that the company invoked the discretion of the court by requesting an extension of time within which to answer or otherwise plead, and that the company was then prohibited from peremptorily challenging the judge. The court held that an extension of time to answer or otherwise plead was a discretionary act, even if in response to the agreed motion or stipulation of the parties, and pointed out that the rule that a judge may not be peremptorily challenged after a party has invoked the discretion of the court depended, actually, not upon whether the court in fact exercised discretion, but depended upon whether the response of the court was subject to discretion. The court explained that the judge could have granted or denied the agreed motion for extension of time, therefore, his entry of the agreed order was subject to discretion and not a mere ministerial act.


OUTCOME: The court denied the petition for mandamus, which sought to excuse the judge from presiding over the underlying case.

 

64 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Roberts v. Southwest Cmty. Health Servs.


No. 19905


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


114 N.M. 248; 1992-NMSC-042; 837 P.2d 442; 1992 N.M. LEXIS 219; 31 N.M. St. B. Bull. 735



July 14, 1992, Decided  
July 14, 1992, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected December 7, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: ORIGINAL PROCEEDING ON CERTIORARI. Susan M. Conway, District Judge



DISPOSITION: Accordingly, we reverse and remand with instructions for further proceedings consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Court of Appeals (New Mexico) affirmed the summary judgment granted in favor of respondent health care provider on petitioner patient's medical malpractice claim. The matter was before the court on the patient's petition for a writ of certiorari. The patient argued that her claim was not barred by the statute of limitations set forth in the Medical Malpractice Act, N.M. Stat. Ann. § 41-5-13.


OVERVIEW: In 1984, the patient underwent surgery at the health care provider's hospital. In 1990, the patient filed a medical malpractice suit alleging that the surgeons and the nurses failed to remove a sponge from her abdomen during the 1984 operation. The complaint joined the health care provider under the theory of respondeat superior. The intermediate appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment that that the patient's claim accrued at the time of the wrongful act and that the three-year statute of limitations set forth in the Medical Malpractice Act (act), N.M. Stat. Ann. § 41-5-13, barred her claim against the health care provider. On appeal, the court held that § 41-5-13 did not apply to the health care provider because § 41-5-5(C) limited the act's benefits to qualified health care providers, § 41-5-13 was a benefit under the act, and the health care provider was not qualified under § 41-5-5(A) of the act. The court further held that the patient's claim, which fell outside the act, accrued when she knew or should have known of her injury and its cause and that it was specifically within the trial court's province to determine when the patient had made that discovery.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded for further proceedings.

 

65 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Jaramillo v. Jaramillo


No. 19324


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


113 N.M. 57; 1991-NMSC-101; 823 P.2d 299; 1991 N.M. LEXIS 401; 31 N.M. St. B. Bull. 74



December 24, 1991  
December 24, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied January 16, 1992. As Corrected.


PRIOR HISTORY: ORIGINAL PROCEEDING ON CERTIORARI. Lalo Garza, District Judge


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner custodial parent sought a writ of certiorari to review whether placing the burden of proof upon a joint custodial parent to show that a proposed relocation was in the child's best interest imposed an unconstitutional restriction upon respondent relocating parent's right to travel.


OVERVIEW: The parents had a joint custody arrangement, with most times spent with custodial parent. The custodial parent claimed that requiring her to remain in one state with the child restricted her rights under the constitution to be free to travel as she saw fit. The court said that when the parents operated under a joint custody arrangement and one of them sought to alter the arrangement, it made perfectly sense to impose a presumption in favor of the parent who wished to continue to operate under the joint custody decree and to place on the party wishing to change the decree the burden to produce evidence that the arrangement is no longer workable and needs to be changed. Finally, the court said that either party could have initiated a proceeding to alter an existing custody arrangement on the ground that a substantial and material change in circumstances affecting the welfare of the child occurred, or was about to occur, and the party seeking such change always would have the burden to show that the existing arrangement was no longer workable.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the court of appeals and remanded to the district court with instructions to reinstate its order revising the parties' parenting plan and permitting the mother to move with the child to another state.

 

66 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State v. Chamberlain


No. 18938


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


112 N.M. 723; 1991-NMSC-094; 819 P.2d 673; 1991 N.M. LEXIS 400



September 25, 1991, Decided  
September 25, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF BERNALILLO COUNTY. Frank Allen, District Judge


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a decision of the District Court of Bernalillo County (New Mexico) that convicted him of first-degree murder and sentences him to life in prison.


OVERVIEW: Defendant hired a prostitute and took her to his home. That evening she called the police to report a beating, and two officers responded. Defendant consented to the officers' search of his house, but later attempted to withdraw consent. When the police insisted on continuing the search, defendant shot and killed one of the officers. Two trials were held. In the first, defendant was convicted of several lesser offenses, but a mistrial was declared on the capital charge. In the second, defendant was convicted of first-degree murder. On appeal, the court affirmed and held, inter alia, that: (1) defendant did not show the necessity of a change of venue, so it was not error for the district court to deny defendant's motion to change venue; (2) it was within the district court's discretion to admit a tape recording of the search of defendant's house including the sounds of the officer after he was shot; (3) the prosecutor's closing argument was proper and did not deny defendant a fair trial; (4) the jury was permitted to experiment with the dead officer's gun and holster during its deliberations; and (5) defendant's claims of ineffective assistance of counsel were unfounded.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the district court, which convicted defendant of first-degree murder and sentenced him to life in prison.

Caristo v. Sullivan


Nos. 19,190, 19,232


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


112 N.M. 623; 1991-NMSC-088; 818 P.2d 401; 1991 N.M. LEXIS 349; 30 N.M. St. B. Bull. 962



September 23, 1991, Decided  
September 23, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied October 24, 1991. As Amended.


PRIOR HISTORY: Original Proceedings on Certiorari; Honorable Joe Cruz Castellano, District Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The court granted petitioner inmates' requests for a writ of certiorari to the District Court, Santa Fe County (New Mexico), to review the district court's dismissal of each inmate's petition for a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: Both cases involved a lengthy delay between the filing of the habeas corpus petition and the ultimate disposition in the district court. The court found that the district court was chiefly responsible for the numerous delays, failures to act, and inappropriate orders that caused the inordinate delays. The inmates argued that the delays entitled them to default judgments on their habeas corpus petitions. Although the court concluded that a default judgment might be appropriate in an extreme case for the state's failure to respond to a writ of habeas corpus, the court declined to impose that remedy in favor of either inmate in the instant action. The court proceeded to consider the merits of both petitions in order to bring the protracted proceedings to an end. The court reversed the denial of one inmate's petition and remanded his case for resentencing because he was not given notice prior to his sentencing hearing of the state's intention to seek enhancement of his basic sentence under N.M. Stat. Ann. § 31-18-15.1. The court dismissed the second inmate's petition, finding no merit in his claim of entitlement to sentencing credit for time served on a separate Georgia offense.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the denial of one inmate's habeas corpus petition and remanded his case for resentencing. The court dismissed the petition of the second inmate, finding that he was not entitled to relief.

 

68 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State v. Neely


No. 19085


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


112 N.M. 702; 1991-NMSC-087; 819 P.2d 249; 1991 N.M. LEXIS 330; 30 N.M. St. B. Bull. 899



September 20, 1991, Decided  
September 20, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Amended. Second Amendment.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of Bernalillo County; W. C. "Woody" Smith, District Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment from the District Court (New Mexico), which, after a jury trial, convicted her of murder in a verdict of guilty but mentally ill pursuant to N.M. Stat. Ann. § 31-9-3 (1978) (Repl. Pamp.1984).


OVERVIEW: Defendant had a history of mental illness and drove her car into a family, killing one member and injuring two others. The sole issue at trial was whether she was criminally insane. The jury returned a verdict of guilty but mentally ill. Defendant argued that there was no difference between those found not guilty by reason of insanity and those found guilty but mentally ill; they were similarly situated, yet they were treated differently. Thus, because it did not create a rational classification, the guilty but mentally ill verdict violated the Equal Protection Clauses of the United States and New Mexico Constitutions. On appeal, the court found that the classification was rational. It allowed those mentally ill who did not have the capacity to form the appropriate criminal intent to avoid criminal liability, and provided criminal liability for those guilty because they possessed the criminal intent, yet who were mentally ill. The court held that although the classification created two classes of mentally ill defendants, those classes were not similarly situated and their legislative creation was not arbitrary. The court affirmed the judgment of the district court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the district court. The court did not find merit in the arguments of defendant or unconstitutionality in the statute that provided for a verdict of mentally ill.

 

69 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State v. Ortega


No. 18225


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


112 N.M. 554; 1991-NMSC-084; 817 P.2d 1196; 1991 N.M. LEXIS 331; 30 N.M. St. B. Bull. 912



September 3, 1991, Decided  
September 3, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Amended. Rehearing Denied October 9, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of Bernalillo County; Richard B. Traub, District Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In accordance with the jury verdict, the District Court of Bernalillo County (New Mexico) convicted defendant of two felony murders, two first-degree kidnappings, armed robbery, attempted armed robbery, and several counts of conspiracy to commit murder, kidnapping, and robbery. Defendant was sentenced to two consecutive terms of life imprisonment for the murders and a total of 87 years' imprisonment on the remaining felonies. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: After meeting two "rich" girls in a park, defendant and co-defendant convinced them to drive to a vacant lot to wait for an expected cocaine delivery. In exchange for use immunity, co-defendant testified that defendant stabbed the girls to death. Although he was found not guilty of first-degree murder, defendant was convicted of all other charges, including felony murder. The state supreme court held that the felony-murder statute required proof that defendant intended to kill. Nevertheless, the felony-murder verdicts were affirmed because there was sufficient evidence that defendant caused the victims' deaths, either through his own acts or those of an accomplice whom he helped and encouraged, and with the intent to commit the killings or with knowledge of a strong probability of death or great bodily harm to each victim. The kidnapping convictions were upheld because both victims were held for service to benefit defendant by being induced, by deception, to accompany him to a remote location as part of an overall plan. The kidnapping and murder convictions did not merge because the conduct underlying the offenses was not unitary. Defendant's other grounds of error lacked merit.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions in their entirety.

 

70 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Thompson v. McKinley County


No. 19,119


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


112 N.M. 425; 1991-NMSC-076; 816 P.2d 494; 1991 N.M. LEXIS 297



August 20, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication September 5, 1991. As Amended.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of McKinley County; Art Encinias, District Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, the owners of retail liquor establishments with drive-up windows, sought review of an order of the District Court of McKinley County (New Mexico), which dismissed their complaint against appellees, the county and the city, in an action seeking to declare unconstitutional N.M. Stat. Ann. § 60-7A-1(F) (Michie Cum. Supp. 1990), as amended 1991 N.M. Laws ch. 255.


OVERVIEW: Section 60-7A-1(F) provided for an election in "eligible counties" on whether a retailer was allowed to sell or deliver alcoholic beverages at any time from a drive-up window. An "eligible county" was one that had reported motor vehicle statistics to the state highway and transportation department informing the state that it had convicted more than 25 persons for each 1,000 licensed drivers of driving while intoxicated. The county named in the suit was near large reservations of Native Americans where alcohol was not sold. The county also had substantial alcohol-related health problems and deaths. The owners of the liquor stores argued that the statute was unconstitutional because there was no evidence that alcohol abuse was greater in their county than in other counties in the state and because there was no proof that the alcohol problem was based on drive-up windows. The court held that: (1) the statute was special legislation; (2) there was a rational relationship between the statute's classification and the evil it was designed to prevent; (3) the statute did not violate the equal protection clause; and (4) the statute was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the district court.

State v. Gonzales


No. 18,955


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


112 N.M. 544; 1991-NMSC-075; 817 P.2d 1186; 1991 N.M. LEXIS 326; 30 N.M. St. B. Bull. 894



August 19, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Amended. Rehearing Denied October 3, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of Bernalillo County; Diane Dal Santo, District Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the District Court of Bernalillo County (New Mexico), convicting him of felony murder and armed robbery.


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed defendant's conviction, holding that (1) the trial court did not fail to sua sponte order a taint hearing to determine if the state's evidence derived from sources independent of immunized testimony given by defendant in a co-defendant's trial because defendant failed to raise the issue at trial or question the source of the state's evidence; (2) defendant's jury selection challenge failed as he did not show that registered voters in the county where the trial was held did not represent a fair cross section of the community; (3) the trial court did abuse its discretion by denying defendant's motion for a continuance because defendant's need for the continuance was caused by his own delay; (4) the trial court did not err by denying defendant's motion for a mistrial on the ground that the prosecutor made improper remarks during voir dire about the standard of proof needed for conviction because the trial court maintained control of voir dire and instructed the prosecutor not to mention further the standard of proof; and (5) the doctrine of cumulative error had no application in defendant's case because no errors were committed and defendant received a fair trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for felony murder and armed robbery.

Stroh Brewery Co. v. Dir. of N.M. Dep't of Alcoholic Beverage Control


No. 19,547


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


112 N.M. 468; 1991-NMSC-072; 816 P.2d 1090; 1991 N.M. LEXIS 306



August 12, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected October 3, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of Santa Fe County; Art Encinias, District Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant brewery sought review of the decision from the District Court of Santa Fe County (New Mexico), which granted summary judgment to appellee alcohol beverage director and awarded appellee damages plus interest.


OVERVIEW: Appellant brewery sought review of the trial court's grant of summary judgment and damages to appellee alcohol beverage director. Appellant's predecessor filed a complaint seeking a declaratory judgment and injunctive relief, alleging that the price affirmation requirement violated the Commerce Clause of the United States Constitution. The trial court entered a preliminary injunction temporarily and then issued a memorandum opinion granting summary judgment to appellee. The United States Supreme Court issued opinions, which changed the law on the subject of pricing affirmation requirements. The parties moved again for summary judgment, which the trial court granted in favor of appellee. On appeal, the court concluded that retroactive application of the Supreme Court opinion to the case at bar would serve no purpose advanced by the Commerce Clause of the United States Constitution. Further, the court found that the trial court was justified to regard any retroactive application of the case as potentially productive of both inequitable results and harm to the state. The court affirmed the judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's grant of summary judgment in favor of appellee alcohol beverage director because the trial court was justified to regard any retroactive application a U.S. Supreme Court case as potentially productive of both inequitable results and harm to the state.

 

73 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Public Serv. Co. v. N.M. Pub. Serv. Comm'n (In re Public Serv. Co.)


No. 19457


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


112 N.M. 379; 1991-NMSC-083; 815 P.2d 1169; 1991 N.M. LEXIS 314; 30 N.M. St. B. Bull. 842



July 9, 1991, Decided  
August 29, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Amended on Denial of Rehearing August 29, 1991. As Corrected October 3, 1991. Second Amendment.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Order of the Public Service Commission; Case No. 2296.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant utility sought review of an order from appellee New Mexico Public Service Commission (Commission), which denied the utility's N.M. Stat. Ann. § 62-9-5 application for abandonment and decertification of the utility's interest in a facility that had been excluded from the utility's rate base as part of the Commission's remedy for the utility's substantial excess generating capacity.


OVERVIEW: With the utility faced with excess generating capacity, the Commission fashioned a remedy that required exclusion of a facility from the utility's rate base. Pursuant to N.M. Stat. Ann. § 62-9-5, the utility filed an application for abandonment and decertification of its interest in the facility. When the Commission denied the application, review was sought, and the court affirmed. After upholding the Commission's use of decertification factors in its consideration of the interests of both the utility and consumers, the court held that because the operative question had turned upon the facility's use, § 62-9-5 had authorized decertification only upon a finding that present and future public convenience and necessity did not otherwise require such use. In upholding the Commission's findings and its refusal to authorize decertification, the court held the utility: 1) had failed to show the facility was not needed for future public convenience and necessity; and 2) had failed to support its claim of financial harm. Finally, the court held that refusing to decertify the utility's interest, while at the same time excluding it from the rate base, was not an unconstitutional taking.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed an order from the Commission which denied the utility's application for abandonment and decertification of the utility's interest in a facility that had been excluded from the utility's rate base as part of the Commission's remedy for the utility's substantial excess generating capacity.

State ex rel. Udall v. Colonial Penn Ins. Co.


Nos. 19,052, 19,268


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


112 N.M. 123; 1991-NMSC-048; 812 P.2d 777; 1991 N.M. LEXIS 203



May 8, 1991, Filed

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of Santa Fe County; Steve Herrera, District Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff state challenged the decision of the District Court of Santa Fe County (New Mexico), which granted summary judgment to defendant insurance companies in two consolidated lawsuits for breach of contract. State also appealed summary judgment in favor of defendant advisor for alleged breach of contract, breach of fiduciary duty, negligent misrepresentation, and fraud.


OVERVIEW: A state investment officer bought stock contrary to state law. It was alleged state's advisor knew of the limitations on purchases and advised them. Insurers issued bonds covering state employees for unfaithful performance of their duties. However, claims were denied under time-to-sue provisions. The trial court granted all defendants' motions for summary judgment. State appealed contending certain provisions asserted against the sovereign violated public policy and should have been declared void. Controverted material issues of fact with regard to knowing willful misfeasance, bad faith, or reckless disregard of advisor's contractual obligations existed and Congress recognized an investment adviser was a fiduciary creating a duty.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part and reversed in part the judgment of the district court. The court remanded for a trial consistent with the opinion.

Swafford v. State


No. 18,974


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


112 N.M. 3; 1991-NMSC-043; 810 P.2d 1223; 1991 N.M. LEXIS 166



May 1, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: May 1, 1991, Filed
As Corrected.


PRIOR HISTORY: Original Proceeding on Certiorari; Fred T. Hensley, District Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought certiorari review of his conviction from the district court (New Mexico) for third-degree sexual penetration, incest, aggravated assault with intent to commit a felony, and false imprisonment, in violation of N.M. Stat. Ann. §§ 30-9-11(C), 30-10-3, 30-3-3, & 30-4-3 (Repl. Pamp. 1984) respectively.


OVERVIEW: Defendant tied his half-sister to a bed then inserted first a candle, then his penis, into her vagina. He was convicted of third-degree sexual penetration, incest, aggravated assault with intent to commit a felony, and false imprisonment, in violation of N.M. Stat. Ann. §§ 30-9-11(C), 30-10-3, 30-3-3, and 30-4-3 (Repl. Pamp. 1984) respectively. After his appeal was dismissed, he brought a petition for post-conviction relief, which was dismissed by the district court. The court affirmed the convictions but remanded for resentencing. The court held that separate, consecutive sentences for sexual penetration and incest were not violative of double jeopardy. The court found strong indicia of legislative intent to punish separately. There was no need to merge the offenses for sentencing. The assault with the candle was distinct from the sexual intercourse. The court held that the sentence for sexual assault was enhanced in error because the enhancement was based on an element of the incest. There was no error in enhancing the sentence for lack of remorse. Such lack is a circumstance "concerning the offender" that could be a factor under N.M. Stat. Ann. § 31-18-15.1(A).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the convictions but remanded the case for resentencing. The court held that separate, consecutive sentences for sexual assault and incest did not violate double jeopardy. The legislature intended to punish them separately. The sentence for sexual assault was erroneously enhanced because such enhancement was based on an element of incest. There was no error in enhancing based on lack of remorse.
