Mitchell v. City of Farmington Police Dep't (In re Forfeiture of Two Thousand Seven Hundred Thirty Dollars & No Cents ($2,730.00) in Cash)


No. 19,309, 19,373


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


111 N.M. 746; 1991-NMSC-035; 809 P.2d 1274; 1991 N.M. LEXIS 148; 30 N.M. St. B. Bull. 429



April 10, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Original Proceeding on Certiorari; James L. Brown, District Judge; Bruce E. Kaufman, District Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In one case, petitioner claimant sought review of a judgment of the court of appeals (New Mexico), which granted respondent city's motion to dismiss the claimant's appeal. The trial court had entered a default judgment of forfeiture against the claimant. In a second case, petitioner state sought review of a judgment of the court of appeals, which reversed the trial court's denial of respondent claimant's motion to set aside a default judgment.


OVERVIEW: The cases involved forfeiture proceedings initiated by state entities under the Controlled Substances Act. The court granted certiorari to consider whether execution on a forfeiture judgment divested an appellate court of jurisdiction to consider an appeal from the judgment. In the first case, the claimant did not file a supersedeas bond to stay execution of a default judgment of forfeiture. In the second case, neither the claimant nor his counsel was given notice of the state's application for default judgment. The appellate court held that it had jurisdiction to hear the appeal because the default judgment had been improperly entered. The court reversed the appellate court's judgment in the first case, remanding the case to the appellate court because the inability to post a supersedeas bond could not have operated to deny the right to a stay. The court affirmed the appellate court's judgment in the second case on the issue of appellate jurisdiction. The court held that when a state entity initiated a forfeiture proceeding, thereby invoking the jurisdiction of the courts of New Mexico, those courts retained in personam jurisdiction until all appeals had been exhausted.


OUTCOME: In the first case, the court reversed the judgment of the appellate court, which granted the city's motion to dismiss the claimant's appeal of a default judgment of forfeiture under the Controlled Substances Act. The case was remanded to the appellate court. In the second case, the court affirmed the judgment of the appellate court, which reversed the trial court's denial of the claimant's motion to set aside a default judgment.

State v. Osborne


No. 19,533


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


111 N.M. 654; 1991-NMSC-032; 808 P.2d 624; 1991 N.M. LEXIS 120



April 4, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Amended.


PRIOR HISTORY: Certification from the Court of Appeals; Benjamin S. Eastburn, District Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed judgment of the trial court, which convicted him of criminal sexual contact of a minor (CSCM). The Court of Appeals (New Mexico) certified questions for review regarding defendant's conviction.


OVERVIEW: Defendant lived with his girlfriend and her daughter. While alone with his girlfriend's daughter and the daughter's friend, defendant allegedly patted or rubbed the friend's buttocks. At defendant's trial, a dispute arose about whether a jury instruction regarding CSCM should have referred to the term "unlawfully." The trial court did not include the term in the instructions, and defendant was convicted of CSCM. Defendant appealed. The appellate court certified questions for the court's review. The court reversed the trial court's judgment and held that by defining CSCM as "unlawfully and intentionally" touching a child's intimate parts, the legislature properly intended that the state had to establish the unlawfulness of the touching as a distinct element of the offense. The court also found that defendant did not waive his claim of error based on the absence of an instruction on unlawfulness, which was an essential element of the offense of CSCM, despite the fact that he objected to an instruction that might have cured the error. The court concluded that the omission in the jury instructions was a fundamental error that required reversal. The case was remanded for a new trial.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment, which convicted defendant of CSCM, and remanded for a new trial.

Lovelace Medical Ctr. v. Mendez


No. 18,766


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


111 N.M. 336; 1991-NMSC-002; 805 P.2d 603; 1991 N.M. LEXIS 22



January 7, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected.


PRIOR HISTORY: Original Proceeding on Certiorari; Albert S. "Pat" Murdoch, District Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner hospital challenged a decision of the Court of Appeals (New Mexico) reversing the district court's partial summary judgment in favor of hospital in respondent parents' tort action against hospital for a negligently performed, unsuccessful sterilization operation.


OVERVIEW: Baby was conceived after respondent mother underwent a tubal ligation that allegedly was negligently performed by a physician employee of hospital. The questions presented on review concerned the jurisdiction of the appellate court to hear petitioner's application for interlocutory appeal and whether parents could recover the costs of raising baby. The court held that the legislature did not intend the 20-day time requirement of N.M. Stat. Ann. § 39-3-4 to be a limitation on the appellate courts' jurisdiction over interlocutory appeals, and there was no claim, nor any indication, that the court of appeals' taking an extra eight days to grant parents' application for interlocutory appeal had any prejudicial effect on hospital. The court also found that given that a tort occurred and that an injury has resulted, parents were entitled to claim damages for physical and emotional pain and suffering associated with pregnancy, but not for emotional or psychological pain and suffering resulting from the presence of an additional family member.


OUTCOME: The judgment reversing the district court was affirmed and the matter was remanded to the district court for further proceedings consistent with the opinion.

State v. Cawley


No. 18634


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


110 N.M. 705; 1990-NMSC-088; 799 P.2d 574; 1990 N.M. LEXIS 329



October 2, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected October 17, 1990. As Corrected.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of Eddy County; Patrick J. Francoeur, District Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment of the District Court of Eddy County (New Mexico), which convicted and sentenced him after a jury trial of rape of a child, criminal sexual contact of a minor, and one count of contributing to the delinquency of a minor. Defendant pleaded nolo contendere to four other counts of contributing to the delinquency of a minor.


OVERVIEW: The trial court imposed the basic sentence for each of defendant's convictions, enhanced each due to aggravating circumstances, and ordered the sentences to run consecutively for a total of life in prison plus 14 years. The court affirmed the judgment and the sentence. The court held that the criminal statute of limitations was properly tolled during defendant's voluntary absence from New Mexico pursuant to former N.M. Stat. Ann. § 40A-1-9(A) (1953, Repl. Vol. 1964), N.M. Stat. Ann. § 30-1-9(A) (1978, Repl. Pamp. 1984). Defendant's constitutional rights to travel and to equal protection were not violated because the tolling provision simply subjected him to responsibility for a longer period of time because of his voluntary choice to leave the state. The five-year limitations period for contributing to the delinquency of a minor did not have to be charged because it was not an essential element of the crime. Jury instructions were not erroneous because they tracked the language of the respective statutes. The trial court did not abuse its discretion in allowing evidence of one of the defendant's nolo contendere pleas to impeach him and did not err in enhancing his sentences.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions and sentences for rape of a child, criminal sexual contact of a minor, and contributing to the delinquency of a minor, as well as his nolo contendere pleas to additional counts of contributing to the delinquency of a minor.

Trujillo v. City of Albuquerque


No. 18296


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


110 N.M. 621; 1990-NMSC-083; 798 P.2d 571; 1990 N.M. LEXIS 305



August 27, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected August 31, 1990. As Corrected October 23, 1990. As Corrected October 25, 1990. As Corrected.


PRIOR HISTORY: Original Proceeding on Certiorari; Albert S. "Pat" Murdoch, District Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff trucker filed a negligence action against defendant city. Following a nonjury trial, the trial court rendered a judgment in favor of the trucker. The city appealed. A New Mexico appellate court reversed two rulings of the trial court regarding the interpretation and application of the statutory damage cap set forth in N.M. Stat. Ann. § 41-4-19(A)(2) of the Tort Claims Act, N.M. Stat. Ann. §§ 41-4-1 to 41-4-27. The trucker appealed.


OVERVIEW: A city employee drove a crane through a red light. The crane collided with the trucker's vehicle, causing injury to the trucker. In rendering a judgment in favor of the trucker, the trial court found that the accident involved two "occurrences" and that the limit of the city's liability was, thus, twice the $ 300,000 cap provide for in N.M. Stat. Ann. § 41-4-19(A)(2). The trial court also held that the damage cap violated the trucker's equal protection rights. The appellate court reversed both rulings. The court held that (1) the city's negligent maintenance of the crane and the employee's negligent operation of the crane constituted a single "occurrence" for the purposes of § 41-4-19(A)(2); (2) the liability limitation set forth in § 41-4-19(A)(2) was subject to intermediate equal protection scrutiny; (3) preservation of the public treasury was an important governmental interest; (4) under intermediate scrutiny standard, the reviewing court was required to consider whether less restrictive means were available; and (5) the record was insufficient to permit a determination of whether § 41-4-19(A)(2) was substantially related to legislature's interest in preserving public funds.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the appellate court and remanded the matter to the trial court for further proceedings.

 

83 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Grantland v. Lea Reg'l Hosp., Inc.


No. 19230


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


110 N.M. 378; 1990-NMSC-076; 796 P.2d 599; 1990 N.M. LEXIS 273



August 23, 1990, Decided  
August 20, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected.


PRIOR HISTORY: Original Proceeding on Certiorari; William J. Schnedar, District Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a patient and his wife, appealed the decision of the Court of Appeals (New Mexico), which reversed the denial of defendant hospital's motion to dismiss the medical malpractice complaint of the patient and his wife on the basis that the statute of limitations barred recovery.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to the Medical Malpractice Act (Act), N.M. Stat. Ann. §§ 41-5-1 to -28 (1978), the patient and his wife filed an application with the medical review commission (commission), requesting consideration of their medical malpractice claim against the hospital. Before they were notified by the commission that the hospital was not a qualified health care provider, the patient and his wife filed a medical malpractice action in the district court. Even though the statute of limitations had expired, the district court denied the hospital's motion to dismiss the complaint. The court of appeals reversed, and the patient and his wife sought review of the decision. The court reversed the court of appeals and affirmed the district court's denial of the hospital's motion to dismiss. The court found that if the patient and his wife were required to file in district court at the peril of losing their case before the classification of the health care provider was known, then every claim would be filed in district court as a safety precaution, and the purpose behind the Act, which was to prevent court filing of nonmeritorious malpractice claims, would be defeated.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision, which reversed the denial of the hospital's motion to dismiss the medical malpractice complaint. The denial of the motion to dismiss was affirmed with directions for the district court to proceed in a manner consistent with the court's opinion.

Los Quatros, Inc. v. State Farm Life Ins. Co.


No. 18443


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


110 N.M. 750; 1990-NMSC-082; 800 P.2d 184; 1990 N.M. LEXIS 317; 29 N.M. St. B. Bull. 967



August 23, 1990, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of Bernalillo County; Rebecca Sitterly, District Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, mortgagee and mortgagee's agent, challenged the judgment of the District Court of Bernalillo County (New Mexico), which declared that appellant's ban on prepayment of appellee mortgagor's loan could not be enforced in light of N.M. Stat. Ann. § 48-7-19(A) (1983). Appellants claimed that the statute violated U.S. Const. art. I, § 10 and N.M. Const. art. II, § 19.


OVERVIEW: After appellee mortgagee was not permitted by appellants, mortgagor and mortgagor's agent, to prepay its loan, appellee sought a declaration that it had the right to prepay and that the prepayment penalty was unenforceable under N.M. Stat. Ann. § 48-7-19 (1983). The court entered a judgment and declared that appellee could prepay the loan. The court affirmed and held that the plain language of § 48-7-19 mandated that the prepayment penalty was unenforceable whether or not there had been a sale of the property and whether or not the lender had sought to exercise its options under a due-on-sale clause. The Garn St.Germain Depository Institutions Act of 1982, 12 U.S.C.S. 1701j-3(b)(1), did not preempt the enforcement of clauses concerning the prepayment of loans or prevent a state from enlarging the class of loans subject to the prohibition on prepayment penalties, so long as they were real property loans made or assumed during the window period. N.M. Stat. Ann. § 48-7-19 promoted the alienability of land to withstand challenge under the Contract Clause of U.S. Const. art. I, § 10 and N.M. Const. art. II, § 19.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the district court that held a prepayment penalty sought to be imposed by the mortgagee and mortgagee's agent was unenforceable against the mortgagor. A statutory prohibition on prepayment penalties applied whether or not there had been a sale and whether or not the lender had sought to exercise its options under a due-on-sale clause and was constitutional under the Contract Clause.

Oil Transp. Co. v. N.M. State Corp. Comm'n


No. 18212


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


110 N.M. 568; 1990-NMSC-072; 798 P.2d 169; 1990 N.M. LEXIS 265



July 17, 1990, Decided  
July 17, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied August 10, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of Santa Fe County; Roger L. Copple, District Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, an oil transport company, sought review of a judgment from the District Court of Santa Fe County (New Mexico), which affirmed the orders of appellee, the New Mexico State Corporation Commission, denying appellant's application for a certificate of public convenience and necessity and granting the application of intervenor, an oil transport competitor.


OVERVIEW: Appellant contended that the Commission's denial of its application was not supported by substantial evidence, was arbitrary, was domestically biased against appellant in violation of 42 U.S.C.S. §§ 1981, 1983, and that the Commission erred in assessing costs against appellant. The court agreed in part. The Commission's finding that intervenor provided sufficient evidence of public need for its services and that appellant did not was improper. Public need was a fact, not the exclusive property of an applicant. Accordingly, appellant was deprived of substantial evidence necessary to support its application. Similarly, the Commission's failure to consider the consolidated record on public need was arbitrary and constituted an abuse of discretion. The civil rights claims were not preserved for review. The record supported the Commission's finding that there was a public need and necessity for the services to be rendered by appellant and intervenor. Therefore, on remand the Commission was directed to make a comparative review of the whole record. N.M. State Corp. Comm'n. R. P. 64 required appellant to pay appellate record preparation costs.


OUTCOME: The court reversed that part of the order denying appellant's application for a certificate of public convenience and necessity and granting the application of intervenor, affirmed that part denying appellant's civil rights claims, and remanded with instructions to the Commission to consider the consolidated record in making its determination.

 

86 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Hydro Conduit Corp. v. Kemble


No. 18446


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


110 N.M. 173; 1990-NMSC-061; 793 P.2d 855; 1990 N.M. LEXIS 184



June 19, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: June 19, 1990, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of Santa Fe County; Patricio M. Serna, District Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sub-contractor provided materials for a public works project. The contractor defrauded appellees governmental entities and became defunct without paying the sub-contractor. The sub-contractor sought recovery from the governmental entities for unjust enrichment. The District Court of Santa Fe County (New Mexico) dismissed the complaint as barred by sovereign immunity under N.M. Stat. Ann. § 37-1-23. The sub-contractor sought review.


OVERVIEW: The sub-contractor argued that a claim for unjust enrichment was not a claim based on contract that was barred by the immunity provisions of § 37-1-23. The sub-contractor argued that liability for unjust enrichment was fundamentally different from liability grounded in either tort or contract and that unjust enrichment provided a third, analytically distinct basis for liability, which fell outside the § 37-1-23 grant of immunity to claims based on contract. The court rejected this argument and affirmed the ruling and reasoning of the district court. The court found that § 37-1-23 was intended to reinstate sovereign immunity to actions based on contract. The court found that an action brought on the theory of unjust enrichment implied an obligation where, on the basis of justice and equity, the law imposed a contractual relationship between parties, regardless of their assent thereto. The court held that, even though an action for unjust enrichment was not based on contract in a strict theoretical sense, it was so closely related to an action that was based on contract that the provisions of § 37-1-23 should be construed to extend immunity to such a claim.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order that dismissed the complaint.

State v. Pierce


No. 18151


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


110 N.M. 76; 1990-NMSC-049; 792 P.2d 408; 1990 N.M. LEXIS 567



May 17, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Amended.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of Bernalillo County; W. John Brennan, District Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the district court of Bernalillo County (New Mexico), which convicted him of first degree murder, three counts of first degree criminal sexual penetration of a minor (CSPM), one count of third degree criminal sexual contact of a minor (CSCM), two counts of fourth degree child abuse, and 14 counts of child abuse resulting in death or great bodily harm.


OVERVIEW: Defendant lived with the mother and her two children. The mother left the children in defendant's care when she attended school. The second day of school, defendant phoned her and stated that her son had broken his arm and was unconscious. The child died several hours later. Medical evidence showed that the child had been injured over 90 percent of his body and that there had been three separate penetrations of the child's anus. Defendant was charged with first-degree murder, three counts of CSPM, two counts of CSCM, 16 counts of child abuse resulting in death, and four counts of child abuse not resulting in death. Defendant was acquitted on one charge of CSCM and four charges of child abuse, and was found guilty of the remaining counts. The court affirmed in part and reversed in part. The court held that the evidence supported only one of the two charges against defendant of child abuse not resulting in death and only one charge of child abuse resulting in death. These offenses merged into the greater offense of first-degree murder. Both the Fifth Amendment and N.M. Const. art. II, § 15 precluded the imposition of multiple punishments for one offense.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions of first-degree murder, three counts of CSPM, and one count of CSCM and reversed the convictions and sentences of child abuse resulting in death or great bodily harm as well as the two convictions and sentences of child abuse not resulting in death or great bodily harm.

Maples v. State


No. 18404


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


110 N.M. 34; 1990-NMSC-042; 791 P.2d 788; 1990 N.M. LEXIS 271



April 26, 1990, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Original Proceeding on Certiorari; Appeal from Workers' Compensation Division.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Certiorari was granted to petitioner claimant who sought to challenge a decision from the Workers' Compensation Division (New Mexico), which determined that the claimant was permanently and totally disabled. No lump sum payment was granted, but the state was to continue to pay her medical bills. Her disability payment was unchanged.


OVERVIEW: The claimant argued that she was barred from appeal because she did not receive notice of the decision until 35 days after the final order was filed, and five days too late for her to appeal. The court held that the claimant's counsel was aware of the ruling of the court, but not the exact date of the filing of the order. The claimant's counsel received notice of the court's ruling in October, and notice of the denial of attorney fees orally from the bench. After receiving notice of the court's ruling on the merits, counsel was not required to wait until the order was filed before he filed his appeal. Under N.M. R. App. P. 12-201(A) (1986), counsel could have immediately filed an appeal, pending the filing of the court's decision. Further, the court noted that while Rule 12-601 allowed appeals from workers' compensation decisions within 30 days from the filing, N.M. Stat. Ann. § 52-5-8(A) (1978) allowed such appeals within 30 days from mailing. Because the rule and the statute involved procedural matters, and rules adopted by the state supreme court governed over an inconsistent statute, N.M. R. App. P. 12-601 (1986) governed over N.M. Stat. Ann. § 52-5-8(A) (1978).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the Workers' Compensation Division. The claimant's counsel had notice of the court's ruling on the merits prior to the filing of the court's order, and counsel could have filed his appeal pending the filing of the order.

State v. Henderson


No. 17638


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


109 N.M. 655; 1990-NMSC-030; 789 P.2d 603; 1990 N.M. LEXIS 100



March 27, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Amended


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF BERNALILLO COUNTY, Albert S. "Pat" Murdoch, District Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the District Court of Bernalillo County (New Mexico), which convicted him of first-degree murder, criminal sexual penetration, kidnapping, aggravated burglary and larceny, the jury sentencing him to death for the first-degree murder of an 89-year-old widow.


OVERVIEW: A jury found defendant guilty of first-degree murder, criminal sexual penetration, kidnapping, aggravated burglary and larceny. The victim was an 89-year-old widow. The jury, in sentencing defendant to death for first-degree murder, considered three aggravating circumstances. The court found no merit in defendant's attack on his convictions. However, the court reversed the death sentence and remanded the case for resentencing on the first-degree murder conviction because the trial court erred in rejecting defendant's proffered jury instruction to the effect that a person sentenced to life imprisonment would be eligible for parole in 30 years, and in allowing the jury to consider murder during the commission of a kidnapping as an aggravating circumstance. The option of prior sentencing on noncapital offenses was a valid option available to a defendant who requests such sentencing.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's death sentence and remanded the case to the trial court for resentencing, but otherwise affirmed defendant's convictions for first-degree murder, criminal sexual penetration, kidnapping, aggravated burglary and larceny, which involved an 89-year-old widow.

Gonzales v. N.M. Educ. Ret. Bd.


No. 18114


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


109 N.M. 592; 1990-NMSC-024; 788 P.2d 348; 1990 N.M. LEXIS 77



February 23, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied March 29, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF SANTA FE COUNTY, Roger L. Copple, District Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner injured worker sought review of an order of mandamus from the District Court of Santa Fe County (New Mexico), which denied retroactive disability benefits. Respondents, Educational Retirement Board (ERB) and director, cross-appealed a declaration that a regulation was unconstitutional and awarding benefits and attorney fees.


OVERVIEW: The injured worker sought disability benefits after she was injured in an accident. She appealed from an order of mandamus which denied retroactive disability benefits to the date of the accident. Respondents cross-appealed the declaration that a regulation was unconstitutional, and an award of benefits and attorney fees. On appeal, the court reversed in part and affirmed in part. The ERB had the authority by regulation to set out an application process in order to determine disability. It did not have the statutory power to create unreasonable or irrelevant requirements within the application process, before it considers the application. The ERB did not have the authority to deny a hearing to a claimed disabled party simply because she maintained an interest in a contract without more. Attorney's fees and prejudgment interest were not appropriate.


OUTCOME: An order of the lower court in a disability benefits case involving the injured worker and respondent was affirmed in part and reversed in part.

Richardson v. Carnegie Library Rest., Inc.


No. 17432


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


107 N.M. 688; 1988-NMSC-084; 763 P.2d 1153; 1988 N.M. LEXIS 295; 78 A.L.R.4th 513



October 18, 1988 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearings Denied November 21, 1988.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff personal representative of the estate of the deceased appealed from a judgment of the court of appeals (New Mexico), which upheld the trial court's determination that granted summary judgment to defendant corporation, entered a default judgment against another defendant corporation, and found that plaintiff's recovery of damages was limited under the Dramshop Act, N.M. Stat. Ann. § 41-11-1 (1978) (Repl. Pamp. 1986).


OVERVIEW: The personal representative of the deceased challenged the grant of summary judgment to the owner of the dump truck, and attacked the cap on liability under the dramshop act as unconstitutional. The court concluded that the limitation of a full tort recovery implicated a substantial and important individual interest and invoked an intermediate standard of review. The court held that the three tacit classifications in the dramshop act effected a substantial injustice in the case. The classifications infringed on an individual's important interest to be compensated fully for his injuries, especially when they were a result of no fault of his own. The court found that the court of appeals erred in its equal protection analysis of the damage limitation. The court determined that plaintiff had presented a prima facie showing of an arbitrary and unreasonable denial of equal protection and of a restriction on a plaintiff's right of access to the courts. On the other hand, the bar owner completely failed to carry its burden of demonstrating that any substantial interest of the state was furthered by the legislation.


OUTCOME: The cap on damages mandated by the Dramshop Act did not withstand heightened scrutiny, and the court held that it was constitutionally invalid as violative of the equal protection clause. The court did not disturb the summary judgment entered by the trial court in favor of the dump truck owner, but the case was remanded for entry of judgment in the amount of $ 250,000 against the bar.

Waisner v. Jones


No. 17503


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


107 N.M. 260; 1988-NMSC-049; 755 P.2d 598; 1988 N.M. LEXIS 166; 6 U.C.C. Rep. Serv. 2d (Callaghan) 1374



June 7, 1988 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: June 7, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: ORIGINAL PROCEEDING ON CERTIORARI, Robert M. Doughty, II, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: The jury verdict on the liability of repossessor and creditor is reversed and the case remanded to the trial court to determine Waisner's actual damages.

IT IS SO ORDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner debtor sought review of a judgment from the court of appeals (New Mexico), which affirmed a jury verdict in favor of respondents, creditor and repossessor, in the debtor's action for unlawful repossession and retention of her vehicle.


OVERVIEW: The debtor filed an action against the creditor and the repossessor for the unlawful repossession of her vehicle. The appellate court affirmed a jury verdict for the creditor and the repossessor on the issue of liability. On appeal, the court reversed the appellate court's judgment and the jury verdict and remanded the case to the trial court for a determination of the debtor's actual damages. The court found that the jury instructions were insufficient because the trial court did not instruct the jury that the repossessor was not permitted to be assisted by law enforcement officials in a self-help repossession in order to prevent a breach of the peace. The court determined that the repossession of the debtor's vehicle was wrongful as a matter of law because a security police sergeant accompanied the repossessor. The court concluded that the introduction of law enforcement personnel into a self-help repossession transcended the permissible extrajudicial remedy under N.M. Stat. Ann. § 55-9-503 (Repl. Pamp. 1987). The court further concluded that the mere presence of a law enforcement official during a self-help repossession was proscribed under the Fifth or Fourteenth Amendments.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the appellate court's judgment and the jury verdict in favor of the repossessor and the creditor as to liability. The court remanded the debtor's action for unlawful repossession and retention of her vehicle to the trial court for a determination of her actual damages.

Southwest Cmty. Health Servs. v. Smith


No. 16543


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


107 N.M. 196; 1988-NMSC-035; 755 P.2d 40; 1988 N.M. LEXIS 133



May 10, 1988 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied June 7, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: Original Prohibition Proceeding


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a medical malpractice action, respondent judge ordered petitioner hospital to produce a credentialing file because N.M. Stat. Ann. § 41-9-5 of the Review Organization Immunity Act (ROIA), N.M. Stat. Ann. §§ 41-9-1 to -7, did not apply or the discovery rules overrode the statute. The hospital sought a writ of prohibition or superintending control. The court issued a preliminary writ and asked for briefs on the constitutionality of § 41-9-5.


OVERVIEW: The real parties in interest brought medical malpractice actions against the hospital and a physician. In response to a motion to compel production of documents, the hospital argued that a credentialing file maintained on the physician was confidential under § 41-9-5. Following in camera inspection, the judge ordered production of the requested documents either because the statute was not applicable to the credentialing file or because the rules of discovery or evidence overrode the statute. Finding that the record was insufficient to review ROIA's applicability to the credentials file, the state supreme court focused on whether § 41-9-5 usurped the court's constitutional power to regulate all pleading, practice, and procedure affecting the judicial branch. While § 41-9-5 encroached upon the court's power by withholding relevant and admissible evidence from discovery, it did not go so far as to create an evidentiary privilege in violation of the court's superintending control over all inferior courts under N.M. Const. art. VI, § 3. However, the court undertook its constitutional responsibility to promulgate the requisite procedures for § 41-9-5 to immunize evidence from discovery.


OUTCOME: The court quashed the alternative writ previously issued and remanded with instructions for the trial court to determine whether the peer review immunity statute was applicable to the hospital's credentialing file and, if so, to proceed in a manner consistent with the court's opinion.

Meyer v. Jones


No. 16640


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


106 N.M. 708; 1988-NMSC-011; 749 P.2d 93; 1988 N.M. LEXIS 65



February 2, 1988 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied February 18, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF BERNALILLO COUNTY, Gerard Thomson, District Judge



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the district court is reversed and the order of the metropolitan municipal court is reinstated.

IT IS SO ORDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant judge sought review of a judgment of the District Court of Bernalillo County (New Mexico) that granted appellee motorist's petition for a writ of mandamus to prohibit the judge from denying the motorist a trial by jury on a charge of a first offense of driving while under the influence of an intoxicating liquor.


OVERVIEW: The motorist was charged with a first offense of driving while under the influence of an intoxicating liquor. He was brought to trial in the municipal court before the judge, who denied the motorist's request for a jury trial. The motorist petitioned the district court for a writ of mandamus to prevent the judge from denying him a jury trial. The district court granted the petition, and the judge appealed. The court reversed the district court and reinstated the order of the municipal court. The legislature's requirement that magistrate judges in metropolitan court be attorneys and magistrates elsewhere throughout the state did not have to meet that qualification, the disallowance of juries in metropolitan courts was not arbitrary, unreasonable nor unrelated to a legitimate legislative purpose. All persons within the county were treated equally, and the classification could be justified on grounds of judicial economy.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the district court and reinstated the order of the municipal court.

 

97 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Casuse v. City of Gallup


No. 17079


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


106 N.M. 571; 1987-NMSC-112; 746 P.2d 1103; 1987 N.M. LEXIS 3810



November 30, 1987 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied December 28, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: Certification from United States District Court, Howard C. Bratton, Senior Judge U.S. District Court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: This case came upon certification from the United States District Court in Albuquerque, New Mexico. Plaintiffs alleged that defendant, the City of Gallup, violated a provision of New Mexico's municipal code, N.M. Stat. Ann. § 3-12-1.1 (Supp. 1987). The issue for review was whether the at-large election charter provisions of the City, a home rule municipality, were invalidated by § 3-12-1.1.


OVERVIEW: The City argued that its home rule charter was not affected by the New Mexico Legislature's enactment of § 3-12-1.1. The City asserted that § 3-12-1.1 was not a general law because it did not expressly deny the right of municipalities to establish the manner in which city councilors were elected, thus, it did not invalidate the City's at-large election charter. The court found that § 3-12-1.1 applied to all municipalities with populations over 10,000. Therefore, § 3-12-1.1, which required city councilors to reside in single-member districts, was a general law. As such, § 3-12-1.1 limited home-rule if it also expressly denied municipalities the authority to legislate similar matters, as required by N.M. Const. art. X, § 6(D). The court concluded that N.M. Stat. Ann. § 3-12-1.1 (Supp. 1987) sufficiently expressed the intent of the legislature to mandate that all municipalities with a population over 10,000 require their candidates for city council to reside in and be elected from single-member districts. Therefore § 3-12-1.1 invalidated the City's home rule election charter that allowed at-large elections for city councilors.


OUTCOME: The court concluded that the provision of New Mexico's municipal code invalidated the City's home rule election charter.

 

98 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Silva v. State


No. 16798


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


106 N.M. 472; 1987-NMSC-107; 745 P.2d 380; 1987 N.M. LEXIS 3784



November 3, 1987 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: November 3, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: ORIGINAL PROCEEDING ON CERTIORARI, Mayo T. Boucher, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, decedent's family, appealed a judgment from the Court of Appeals, New Mexico, which affirmed the ruling that the decedent's family was not entitled to partial summary judgment of liability and affirmed the dismissal of a direct action under the Tort Claims Act, N.M. Stat. Ann. §§ 41-4-1 to -29, against defendants, State, the Corrections and Criminal Rehabilitation Department of the State of New Mexico, and the Secretary of Corrections.


OVERVIEW: The decedent's family sought damages for a wrongful death claim due to the decedent's suicide while in custody of the Department. The decedent's family alleged partial summary judgment should have been granted on the grounds of claim or issue preclusion that arose out of a prior action. The court determined that the ultimate fact issue concerned whether the failure of the Department to exercise ordinary care was the proximate cause of the decedent's death. The court concluded that the ultimate fact issue had not been decided in the prior case, so the use of collateral estoppel was not appropriate. However, the court found that the State and the Department could be liable under the Tort Claims Act under traditional concepts of respondeat superior and that the lower court erred in concluding that certain statutory waivers of immunity were inapplicable as a matter of law to the acts or omission of the Secretary of Corrections regarding the decedent's death. The court concluded that the trier of fact had to determine whether the Secretary of Corrections exercised ordinary care in the discharge of duties proximately related to the decedent's death.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the lower court with respect to the ruling that the decedent's family was not entitled to partial summary judgment of liability. The court reversed the judgment with respect to the dismissal of a direct action under the Tort Claims Act against the State, the Department, and the Secretary of Corrections. The court remanded the case for further proceedings.

 

99 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State v. Cheadle


No. 16919


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


106 N.M. 391; 1987-NMSC-100; 744 P.2d 166; 1987 N.M. LEXIS 3762



October 7, 1987 


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF BERNALILLO COUNTY, Philip R. Ashby, District Judge


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was sentenced to various terms for three non-capital offenses and to death for murder with the sentences to run concurrently. The District Court of Bernalillo County (New Mexico) granted defendant's motion to set aside the death penalty and sentenced defendant to life imprisonment to run concurrently with the prior sentences. The State appealed from the denial of its motion for reconsideration of the concurrent life sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the State had no right to appeal because N.M. Stat. Ann. § 33-3-3(C) prohibited appeals when the Double Jeopardy Clause of the United States Constitution or N.M. Const. art. VI, § 2 prohibited further prosecution. The sentencing court determined that it had no authority to impose a sentence greater than the originally imposed sentence and thus could not exercise its discretion in the matter. The court held that the sentencing court properly declined to exercise its discretion to reconsider the sentence and properly denied the State's motion for reconsideration. N.M. Stat. Ann. § 39-3-3(C) precluded an appeal by the State when the constitutional guarantee against double jeopardy prohibited further prosecution. Thus, the issue was not whether the State was an aggrieved party with a right to appeal under § 39-3-3(B). Even if the State was an aggrieved party with a right to appeal, the sentencing court was prohibited from resentencing defendant so that his life estate ran consecutively with his other sentences. There was no statute that permitted the State to appeal from the sentence and thus defendant had an expectation of finality in his original sentencing.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the sentencing court that denied the State's motion for reconsideration.

 

100 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State v. Hovey


No. 16576


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


106 N.M. 300; 1987-NMSC-080; 742 P.2d 512; 1987 N.M. LEXIS 3712



September 2, 1987 


PRIOR HISTORY:  APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF BERNALILLO COUNTY, Richard Blackhurst, District Judge. 



DISPOSITION: We AFFIRM. defendant's conviction.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a conviction from the District Court of Bernalillo County (New Mexico), which was for first-degree murder.


OVERVIEW: A jury convicted defendant of first-degree murder. On appeal, the court affirmed the conviction. The court found that defendant waived any impediment to a grand jury indictment because he failed to request a stay during the pendency of his appeal of a transfer order from children's court. The court concluded that defendant failed to present any evidence that televising portions of the proceedings prejudiced the presentation of his testimony and that he also failed to show that pre-trial media coverage of the case warranted a change of venue. The court also concluded that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in limiting the number of entries from defendant's diaries that could be read to the jury and explained by defendant. The court determined that a comment during the State's opening argument about raw test data that had not been furnished to defendant did not require a mistrial and that his motion for a mistrial on the issue of jury taint was untimely. The court found that the trial court properly exercised its discretion in limiting the testimony of a defense witness who was inadvertently present in the courtroom during the testimony of another defense witness.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's first-degree murder conviction.

 

101 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Madrid v. Univ. of Cal.


No. 16172


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


105 N.M. 715; 1987-NMSC-022; 737 P.2d 74; 1987 N.M. LEXIS 3830



March 18, 1987 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied May 29, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: ORIGINAL PROCEEDING ON CERTIORARI, Lorenzo F. Garcia, District Judge


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner employee requested a rehearing following the judgment of the court of appeals (New Mexico), which affirmed the trial court's dismissal of the employee's workmen's compensation action. The trial court had excluded the testimony of the employee's psychologist as to her mental instability on the basis that it was not considered expert medical testimony under N.M. Stat. Ann. § 52-1-28(B) (1978).


OVERVIEW: The trial court dismissed the employee's workmen's compensation action. The trial court had found that her psychologist's testimony concerning her mental condition had to be excluded because it was not considered expert medical testimony under § 52-1-28(B). The court of appeals affirmed. On appeal, the court reversed. The court held that it was improper to exclude the testimony of the psychologist. The phrase "expert medical testimony," as used in § 52-1-28(B) described the kind of testimony that was required. It did not describe the witness's educational or licensing requirements. Therefore, the fact that psychologists were not licensed to practice medicine in New Mexico was an insufficient basis for the exclusion of their testimony under § 52-1-28(B). Also, because § 52-1-28(B) concerned an evidentiary matter, it should have been read in pari materia with N.M. R. Evid. 11-702 (1986), which indisputably recognized that an expert witness could be qualified on foundations other than licensure. Further, there was no legislative intent to limit the qualification of expert testimony to licensed physicians.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the dismissal of the employee's workmen's compensation action. On remand, the court instructed the district court to determine, considering the testimony of the clinical psychologist, whether the employee established her claim.

 

102 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Dupper v. Liberty Mut. Ins. Co.


No. 16330


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


105 N.M. 503; 1987-NMSC-007; 734 P.2d 743; 1987 N.M. LEXIS 3520



February 3, 1987 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied March 12, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: ORIGINAL PROCEEDINGS ON CERTIORARI, Rebecca Sitterly, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the lower court is AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner employee appealed a decision of the Court of Appeals (New Mexico), which ruled that the employee failed to establish that her injury that happened while walking to her car after work was caused by defendant employer's negligence.


OVERVIEW: After having completed her shift at work, the employee signed out for the day, and was on her way to the employee parking lot when she tripped over a "pop-up" sprinkler head that had failed to retract after use. The employee sought compensation from the employer and defendant insurer. The insurer denied compensation for her injury on the ground that the accident occurred after she had left her duties of employment, thereby precluding her from recovery under the "going-and-coming" rule. The trial court ruled that the employee failed to establish that her injury was caused by the employer's negligence but awarded compensation by purporting to adopt the "premises" rule. The employee appealed, and the court affirmed holding that the employee, while on the employer's premises coming to or going from the actual workplace was in a place where the employee was reasonably expected to be, and that she was engaged in a necessary incident of employment. The court concluded that because it adopted the premises rule that allowed compensation under the Workmen's Compensation Act, it was unnecessary to respond to the employee's appeal of the trial court's refusal to find the employer negligent.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment that the employee failed to establish that her injury that happened while walking to her car after work was caused by defendant employer's negligence.

 

103 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Kennedy v. Yates Petro. Corp.


No. 15873


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


104 N.M. 596; 1986-NMSC-064; 725 P.2d 572; 1986 N.M. LEXIS 3033



September 10, 1986 


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF EDDY COUNTY, John B. Walker, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: In light of the foregoing, the judgment of the district court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowners appealed a judgment from the District Court of Eddy County (New Mexico) that, on remand and after consolidating the landowners' trespass action with defendant gas company's condemnation petition, determined that the use of the company's natural gas pipeline was a public use as required for condemnation under the Eminent Domain Code, N.M. Stat. Ann. § 42A-1-22 (Repl. Pamp. 1981).


OVERVIEW: In the prior action, the court instructed the trial court to conduct an evidentiary hearing to determine whether the company's pipeline satisfied the court's case law criteria for establishing a real and substantial relation to the public use for condemnation purposes. The company showed that the pipeline was required by rules promulgated a state agency and that the state derived substantial tax revenues from the company's and other utilities' operations. On appeal, the court ruled that the trial court properly found that the company's pipeline bore a real and substantial relation to the public use as required by statute and the court's case law. The gas from the pipeline flowed into the stream of commerce and was essential to the efficient production of oil. The court also ruled that the pipeline was a gathering line and was exempt from regulations governing common carrier, under N.M. Stat. Ann. § 70-3-3 (Cum. Supp. 1985). Finally, the court ruled that N.M. Stat. Ann. § 70-3-5 (Cum. Supp. 1985) did not unconstitutionally create a private right of condemnation in a private entity when the entity showed its use was consistent with a public purpose. The company carried that burden.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

104 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Delgadillo v. City of Socorro


No. 15,867


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


104 N.M. 476; 1986-NMSC-054; 723 P.2d 245; 1986 N.M. LEXIS 3007



August 12, 1986 


PRIOR HISTORY:  APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF SOCORRO COUNTY, Edmund H. Kase, III, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: IT IS SO ORDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Third-party plaintiff city appealed from the decision of the District Court of Socorro County (New Mexico), which granted summary judgment to third-party defendant construction company on the city's claim seeking reimbursement for indemnity, negligence, and breach of warranty.


OVERVIEW: The construction company installed new gas lines and routed existing lines for the city. After a gas explosion occurred, some homeowners filed suit against the city and the city filed a third party complaint against the company seeking reimbursement for indemnity and negligence and added a claim for breach of warranty. The lower court granted the company summary judgment and the court affirmed. The court found that the city's claim was barred under the statute of limitations imposed by N.M. Stat. Ann. §37-1-27 (1978). The court determined that the installation of gas lines was a physical improvement for real property and thus the statute concerning the liability of architects and contractors for injuries caused by negligent designs or constructions was applicable. The court concluded that the city's cause of action did not accrue within the required ten year period after the completion of the project and that summary judgment had been properly granted.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment to the construction company because the city's claim for reimbursement was barred by the statute of limitations.

 

105 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State v. Aqui


No. 16313


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


104 N.M. 345; 1986-NMSC-048; 721 P.2d 771; 1986 N.M. LEXIS 2956; 25 N.M. St. B. Bull. 662



June 24, 1986 



DISPOSITION:  Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State sought review by writ of certiorari of a decision from the Court of Appeals (New Mexico), mandating the awarding of good time credits against sentence to defendants for the period of their confinement in the county detention center prior to trial, judgment, and sentencing.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were arrested on criminal charges and detained prior to trial when they failed to make bail. The district court denied defendants' motions for good time credits on the grounds that it lacked statutory authority to grant them. The court of appeals held that the granting of good time credits for presentence confinement was constitutionally required. On further appeal, the court held that the granting of good time credits was an administrative matter for the Corrections Department or the county sheriff or jail administrator, and that N.M. R. Crim. P. 57.1 did not give the district court jurisdiction to entertain a motion for good time credits. The statutory scheme under which defendants were denied good time credits for the periods of their presentence confinement did not offend the constitutional guarantees of equal protection and due process of law because there was a rational justification for declining to award good time credits for presentence confinement under the circumstances. The court held that the district court did not have jurisdiction under Rule 57.1(a) to correct or modify sentences by awarding good time credits for periods spent in presentence confinement.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the court of appeals' decision and reinstated the district court's orders dismissing defendants' motions for good time credits.

 

106 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State v. Ball


No. 15755


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


104 N.M. 176; 1986-NMSC-030; 718 P.2d 686; 1986 N.M. LEXIS 2899



April 24, 1986 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: April 24, 1986


PRIOR HISTORY: ORIGINAL PROCEEDING ON CERTIORARI, Rozier E. Sanchez, District Judge



DISPOSITION: We reverse the orders in all the cases denying defendants the right of an appeal de novo in district court, and remand for further proceedings.

IT IS SO ORDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After defendants entered pleas of guilty or nolo contendere to misdemeanor charges, they appealed and sought a trial de novo. The Court of Appeals (New Mexico) held that N.M. Stat. Ann. § 34-8A-6(C) (Pamp. 1981) was unconstitutional because it limited appeals to "aggrieved" defendants and N.M. Const. art. VI, § 27, guaranteed appeals to defendants who were not aggrieved as well, and the state sought review of the appellate court's decision.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were found guilty after either entering pleas of guilty or nolo contendere and appealed seeking a trial de novo. The trial court dismissed their appeals and the appellate court reversed and found that N.M. Stat. Ann. § 34-8A-6(C) (Pamp. 1981) was unconstitutional because it limited the right to appeals to aggrieved defendants. On appeal, the court reversed and held that the constitutional right of appeal extended only to persons aggrieved by judgments of inferior courts and that defendants were not aggrieved because they voluntarily plead guilty or nolo contendere. The court overruled City of Albuquerque v. Sanchez, 466 P.2d 118 (N.M. Ct. App. 1970), because it defined the constitutional right to appeal too broadly and failed to limit the right to appeal de novo to "aggrieved" persons, overruled State v. Bazan, 641 P.2d 1078 (N.M. Ct. App. 1982), to the extent it suggested that the constitutional right to appeal could be modified by "legislative therapy," and overruled Douthitt v. Bailey, 99 P. 342 (1908), to the extent that it suggested that a defendant who plead guilty before an inferior court was aggrieved and enjoyed the right to appeal for a trial de novo.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the appellate court's decision and remanded the case to it with instructions to reinstate the orders of the trial court dismissing defendants' appeals.

 

107 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Pruey v. Dep't of Alcoholic Beverage Control


No. 16033


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


104 N.M. 10; 1986-NMSC-018; 715 P.2d 458; 1986 N.M. LEXIS 2849



March 10, 1986 


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF SANTA FE COUNTY, Tony Scarborough, District Judge



DISPOSITION: We find that based upon the challenges raised in this case, Section 60-7A-1 does not violate appellants' constitutional rights under either U.S. Const. amend. XIV, § 1 and N.M. Const. art. II, § 18 or U.S. Const. amend. I and N.M. Const. art. II, § 11. It is a proper exercise of legislative power. This opinion is limited to a determination of the issue of constitutionality of Section 60-7A-1. We affirm the trial court.

IT IS SO ORDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant retailers sought review of a judgment of the District Court of Santa Fe County (New Mexico), which denied the retailers' petition for declaratory and injunctive relief against appellees, Department of Alcoholic Beverage Control, its director, cities, and counties.


OVERVIEW: The retailers were holders of valid and unexpired licenses authorizing them to sell and serve alcoholic beverages. They asked the trial court to declare void the local option elections held in local option districts and to enjoin the enforcement of any prohibition against the sales of alcoholic beverages by appellants on Sunday. The trial court denied relief and dismissed the action. Appellants sought review and argued that N.M. Stat. Ann. § 60-7A-1 (Cum. Supp. 1985) was unconstitutional because it violated their right to equal protection and furthered the establishment of religion. The court held that the statute did not violate equal protection because the legislature provided a rational basis for the prohibition of sales of alcoholic beverages on Sunday, namely, to protect the public health, safety, and morals of every community in the state. The court held that the law did not further religion. The court held that secular purposes had been advanced to make Sunday a day of rest and recreation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

State v. Compton


No. 15218


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


104 N.M. 683; 1986-NMSC-010; 726 P.2d 837; 1986 N.M. LEXIS 2934



February 17, 1986 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Stay Granted March 5, 1986. Stay Dissolved October 22, 1986.
Writ of certiorari denied Compton v. New Mexico, 479 U.S. 890, 93 L. Ed. 2d 265, 107 S. Ct. 291, 1986 U.S. LEXIS 4334, 55 U.S.L.W. 3258 (1986)
Writ of certiorari granted Compton v. Lytle, 65 P.3d 1094, 2003 N.M. LEXIS 65 (N.M., 2003)
Post-conviction relief denied at Compton v. Lytle, 2003 NMSC 31, 2003 N.M. LEXIS 231 (N.M., 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF BERNALILLO COUNTY, A. JOSEPH ALARID, District Judge



DISPOSITION: For the foregoing reasons, we determine that the convictions of Compton and the sentence of death imposed upon him for the murder of Officer Cline should be affirmed.

IT IS SO ORDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The District Court of Bernalillo County (New Mexico) convicted defendant of capital murder and aggravated assault. Defendant was sentenced to death for the murder and 18 months imprisonment for the aggravated assault. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: During an incident at a hotel, defendant shot and killed a police officer. Defendant was convicted of capital murder and aggravated assault. On appeal, the court affirmed the convictions and the sentence of death. The court held that the trial court did err in ruling that defendant's wife had waived the husband-wife privilege when she made a sworn statement to police shortly after the shooting. However, the court concluded that the admission of the wife's statement was harmless error because it could only have had an insignificant effect on the verdict, in light of the other evidence that was introduced, which showed defendant's awareness that a police officer was on the premises. The court rejected defendant's contentions of prosecutorial misconduct in the sentencing phase. The court found that the effect of the prosecutor's comments was insignificant when viewed in context. Moreover, the court noted that one of the proper lines of argument during the sentencing phase involved the consideration of the accepted justifications for the use of the death penalty. Those justifications were retribution and deterrence. The court also found that the jury instructions were proper.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment that convicted defendant of capital murder and aggravated assault. The court also affirmed the sentence of death imposed upon defendant for the murder of the police officer.

 

109 of 795 DOCUMENTS


United Nuclear Corp. v. Allendale Mut. Ins. Co.


Nos. 15094, 15104


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


103 N.M. 480; 1985-NMSC-090; 709 P.2d 649; 1985 N.M. LEXIS 2033



October 15, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied December 5, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF SANTA FE COUNTY, Michael Francke, District Judge, Art Encinias, District Judge



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the trial court is affirmed in part and reversed in part.

IT IS SO ORDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the order of the District Court of Santa Fe County (New Mexico), which awarded plaintiff reimbursement for business interruption, property damage losses, attorney fees, prejudgment interest, and punitive damages under the insurance policy issued by defendant.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff brought suit after defendant denied coverage for business interruption and property damage losses that occurred when a dam collapsed at plaintiff's uranium mill. The policy excluded coverage for subsidence or any other earth movement. The trial court awarded judgment to plaintiff, including attorney fees, prejudgment interest, and punitive damages. The court affirmed in part, and reversed in part The trial court did not err in finding that the differential settlement that caused the collapse was not subsidence, or an earth movement, defined as a naturally occurring phenomenon. While the court adopted a preponderance of the evidence standard of proof for punitive damages, the punitive damage and attorney fee awards were erroneous since defendant's refusal to pay was based on legitimate questions regarding the amount of damages that should be paid. The compensatory damages award was within the range of evidence, and the prejudgment interest fell within trial court's discretion.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part, and reversed in part, holding that the policy did not exclude coverage, compensatory damages were within the range of evidence, and the trial court did not abuse its discretion in awarding prejudgment interest. The award of punitive damage and attorney fees was reversed since legitimate questions were raised regarding damages.

Las Cruses TV Cable v. N.M. State Corp. Comm'n (In re Generic Investigation into Cable TV Servs.)


No. 15620


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


103 N.M. 345; 1985-NMSC-087; 707 P.2d 1155; 1985 N.M. LEXIS 2003



October 8, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY: REMOVAL FROM CORPORATION COMMISSION



DISPOSITION: The Commission's order is vacated, however, because the Certification Act, upon which it was based in part, is no longer applicable. The case is remanded to the Commission for hearings and a new order to be made pursuant to the Telecommunications Act.

IT IS SO ORDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant communications companies sought review of a decision of appellee state corporation commission to regulate appellants' digital data transmission services.


OVERVIEW: This case was before the court on removal from appellee state corporation commission. The proceeding before appellee commission was initiated by appellant communications companies to determine whether cable television systems within the State of New Mexico were providing public utility telephone service, or anticipating providing such service, without the requisite authority from appellee. Appellee determined that appellants were offering public telephone services that fell within appellee's jurisdiction. In its decision and order, appellee ordered appellants to cease and desist until further order and required that any New Mexico cable television company apply for and be granted a Certificate of Public Convenience and Necessity before performing any construction for furnishing public telephone service and before furnishing any public telephone service to any customer. The issue presented on appeal was whether appellee had authority to regulate the cable companies' digital data transmission services. The court concluded that intrastate digital data transmission services may properly be subject to regulation by appellee commission.


OUTCOME: The Commission's order was vacated, however, because the Certification Act, upon which it was based in part, was no longer applicable. The case was remanded to the Commission for hearings and a new order to be made pursuant to the Telecommunications Act.

Elliott v. N.M. Real Estate Comm'n


No. 15554


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


103 N.M. 273; 1985-NMSC-078; 705 P.2d 679; 1985 N.M. LEXIS 1988



September 3, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF BERNALILLO COUNTY, Frank H. Allen, District Judge



DISPOSITION: We affirm the decision of the district court and uphold suspension of Elliott's broker's license.

IT IS SO ORDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant broker sought review of a judgment from the District Court of Bernalillo County (New Mexico), which affirmed the suspension of his license by appellee New Mexico Real Estate Commission. He contended that the Commission lacked jurisdiction over the parties or the subject matter, and that in addition their suspension was unlawful, arbitrary, and capricious.


OVERVIEW: The broker agreed to sell an owner's interest in a New Mexico real estate contract for which he was to receive a selling fee. After the property was sold, he delayed distributing the entirety of the balance of the proceeds to the owner. The Commission found that he had commingled funds and that he should have set up a trust account to handle the proceeds. In affirming the judgment, the court held that its scope of review was governed by N.M. Stat. Ann. § 61-1-20 (1978, Repl. Pamp. 1981) of the Uniform Licensing Act, and that it could only reverse where administrative decisions were unconstitutional, were in excess of their authority or jurisdiction, were procedurally or legally defective, were unsupported by substantial evidence on the record as a whole, or were arbitrary and capricious. The court held that the Commission had jurisdiction, because the broker was acting as a real estate broker as defined in N.M. Stat. Ann. § 61-29-2(A). The court held that although he had obtained the owner's power of attorney, this did not alter his status as a broker in this transaction. The court also held that the evidence supported the Commission's decision.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment and upheld the broker's suspension by the Commission.

State ex rel. Harkleroad v. N.M. State Police Bd.


No. 15720


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


103 N.M. 270; 1985-NMSC-076; 705 P.2d 676; 1985 N.M. LEXIS 1985



August 22, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF SANTA FE COUNTY, Bruce E. Kaufman, District Judge



DISPOSITION: For the above reasons, we reverse the decision of the district court, and reinstate the decision of the Board.

IT IS SO ORDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a police board, a police department, and a police chief, challenged a judgment of the District Court of Santa Fe County (New Mexico), which reversed a decision of the board that sustained appellee employee's suspension.


OVERVIEW: The employee, a police officer, stated to the police chief that the employee was thinking about running for the office of governor. The employee did not resign but continued to engage in political activity. The police chief asked the employee to refrain from being a candidate for office. The employee disregarded the order and was suspended by the board. The trial court reversed the order. The court reversed the trial court's judgment and reinstated the board's decision, suspending the employee. The employee was engaged in political activity in violation of N.M. State Police Dept. R. 134.0 (1982). The State and the police department had an imperative interest in prohibiting its police officers from running for an elective public office. As conservators of the peace, state police officers had to enforce the laws in an impartial and uniform manner. There could be no situations where there could be an appearance of favoritism in dealing with the public or enforcing the laws. There could be no situation where a state policeman was linked to organized political activity or appeared to devote less than full attention to necessary duties because of political involvement.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the trial court and reinstated the board's decision, which suspended the employee.

Kern v. St. Joseph Hosp., Inc.

102 N.M. 452; 1985-NMSC-031; 697 P.2d 135; 1985 N.M. LEXIS 1941

OUTCOME: The court reversed the decisions of the lower courts because a genuine issue of material fact existed as to whether respondent health care providers fraudulently concealed medical malpractice from petitioner decedent's wife and personal representative, and remanded the matter to the trial court.

 

114 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Vallejos v. Barnhart


No. 15019


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


102 N.M. 438; 1985-NMSC-026; 697 P.2d 121; 1985 N.M. LEXIS 1946



March 19, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF BERNALILLO COUNTY, Rozier Sanchez, District Judge



DISPOSITION: We hold, therefore, that because defendants face aggregate penalties of 90 days or more, they are either entitled to jury trial under Subsection 34-8(A)-5(B)(2) because demanded, or to be scheduled for jury trial under Subsection 34-8(A)-5(B)(3) because mandated by statute. The district court is reversed and the case is remanded with directions to issue a permanent writ of prohibition in accordance with this opinion.

IT IS SO ORDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner individuals, who were charged in metropolitan court with multiple traffic violations, sought review of a decision by the District Court of Bernalillo County (New Mexico), which denied the individuals' petition for a writ of prohibition against respondents, various metropolitan court judges, to curtail bench trials and to require a jury trial in multiple offense cases for which aggregate sentences could be 180 or more days.


OVERVIEW: The individuals were charged with multiple violations, including driving under the influence of intoxicating liquor or drugs in violation of N.M. Stat. Ann. § 66-8-102 (Cum. Supp. 1980, Cum. Supp. 1981). The initial charges were for second violations under § 66-8-102, which authorized imprisonment for not less than 90 days nor more than 1 year. The State of New Mexico was later granted its motions to reduce the charges to first offense violations, which carried imprisonment terms of 30 through 90 days. In each case, the metropolitan court granted the State's motion for a bench trial and denied each individuals' request for a jury trial. On appeal, the court reversed the denial of the writ and ordered that it be issued. The court first found that each individual faced a maximum possible aggregate penalty of 180 days or more. Therefore, N.M. Stat. Ann. § 34-8A-5(B), relating to the right to a jury trial, afforded the right to a jury trial to each individual because that statute entitled each individual to a jury trial because demanded under § 34-8A-5(B)(2) or because mandated by statute under § 34-8A-5(B)(3).


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's denial of the individuals' petition, and the court remanded the action with directions to the trial court to issue a permanent writ of prohibition in accordance with the court's opinion.

 

115 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Otero v. Zouhar


No. 15457


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


102 N.M. 482; 1985-NMSC-021; 697 P.2d 482; 1985 N.M. LEXIS 1936



February 28, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied April 1, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: ORIGINAL PROCEEDINGS ON CERTIORARI



DISPOSITION: We reverse the decisions of the trial court and Court of Appeals to the extent necessary to permit the claims against Zouhar, Layne and Albuquerque Anesthesia Services, Ltd. to proceed to trial. We affirm the Court of Appeals on plaintiff's standing to raise other constitutional issues in this appeal.

IT IS SO ORDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff injured party, in a malpractice action against defendants, two physicians and a clinic, challenged a finding by the trial court and the Court of Appeals (New Mexico), that his complaint with the medical review commission (commission) was untimely filed and that he followed improper procedure in not waiting for the commission's ruling before filing suit.


OVERVIEW: The injured party intended to file a malpractice action against the two physicians and a clinic. The Superintendent of Insurance told the injured party, incorrectly, that only one of the physicians was "qualified" (having $ 100,000 in insurance coverage) pursuant to N.M. Stat. Ann. § 41-54 et seq. In reality, all defendants were "qualified." The injured party filed a complaint with the medical review commission against the one "qualified" physician and filed suit against the other two parties. Although the complaint to the medical review commission was mailed prior to the running of the statute of limitations, it was not received until later. The "qualified" physician claimed that the complaint was filed too late and that suit was filed in violation of N.M. Stat. Ann. § 41-5-15A in not waiting for the commission's ruling before filing suit. The trial court agreed, and the appeals court affirmed. However, the court reversed, finding that the date of mailing of the complaint was the controlling date. While normally the injured party should have waited for the commission's ruling, he acted appropriately under the circumstances, given that he received incorrect information.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the appellate court and allowed the injured party to proceed to trial.

 

116 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Miller & Assocs. v. Rainwater


No. 15246


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


102 N.M. 170; 1985-NMSC-001; 692 P.2d 1319; 1985 N.M. LEXIS 1915



January 3, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF SOCORRO COUNTY, Robert M. Doughty, District Judge



DISPOSITION: We hold Section 38-7-1 unconstitutional and expressly overrule all prior cases to the contrary. We therefore reverse and remand the matter to the trial court, directing that the judgment on Count I be set aside and that matter reinstated for trial.

IT IS SO ORDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant clients sought review of an order from the District Court for Socorro County (New Mexico), which, in an action brought by plaintiff law firm to recover attorney fees, directed a verdict against the clients for the full amount of the open account alleged by the law firm in the verified complaint. The district court found that the account was a duly verified open account within the meaning of N.M. Stat. Ann. § 38-7-1(1978).


OVERVIEW: The district court ruled that because the account was a duly verified open account and because the clients did not deny the account under oath in a writing filed as part of the pleadings prior to trial, the district court was obliged to direct a verdict. On review the court held that N.M. Stat. Ann. § 38-7-1 (1978) was unconstitutional and expressly overruled all prior cases to the contrary. That statute provided that accounts duly verified by the oath of the party claiming the same, and promissory notes and other instruments in writing, not barred by law, were sufficient evidence in any suit to enable a plaintiff to recover judgment for the account, unless the defendant denied the same under oath. The court noted that in light of more recent rules of civil procedure and of evidence, § 38-7-1 no longer enjoyed constitutional validity. Rules of evidence were procedural, and the New Mexico Constitution reposed the inherent power to regulate all pleading, practice, and procedure that affected the judicial branch exclusively in the New Mexico Supreme Court.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the district court's order and remanded, directing that the judgment be set aside and that the matter be reinstated for trial.

 

117 of 795 DOCUMENTS


City of Albuquerque v. State


No. 15627


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


102 N.M. 38; 1984-NMSC-113; 690 P.2d 1032; 1984 N.M. LEXIS 1757



November 19, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF SANTA FE COUNTY, LORENZO F. GARCIA, District Judge



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the trial court is affirmed.

IT IS SO ORDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants sought review of the judgment from the District Court of Santa Fe County (New Mexico), which held in favor of appellees in appellees' constitutional challenge to 1979 N.M. Laws 319.


OVERVIEW: In appellees' suit against appellants, the trial court held that 1979 N.M. Laws 319 § 1, insofar as it attempted to amend N.M. Stat. Ann. § 3-21-6 (1978), was unconstitutional as it violated N.M. Const. art. IV, § 16. Appellants sought the court's review. The court held that under art. IV, § 16, the subject of every bill had to be clearly expressed in its title, and no bill embracing more than one subject could be passed except general appropriation bills and bills for the codification or revision of the laws. However, if any subject was embraced in any act which was not expressed in its title, only so much of the act as is not so expressed was void. Further, the cardinal test for interpreting art. IV, § 16, was whether the title of the act in question gave reasonable notice of the subject matter of the body of the act. Here, the title to Ch. 319 referred to a specific act, the Community Development Act (the Act), N.M. Stat. Ann. §§ 3-6-1- (1984), which was in no way related to § 3-21-6. Further, nowhere did the title refer to § 3-21-6. Accordingly, the title to Ch. 319, § 1 violated art. IV, § 16, and was unconstitutional and void.


OUTCOME: The judgment in favor of appellees was affirmed.
