Lazo v. Bd. of County Comm'rs


No. 15420


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


102 N.M. 35; 1984-NMSC-111; 690 P.2d 1029; 1984 N.M. LEXIS 1746; 120 L.R.R.M. 3014



November 13, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF BERNALILLO COUNTY, Mayo T. Boucher, District Judge



DISPOSITION: Thus, although we are sympathetic to Lazo's plight under the circumstances as they exist in this case, Section 44-6-12 and the Union contract are clear and unambiguous. The matter should have been adjudicated in favor of the County. The district court judgment is reversed.

IT IS SO ORDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county sought review of a decision of the District Court of Bernalillo County (New Mexico), which entered judgment in favor of appellee employee in his action for breach of a collective bargaining agreement, declaratory judgment, and injunctive relief.


OVERVIEW: An employee brought an action against the county for breach of collective bargaining agreement, declaratory judgment, and injunctive relief, and he requested back pay, restoration of seniority, and reinstatement of employment. Judgment was entered in favor of the employee. In reversing the decision, the court held that the employee failed to serve the attorney general as required by N.M. Stat. Ann. § 44-6-12. The court could not interpret § 44-6-12 as requiring service upon the attorney general only when it was alleged that a statute, on its face, was unconstitutional. The court could not construe unambiguous legislation. Further, the union, acting on the employee's behalf, failed to timely deliver employee's grievance to the department head. Therefore, because step one of the grievance procedure was not followed and under the terms of the contract, that matter was ended.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment that was entered in favor of the employee in his action for breach of collective bargaining agreement, declaratory judgment, and injunctive relief.

Velasquez v. Chavez


No. 15641


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


102 N.M. 54; 1984-NMSC-109; 691 P.2d 55; 1984 N.M. LEXIS 1751



November 8, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF GUADALUPE COUNTY, Donaldo A. Martinez, District Judge



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the trial court is affirmed.

IT IS SO ORDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant candidate sought review of a judgment of the District Court of Guadalupe County, New Mexico that determined that the candidate was ineligible to seek or hold the office of Guadalupe County Commissioner for District 3 because he was not a resident of that county district.


OVERVIEW: The candidate sought his democratic party's nomination in the election for the position of Guadalupe County Commissioner for District 3. When the candidate won the democratic primary, another candidate filed an election contest alleging that the candidate was ineligible for the position because he did not reside in District 3. The trial court ruled that the candidate resided in District 2 and was not eligible to hold the county commissioner position for District 3. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's judgment. The court ruled that the candidate failed to comply with the residency requirement. The court noted that candidate should have known about the residency requirement because the candidate was required to sign an affidavit of declaration of candidacy prior to being placed on the primary ballot stating that he was a resident of the commission district for which he declared his candidacy. The court held that by requiring candidates to be residents of the district from which they sought election insured that each elected commissioner had knowledge of the problems and the needs of the district in which he sought office.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment that declared the candidate ineligible to seek or hold the county commissioner's position in a district where he did not reside.

Thompson v. Robinson


No. 15608


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


101 N.M. 703; 1984-NMSC-096; 688 P.2d 21; 1984 N.M. LEXIS 1705



September 25, 1984 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied October 2, 1984.


PRIOR HISTORY: ELECTION CONTEST IN THE BERNALILLO COUNTY DISTRICT COURT, Patricia Madrid, District Judge



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner contestee sought a writ of superintending control to review a judgment from the Bernalillo County District Court (New Mexico), which struck his name from the general election ballot as the Democratic candidate and substituted respondent contestant as the candidate.


OVERVIEW: The contestant filed a challenge to the contestee's primary victory, alleging that the contestee did not reside in the district for which he sought office. In affirming the judgment in part, the court first held that the challenge was timely filed under N.M. Stat. Ann. § 1-14-3 (1978). The court next held that a residency challenge was a proper election contest under N.M. Stat. Ann. §§ 1-14-1 and 1-14-3 (Repl. Pamp. 1984), noting that N.M. Stat. Ann. § 1-14-1 provided for contest of "the election" of a candidate, and the eligibility of the candidate determined, in the first place, the validity of his election. The court noted that the contestee was ineligible because he did not reside in the district, as required by N.M. Stat. Ann. § 2-8B-4 (Repl. Pamp. 1983). The court then noted that the 56-day limitation in N.M. Stat. Ann. § 1-8-8 of the New Mexico Election Code, N.M. Stat. Ann. §§ 1-1-1 through 1-8-64 (1978), on the appointment of a new candidate was impossible of performance in this case and totally impracticable in any case, and held that it was inconsistent with the panoply of contest rights provided in N.M. Stat. Ann. § 1-14-1 et seq.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the removal of the contestee's name form the ballot but reversed the substitution of the contestant's name.

 

121 of 795 DOCUMENTS


First Nat'l Bank v. Southwest Yacht & Marine Supply Corp.


Nos. 14961, 14974


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


101 N.M. 431; 1984-NMSC-075; 684 P.2d 517; 1984 N.M. LEXIS 1671



July 23, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF SANTA FE COUNTY, Michael Francke, District Judge



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant bank sought review of an order of the District Court of Santa Fe County (New Mexico), which granted appellee corporation's motion to dissolve the bank's writ of replevin and denied the bank's motion for partial summary judgment on its claim that an amended affidavit in replevin cured the defects in the original affidavit.


OVERVIEW: The bank filed an action against the corporation to replevy goods pledged as security for the payment of a promissory note. The trial court dissolved the affidavit in replevin. The bank filed an amended affidavit and filed a motion for partial summary judgment. The trial court ruled that the amended affidavit did not relate back to cure the defects in the original affidavit. However, it granted the bank's motion for partial summary judgment on its claim that it was not liable to the corporation for wrongful replevin. The court reversed and remanded. It held that the amended affidavit in replevin related back to the date of the original affidavit. The trial court erred in limiting damages recoverable for wrongful replevin to those set forth in N.M. Stat. Ann. § 42-8-11 (1978). Pursuant to N.M. Stat. Ann. § 42-8-19 (1978), the corporation could recover reasonable attorney fees that it incurred in the dissolution of the wrongfully issued writ of replevin. The measure of damages recoverable by the corporation for the bank's wrongful replevin was double damages for the use of the property wrongfully replevied, for the period of time from its wrongful taking to its tendered return.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order denying the bank's motion for partial summary judgment and ruling that its amended affidavit in replevin did not cure the defects in the original affidavit and remanded the cause for further proceedings.

Smith v. Love


No. 15356


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


101 N.M. 355; 1984-NMSC-061; 683 P.2d 37; 1984 N.M. LEXIS 1678



May 30, 1984 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied June 27, 1984.


PRIOR HISTORY: PROCEEDING ON SUPERINTENDING CONTROL



DISPOSITION: Petition denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner claimant sought a writ of prohibition or superintending control directing respondent, a New Mexico district court, to dismiss with prejudice the appeal of the state from the dismissal of an indictment against the claimant and prohibiting the district court from remanding the proceedings to the Metropolitan Court.


OVERVIEW: The state appealed from the dismissal of drunk driving charges against the claimant. The claimant petitioned for a writ of prohibition to direct the district court's dismissal of the state's appeal and to prohibit the district court from remanding the proceedings. The claimant contended that the state's appeal was untimely filed based on an order that the district court had no jurisdiction to enter. The court denied the claimant's request, concluding that the district court's order was the final order. The alleged prior order was merely an oral ruling that did not trigger the time for filing an appeal. Moreover, N.M. R. Crim. P. Metro. Ct. 71(b) unconstitutionally limited the state's right to appeal to two bases. That was inconsistent with the state constitution's grant of an unrestricted right to appeal final judgments. Thus, Rule 71(b) was retracted.


OUTCOME: The court denied the claimant's request for a writ of prohibition or superintending control and retracted an unconstitutional court rule, which limited the state's right to appeal.

 

123 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Kennedy v. Yates Petro. Corp.


No. 14986


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


101 N.M. 268; 1984-NMSC-033; 681 P.2d 53; 1984 N.M. LEXIS 1632



March 21, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM DISTRICT COURT EDDY COUNTY, John B. Walker, District Judge



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owners sought review of a judgment entered by the District Court of Eddy County (New Mexico), which dismissed with prejudice their trespass action against defendant company. The trial court found that company's use of the property owners' land was a public one under N.M. Stat. Ann. § 70-3-5 (Cum. Supp. 1983) and that their exclusive remedy was the statutory remedy of inverse condemnation.


OVERVIEW: The property owners brought a trespass action against the company after they discovered a pipeline on their land. The trial court stayed that action on the condition that the company initiate condemnation proceedings. A condemnation petition was filed. The trial court found that § 70-3-5 made the company's use of the land, as a matter of law, a public use and that it had an immediate right to possess the right-of-way. It also found that statutory remedy of inverse condemnation was the property owners' exclusive remedy and dismissed their complaint. The property owners appealed from that judgment, which was reversed. The matter was remanded. A provision of the Eminent Domain Code, N.M. Stat. Ann. § 42A-1-22 (Repl. Pamp. 1981), authorized immediate possession of the property by the condemnor provided that its use was a public one and immediate possession was necessary. While the declaration of public use contained in § 70-3-5 was entitled to deference, that issue was reserved for the courts. Therefore, the trial court erred when it found that § 70-3-5 was conclusive. Rather, a real and substantial relation to the public use had to be demonstrated.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment, which had dismissed with prejudice the property owners' trespass action against the company. The matter was remanded for further proceedings.

Chapman v. Luna


No. 14867


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


101 N.M. 59; 1984-NMSC-029; 678 P.2d 687; 1984 N.M. LEXIS 1638; 20 ERC (BNA) 2170



March 13, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF BERNALILLO COUNTY, Philip R. Ashby, District Judge



DISPOSITION: We conclude that the Program may be continued without imposition of a fee and without a repair cap for vehicles that do not come into compliance; otherwise, the Council and Commission will have to discontinue the Program.

IT IS SO ORDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners appealed the judgment of the District Court of Bernalillo County (New Mexico), which dismissed their suit against respondents, city and county officials and an air quality control board, seeking a declaratory judgment that the operation and enforcement of a joint motor vehicle emissions inspection program was unlawful.


OVERVIEW: The city and county officials enacted ordinances that established prohibitions against excessive air pollutant emissions from motor vehicles in the city and county. The ordinances delegated the power to regulate the operation of the vehicle emissions inspection and maintenance program to the board, and the board adopted regulations for the establishment of the program. The court affirmed in part and reversed in part the trial court's judgment for respondents in petitioners' declaratory judgment action. The court held that the imposition of an inspection fee was prohibited under N.M. Stat. Ann. § 66-6-25 and was not a valid exercise of local authorities' home rule power. Further, the repair provision was invalid as it was discriminatory in its application. However, the criminal penalty provisions of the program were not invalid, and the invalid provisions did not nullify the ordinances because of the severability clause. Thus, the program could be lawfully operated without the imposition of the inspection fee and without a repair cap for vehicles that were not in compliance.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part and reversed in part. The court held that the program could be continued without the unlawful imposition of the inspection fee and without a repair cap for vehicles that were not in compliance.

 

125 of 795 DOCUMENTS


FIRST NATL. BANK OF SANTA FE v. SOUTHWEST YACHT & MARINE SUPPLY CORP.


NO. 14,961, NO. 14,974


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


1984 N.M. LEXIS 1623; 23 N.M. St. B. Bull. 253



February 20, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF SANTA FE COUNTY, Michael Francke, District Judge



DISPOSITION: The cause is remanded to the trial court for further proceedings in accordance with this opinion.

IT IS SO ORDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an action between appellant bank and appellee company to replevy goods securing payment of a promissory note, the District Court of Santa Fe County (New Mexico) granted the company's motion to dissolve the writ of replevin. Subsequently, the bank filed a motion for summary judgment on its amended affidavit in replevin and on the wrongful replevin counterclaim. The district court granted the motion in part and denied it in part.


OVERVIEW: On cross appeal, the company argued that the district court erred in limiting damages for wrongful replevin to those set forth in N.M. Stat. Ann. § 42-8-11 (1978). The court noted that two sections of the replevin statute provided remedies for situations in which a wrongful replevin had occurred, § 42-8-11 and § 42-8-19. The bank argued that these two sections were mutually exclusive; that once the company chose not to accept its offer to return the wrongfully replevied property its remedies were limited to those under § 42-8-11. The court disagreed. Although the company was limited to the remedies found in the replevin statute, it was not limited to remedies found in only one section of that statute. The two sections addressed two separate wrongs. Section 42-8-19 addressed the specific failure of a plaintiff to prove the truth of the facts in his affidavit. Section 42-8-11, on the other hand, allowed a defendant to recover judgment in case a plaintiff failed to prosecute his suit with success and without unreasonable or unnecessary delay. The company could recover reasonable attorney fees incurred in the dissolution of the wrongfully issued writ of replevin under § 42-8-19.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the district court on the issue of relation back of the amended replevin affidavit, and remanded for determination of the company's damages for wrongful replevin.

State v. Guzman

OVERVIEW: Defendant kidnapped two college students at knifepoint. He repeatedly stabbed one victim and left her on the side of the road, then raped and killed the second victim. The court concluded that a review of the evidence supported the jury's determination.

State v. McCormack


No. 14859


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


100 N.M. 657; 1984-NMSC-006; 674 P.2d 1117; 1984 N.M. LEXIS 1605



January 9, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY: ORIGINAL PROCEEDING ON CERTIORARI, N. Randolph Reese, District Judge



DISPOSITION: Decision of the Court of Appeals reversed and case remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of criminal trespass. The Court of Appeals (New Mexico) determined that the lands upon which defendant traversed were owned by the federal government, were public, and could not form the basis of a trespass action, and reversed the conviction. The State obtained certiorari review.


OVERVIEW: Citizens planned a demonstration at a waste plant, which was owned by the U.S. government pursuant to the Treaty of Guadalupe Hidalgo. After New Mexico became a state it acquired sovereign control over the site, subject to the federal government's proprietary management of the land. Defendant, a photographer, followed the demonstrators into an area that the protestors were warned was a no trespass area, and was charged with trespass. The appellate court held that the property was public land and there could be no trespass on public land. The court held that because the State retained sovereignty and dominion over the property, and the federal government's position was one of an individual proprietor, the property belonged to the State and was not public property. The court held that the property was thus "lands of another" as defined by N.M. Stat. Ann. § 30-14-1(A), and reversed the appellate court's judgment.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and remanded for further proceedings.

State v. Cheadle


No. 14177


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


101 N.M. 282; 1983-NMSC-093; 681 P.2d 708; 1983 N.M. LEXIS 2365



November 21, 1983 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied December 21, 1983. Stay Granted and Mandate Recalled January 5, 1984. Certiorari Denied, April 16, 1984. See 104 S.Ct. 1930.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF BERNALILLO COUNTY, Harry E. Stowers, Jr., District Judge



DISPOSITION: Affirmed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment from the District Court of Bernalillo County (New Mexico), which convicted him of murder in the first degree, kidnapping, armed robbery, and criminal sexual penetration. He was sentenced to death. The defendant contended that the death sentence was excessive and the trial court erred in denying his motion to strike identification testimony and in refusing to grant immunity to a defense witness.


OVERVIEW: Defendant approached a man and woman in the parking lot of a bar, brandished a gun and instructed them to walk into an alley. He demanded their money, shot the man, and attempted to rape the woman. The woman escaped, stopped a policeman, and described defendant. Defendant was tried and convicted of first degree murder, kidnapping, armed robbery, and criminal sexual penetration. On appeal he claimed that the identification of all witnesses should be struck because they had viewed his picture furnished to the media by the police, that the trial court erred in refusing to grant immunity to a defense witness, and that the death sentence was excessive. The court affirmed the trial court's decision. The court held that: (1) the out-of-court identification testimony was proper where the witnesses based their identification upon their own confrontations with defendant; (2) defendant was not entitled to a grant of defense witness immunity where he failed to comply with N.M. R. Crim. P. 58 (1980) and the trial court had no authority to demand that the state seek immunity; and (3) defendant's death sentence was neither excessive nor disproportionate.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's conviction of the defendant for first degree murder and the trial court's judgment of death sentence. The court remanded the case to the trial court to set a date of execution, not less than 60 days nor more than 90 days from the issuance of the mandate on the court's judgment.

State v. Segotta


No. 14972


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


100 N.M. 498; 1983-NMSC-092; 672 P.2d 1129; 1983 N.M. LEXIS 2371



November 17, 1983

DISPOSITION: Court of Appeals' decisions reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State filed a petition for a writ of certiorari seeking review of a decision of the Court of Appeals (New Mexico), which affirmed defendants' convictions for second degree murder and one defendants' conviction for solicitation to commit first degree murder, but remanded both cases for resentencing because N.M. Stat. Ann. § 31-18-15.1 (1978) was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The State indicted defendants for first degree murder and conspiracy to commit first degree murder. One of the defendants was also charged with solicitation to commit first degree murder. Defendants were convicted of second degree murder and the one defendant was convicted for solicitation to commit first degree murder, but the appellate court remanded both cases for resentencing, finding that § 31-18-15.1 was unconstitutional. On appeal, the court held that the appellate court, in a prior holding, had specifically held that § 31-18-15.1 was not unconstitutional as violative of either due process, separation of powers, or double jeopardy. The court found that the statute was not unconstitutionally vague. The court determined that some of the factors which a trial court might consider and weigh as mitigating or aggravating circumstances in sentencing pursuant to § 31-18-15.1 were unusual aspects of defendant's character, past conduct, age, health, any events surrounding crime, and the possibility of rehabilitation. The court reversed the order finding the statute unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the order from the trial court.

 

130 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State v. Gilbert


No. 13443


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


100 N.M. 392; 1983-NMSC-083; 671 P.2d 640; 1983 N.M. LEXIS 2353



October 17, 1983 


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF BERNALILLO COUNTY, Richard B. Traub, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the decision of the District Court of Bernalillo County (New Mexico), which convicted defendant of two counts of kidnapping in the first degree with firearm enhancement, two counts of criminal sexual penetration in the second degree with firearm enhancement, and two counts of first degree murder with aggravating circumstances. Defendant was sentenced to death for each count of first degree murder.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the trial court's automatic exclusion for cause of potential jurors based on their views of capital punishment was error. The court held that as defendant did not contend that any particular juror was improperly disqualified, the argument was viewed as a general constitutional attack on the very process of death qualification. The court affirmed defendant's conviction, holding that the trial court correctly followed constitutional and statutory requirements in conducting the death qualification of the jury. The court rejected defendant's contention that the trial court erred in failing to instruct the jury on the defense of insanity, holding that there was no basis in the evidence for an insanity instruction. The court affirmed the sentence holding that the death penalty in and of itself did not violate federal or state constitutional mandates against cruel and unusual punishment. The court held that the bifurcated trial to one jury did not offend constitutional principles as firsthand observation of the evidence provided the jury with the best information possible to make the weighty decisions involved in both guilt determination and sentencing.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction of defendant for two counts of kidnapping in the first degree with firearm enhancement, two counts of criminal sexual penetration in the second degree with firearm enhancement, and two counts of first degree murder with aggravating circumstances.

 

131 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Chronis v. State


No. 14130


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


100 N.M. 342; 1983-NMSC-081; 670 P.2d 953; 1983 N.M. LEXIS 2349



October 13, 1983 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: October 13, 1983


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF SANTA FE COUNTY, C. Fincher Neal, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, owners-operators and owners-lessors of liquor licenses, challenged the judgment of the District Court of Santa Fe County (New Mexico), which held that the Liquor Control Act (act) was not affected by the unconstitutionality of certain sections of the act and that § 36 was constitutional. Appellees, alcohol beverage control and revenue department, challenged the judgment insofar as it held that §§ 103 and 114 were unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Appellants sought a declaration that the act was unconstitutional. The trial court held that the act was constitutional except for §§ 103 and 114. It also held that the entire act was not affected by the successful attack on §§ 103 and 114 despite the governor's veto of a severability clause. On appeal, the court reversed the trial court's finding that the governor's veto of the severability clause was constitutionally permissible. In all other respects, the judgment was affirmed. Because the act did not appropriate money, the governor's veto power was invalidly exercised. Because liquor licensees had no property right in their license, § 36 was constitutional. The act did not unreasonably deprive a licensee of all or substantially all of the beneficial use of his license. Thus, it did not effectuate a taking without due process. However, § 103, which allowed summary temporary suspension of a license without prior notice or a hearing, violated procedural due process and was unconstitutional. Section 114 was unconstitutional because the reduction in gross receipts taxes was an unconstitutional subsidy to the liquor industry in violation of N.M. art. IX, § 14.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's finding that the governor's veto of the severability clause was constitutionally permissible and held that the act was severable. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment holding that § 36 of the act was constitutional but that §§ 103 and 114 of the act were unconstitutional.

 

132 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Battaglini v. Town of Red River


No. 14038


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


100 N.M. 287; 1983-NMSC-067; 669 P.2d 1082; 1983 N.M. LEXIS 2403



September 8, 1983 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied September 28, 1983.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant town appealed a judgment of the trial court (New Mexico), which held that its sign ordinance was unenforceable because it contravened N.M. Stat. Ann. § 42A-1-34 (Repl. Pamp. 1981), and granted plaintiff sign owners a writ of prohibition against enforcement of the ordinance.


OVERVIEW: The town had an ordinance that regulated the size, design, placement, and maintenance of signs. The ordinance allowed two years for owners of signs to bring them into compliance or remove them. One year later the town amended the ordinance to allow five years for compliance, measured from the date of the amendment. Prior to the date for compliance, the state enacted N.M. Stat. Ann. § 42A-1-34, which prohibited a municipality from requiring removal of an advertising structure without just compensation. The sign owners filed an action to enjoin the enforcement of the ordinance, and the trial court granted a writ of prohibition, finding that the ordinance violated the statute. The town appealed. On appeal the court affirmed. It held that (1) the town did not have the legal right to cause the removal of the signs until five years had passed, (2) the fact that the application of section 42A-1-34 drew upon facts arising before its enactment did not cause a retroactive application, (3) the statute did not violate N.M. Const. art. IV, § 24 because it was not a "special law," and (4) the five-year amortization period did not constitute "paying just compensation," as required by the statute.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which held that the town's sign ordinance was unenforceable because it contravened state statute, and granted the sign owners a writ of prohibition against enforcement of the ordinance.

United States Brewers Ass'n v. Dir. of N.M. Dep't of Alcoholic Beverage Control


No. 13053


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


100 N.M. 216; 1983-NMSC-059; 668 P.2d 1093; 1983 N.M. LEXIS 2326; 1983-2 Trade Cas. (CCH) P65,750



July 21, 1983 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied August 25, 1983.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF SANTA FE COUNTY, Lorenzo F. Garcia, District Judge



DISPOSITION: Affirmed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, brewing association and others, sought review of an order from the District Court of Santa Fe County (New Mexico), which granted a summary judgment in favor of appellee Director of New Mexico Department of Alcoholic Beverage Control in an action in which appellants challenged the constitutionality of the 1979 amendment to the Discrimination in Selling Act (Act), N.M. Stat. Ann. §§ 60-12-1 through 60-12-10 (1978).


OVERVIEW: Appellants filed an action seeking to obtain an injunction against the director to enjoin him from enforcing an amendment to the Act, N.M. Stat. Ann. § 60-12-2 (1978), which extended a price affirmation law to brewed products that had previously been excluded. The trial court granted a summary judgment in favor of the director. The court concluded the Act was a valid exercise of the state's police power.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed an order that granted a summary judgment in favor of the director in an action in which appellants challenged the constitutionality of a statutory amendment that extended a price affirmation law to brewed products that had previously been excluded. 134 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Taylor v. Delgarno Transp., Inc.


No. 14614


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


100 N.M. 138; 1983-NMSC-052; 667 P.2d 445; 1983 N.M. LEXIS 2307



June 10, 1983 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied August 4, 1983.


PRIOR HISTORY: CERTIFICATION FROM UNITED STATES DISTRICT COURT, Honorable Edwin L. Mechem, Judge


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The United States District Court for the District of New Mexico certified a question, pursuant to N.M. Stat. Ann. § 34-2-8 (1978), regarding whether plaintiff workman was required to reimburse defendant employer for workmen's compensation benefits that he had received prior to a jury award that apportioned liability between the employer and defendants, manufacturers and a subcontractor.


OVERVIEW: After the workman was injured on the job, he filed a negligence action against the manufacturers of the machinery that caused his injury. His employer and the subcontractor were impleaded. When the jury apportioned liability among the defendants, and allocated 10 percent to the employer, the workman contented that any amount subrogated to the employer's insurer as reimbursement of workman's compensation benefits should be reduced by that percentage. The trial court certified the question, and the court entered an order the subrogation award for compensation and medical benefits should not have been reduced. The Workmen's Compensation Act, N.M. Stat. Ann. §§ 52-1-1 to 52-1-69 (1978), provided the exclusive remedy for claims by injured workmen against their employers. Because workmen were covered by the Act, irregardless any fault by an employer, the employer's liability for the injury could not be used to offset any subrogation obligation. Further, although the jury was able to apportion liability under the pure comparative negligence standard, this did not reduce the employer's absolute right to reimbursement under N.M. Stat. Ann. § 52-1-56.


OUTCOME: The court entered an order that found the employer's insurer entitled to reimbursement for workmen's compensation benefits without apportionment as to fault.

State v. Cruz

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On certiorari, the court reviewed the reversal, by the Court of Appeals (New Mexico), of the trial court's denial of respondent's motion to dismiss an indictment, and of respondent's convictions for two counts of battery on a peace officer.


OVERVIEW: Respondent received a letter notifying him that he was the target of a grand jury investigation and that he had a right to appear and testify. Respondent was given several opportunities to testify, but he refused to make a decision, repeatedly insisting that he wished to testify after another witness; the prosecutor refused to allow this and told respondent that if he did not make a decision, he would be foreclosed from testifying. Respondent failed to comply, but later told the prosecutor that he wished to testify; the prosecutor refused to allow this. Respondent moved to dismiss the subsequent indictment, alleging that he had been deprived of a meaningful opportunity to testify before the grand jury in violation of N.M. Stat. Ann. § 31-6-11(B). The court reversed the judgment dismissing the indictment and affirmed the convictions. It held that the four days' notice given to respondent was sufficient time to exercise his right to testify. It further held that the prosecutor did not obstruct respondent's opportunity to testify. The court concluded that the statutory requirements had been met where respondent both notified of his target status and given an opportunity to testify.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment, and affirmed defendant's convictions.

Springer Elec. Coop., Inc. v. Raton

SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO

PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF COLFAX COUNTY, John B. Wright, District Judge



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part, affirmed in part; and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff cooperative appealed from a decision of the District Court of Colfax County (New Mexico), which declared that unrestricted competition between the cooperative and defendant municipality and defendant public service company was permitted. The municipality had formed the public service company and constructed electric service lines within the municipality and within five miles of the municipality's boundaries.


OVERVIEW: The cooperative sued to enjoin the municipality and the public service company from constructing electric service lines within five miles from the municipality's boundary and sought declaratory relief as to the service rights of the cooperative and the municipality and public service company within five miles of the municipality's boundaries. The district court denied the cooperative relief. The cooperative appealed. The court noted that the municipality acquired an electric system by creating and incorporating the public service company as a municipally owned corporation and could do so under N.M. Stat. Ann. § 3-24-1 (1982), which allowed a municipality to maintain an electric utility for the generation and distribution of electricity to persons residing within the municipality and within five miles of the municipality's boundary. The court reversed the district court finding that the municipality and public service company did not exercise dominion over territory within five miles of the municipality's boundaries, affirmed the finding that customers were indispensable parties in an enjoinment action against the public service company and remanded for further proceedings.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the district court finding, but affirmed a finding that customers were indispensable parties in respect of an action to enjoin them from receiving electric utility service. The matter was remanded to the district court for further proceedings.

State ex. rel Human Servs. Dep't v. Staples (In re Doe)


No. 14692


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


100 N.M. 92; 1983-NMSC-021; 666 P.2d 771; 1983 N.M. LEXIS 2247



February 18, 1983 


PRIOR HISTORY: ORIGINAL PROCEEDING ON CERTIORARI, George L. Zimmerman, District Judge



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In original proceedings, certiorari was granted in a parental termination case upon the application of petitioner State of New Mexico to review a court of appeals decision, which addressed the constitutionality of N.M. Stat. Ann. § 40-7-4(B)(4) (Supp. 1982). The court of appeals held that § 40-7-4(B)(4) was void for vagueness and reversed a decision of the trial court terminating respondent mother's parental rights.


OVERVIEW: One judge dissented from the majority opinion of the court of appeals and outlined her reasons for finding § 40-7-4(B)(4) neither vague nor indefinite. On certiorari, the court adopted the dissenting opinion as its opinion, thereby upholding the constitutionality of § 40-7-4(B)(4). The majority of the appellate court was correct that the test to be applied when a claim of unconstitutional vagueness was whether persons of common intelligence had to guess at its meaning. But it was also an indispensable rule that the whole statute had to be brought under consideration. Section 40-7-4(B)(4) was only a part of a subsection of the statute entitled "Termination of parental rights," which section, in turn, was only a part of the Adoption Act, N.M. Stat. Ann. §§ 40-7-1 to 40-7-11 and N.M. Stat. Ann. §§ 40-7-13 to 40-7-17 (Supp. 1982). The dissenting judge concluded that she could not agree that from the great wealth of information and precedent available, and from a lifetime of familiarity with the English language, one had to guess at the meaning of any of the words used in § 40-7-4(B)(4). The trial court's judgment should have been affirmed. By adoption of the opinion, the court agreed.


OUTCOME: The majority opinion of the court of appeals was reversed, and the dissent, which upheld the constitutionality of the challenged section of the parental rights termination statute, was adopted as the order of the court.

In re DOE


No. 5306


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


1982 N.M. LEXIS 3031



November 9, 1982 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF OTERO COUNTY, ZIMMERMAN, Judge. 98 N.M. 540; 650 P.2d 824 



DISPOSITION: REVERSED. The statute being void, the child should be returned to the mother. The State shall pay the costs of this appeal.

IT IS SO ORDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant mother appealed a judgment from the District Court of Otero County (New Mexico), which terminated the mother's parental rights and awarded custody to plaintiff human services department under N.M. Stat. Ann. § 40-7-4.


OVERVIEW: The human services department filed a petition seeking to terminate the mother's parental rights. The trial court granted the petition. The mother appealed, arguing that § 40-7-4 was unconstitutional because it was vague. The court agreed and reversed the judgment. The court held that to withstand a vagueness challenge a statute must state its standard with adequate clarity and establish sufficient boundaries for the law to be fairly administered. The court found that the terms parent and disintegrated were not sufficiently defined within the statute. The evil that had to be avoided was conduct on the part of a parent that would deny the child the care, guidance, or control necessary for his physical, emotional, and medical needs. Parent child disintegration did not have a precise meaning: it lacked metes and bounds. The language did not inform parents of what they needed to do to avoid termination of their parental rights.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and ordered that the minor child be returned to the mother.

McKay v. Davis


No. 13945


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


99 N.M. 29; 1982-NMSC-122; 653 P.2d 860; 1982 N.M. LEXIS 2905



September 30, 1982 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied November 2, 1982.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM DISTRICT COURT OF BERNALILLO COUNTY, Richard B. Traub, District Judge



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant judge sought review of the decision of the District Court of Bernalillo County (New Mexico), which prohibited the introduction of evidence of appellee driver's refusal to submit to a breath alcohol test.


OVERVIEW: The driver was arrested for driving while under the influence of liquor and refused to submit to a breath-alcohol test, the driver refused. The driver filed a motion to exclude reference to his refusal to take the test and the judge of the metropolitan court denied his request. The driver obtained a writ from the district court prohibiting the introduction of or comments on evidence of the driver's refusal to take the test. On appeal, the court reversed. The court held that the driver's refusal to take the breath test was admissible under the Implied Consent Act, N.M. Stat. Ann. §§ 66-8-105 through 66-8-112 (1978), under U.S. Const. Amend. V, and under N.M. R. Evid. 401. The court held that there was no constitutional right to refuse and that any testimony about the refusal to submit did not burden the Fifth Amendment. The court held that the introduction of and comment on the driver's refusal to take a breath test did not violate the U.S. Const. Amend. V. The court held that the driver's refusal to take a chemical test was relevant to show his consciousness of guilt and fear of the test results.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the district court's grant of the writ prohibiting the judge from allowing the introduction of evidence of driver's refusal to take a breath alcohol test and remand the case for further proceedings.

Kent Nowlin Constr. Co. v. Gutierrez


No. 13914


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


99 N.M. 389; 1982-NMSC-123; 658 P.2d 1116; 1982 N.M. LEXIS 3038



September 30, 1982 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Order January 14, 1983. Rehearing Denied January 14, 1983.


PRIOR HISTORY:  99 N.M. 394, 658 P.2d 1121.



DISPOSITION: Reversing judgment. Since we have held that the motion for summary judgment should have been granted, we do not reach the other issues raised on certiorari.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner employer sought review of the decision from the Court of Appeals (New Mexico), which affirmed a judgment in favor of respondent estate representatives in their wrongful death action against the employer, which asserted the Workmen's Compensation Act, N.M. Stat. Ann. §§ 52-1-1 through 52-1-69, as a complete defense.


OVERVIEW: The employee was killed in the course and scope of his employment and the employer paid benefits as required by the act. The representatives, who were non-United States resident relatives at the time of the accident, filed a wrongful death action against the employer and the employer argued that the Act was the exclusive remedy and that N.M. Stat. Ann. § 52-1-52 (1978) barred recovery to non-residents. The trial court rendered a verdict in favor of the representatives, and the appellate court affirmed. The employer challenged the decision, and the court reversed. The meaning of N.M. Stat. Ann. §§ 51-1-8(C), 52-1-9 (1978) was that the Act was an exclusive remedy unless otherwise provided for in the Act. Thus, dependents residing outside the United States at the time of the employee's injury were barred from pursuing their common law remedies due to the exclusive remedy provisions under the Act.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment in favor of the representatives in their wrongful death action against the employer.

 

144 of 795 DOCUMENTS


N.M. State Highway Comm'n v. Ferguson


No. 13743


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


98 N.M. 680; 1982-NMSC-107; 652 P.2d 230; 1982 N.M. LEXIS 2894



September 27, 1982 


PRIOR HISTORY: ORIGINAL PROCEEDING ON CERTIORARI



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, the State of New Mexico and the New Mexico State Highway Commission, sought review of a decision of the Court of Appeals (New Mexico), which reversed a trial court's order dismissing them as parties in respondent passengers' suit against them for damages for personal injuries and wrongful death.


OVERVIEW: The passengers alleged that petitioners' negligent design, construction, and maintenance of a state highway caused the vehicle in which they were riding to go off the road. Petitioners sought dismissal for failure to state a claim on the ground that notice under the Tort Claims Act had not been given within the statutory period. The trial court granted the motion and dismissed defendant county. The Court of Appeals affirmed the order dismissing the county and reversed the order dismissing the State and the Commission. On appeal, the court reversed. The court held that an accident report prepared by the state police did not constitute actual notice within the meaning of N.M. Stat. Ann. § 41-4-16(B) (1978). The court was of the opinion that the statute meant that the particular agency that caused the alleged harm must have had actual notice before written notice was required. The court held that the notice provisions of the Tort Claims Act were to ensure that the agency allegedly at fault was notified that it might be subject to a lawsuit. Moreover, the court held that it would construe a statute to give it its intended effect, pursuant to N.M. Stat. Ann. § 12-2-2 (1978).


OUTCOME: In the passengers' action for damages, the court reversed the decision of the Court of Appeals, which affirmed the trial court's order of dismissal with regard to the county and reversed the order of dismissal with regard to the State and the Commission.

 

145 of 795 DOCUMENTS


General Tel. Co. v. Corp. Comm'n (In re General Tel. Co.)


No. 13726


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


98 N.M. 749; 1982-NMSC-106; 652 P.2d 1200; 1982 N.M. LEXIS 2901



September 15, 1982 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied October 20, 1982.


PRIOR HISTORY: DIRECT REMOVAL FROM CORPORATION COMMISSION



DISPOSITION: Order remanded to Commission for further proceeding.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The court granted a petition filed by appellant telephone utility for removal of its application to appellee, the New Mexico State Corporation Commission (SCC), for a rate increase. In its final order, the SCC concluded that the rates proposed by the utility were unreasonable, and it provided a lesser rate increase than the utility had requested.


OVERVIEW: During hearings on the utility's application to the SCC, intervenors, a board of county commissioners and four cities, produced evidence to show that the utility's quality of service was inadequate. In the removal proceedings, the utility raised constitutional objections to the SCC's use of the double leverage method, its determination of cash working quality, and its use of service quality issues to penalize the utility. Weighing the evidence pursuant to N.M. Const. art. XI, § 7, the court adopted certain of the SCC's findings as its own, but it remanded the SCC's order for further proceedings. The court held that the SCC lawfully and reasonably used the double leverage method to determine a fair rate of return, and the use of the method did not deprive the utility of due process or equal protection of the law. It was arbitrary and capricious, however, for the SCC to depart from its past practice in determining the utility's cash working capital without sufficient prior notice or reasonable justification as reflected in the record. The SCC was without authority to penalize the utility for service quality issues after it had arrived at a fair and reasonable rate of return.


OUTCOME: The court remanded the order to the SCC for further proceedings.

United Nuclear Corp. v. General Atomic Co.


No. 13536


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


98 N.M. 633; 1982-NMSC-105; 651 P.2d 1277; 1982 N.M. LEXIS 2902



September 15, 1982 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied October 4, 1982.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF SANTA FE COUNTY, James W. Musgrove, District Judge



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: This suit arose out of a complex billion-dollar dispute between appellee nuclear corporation and appellant atomic company. In this action, the atomic company challenged the decision of the District Court of Santa Fe County (New Mexico) which declared void a California arbitration award in its favor and affirmed prior judgments in favor of the nuclear corporation.


OVERVIEW: The issues on appeal were: (1) whether prior United States Supreme Court (Supreme Court) decisions prohibited the trial court from voiding the arbitration award and affirming the prior judgments; (2) whether the trial court had jurisdiction to void the arbitration award under the Federal Arbitration Act, 9 U.S.C.S. §§ 1-14 (Arbitration Act); (3) whether the Arbitration Act prevented the trial court from voiding the award; (4) and whether the nuclear corporation's claim for supplemental relief was cognizable under the New Mexico Declaratory Judgment Act, N.M. Stat. Ann. §§ 44-6-1 to 15 (1978). The nuclear corporation claimed that the trial court's decision conformed to the Supreme Court mandates, that the arbitration award was void under the doctrine of res judicata, and that there was no agreement to arbitrate. After review, this court concluded that the trial court had jurisdiction. Further, it agreed with the trial court and held that antitrust issues were not arbitrable, and the arbitrators did not have jurisdiction to issue an award. They acted in manifest disregard of the law and in excess of their powers in failing to give full faith and credit to the prior decisions.


OUTCOME: The district court's judgment was affirmed.

State ex. rel. Human Servs. Dep't. v. Staples (In re Doe)


No. 14196


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


98 N.M. 540; 1982-NMSC-099; 650 P.2d 824; 1982 N.M. LEXIS 2897



September 7, 1982 


PRIOR HISTORY: ORIGINAL PROCEEDING ON CERTIORARI



DISPOSITION: Court of Appeals reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner State of New Mexico brought an action against respondent mother to terminate her parental rights to her minor son pursuant to N.M. Stat. Ann. § 40-7-4, (Supp.1981). The trial court terminated the mother's rights. The basis for the mother's appeal was a challenge to the constitutionality of § 40-7-4. The court of appeals (New Mexico) reversed, ignoring the constitutionality argument. The State brought a further appeal.


OVERVIEW: The conditions required by N.M. Stat. Ann. § 40-7-4, (Supp.1981) were all found to exist by the trial court. The opinion of the court of appeals ignored the arguments presented in the briefs and held that the trial court's termination order was improper because the child was not placed in foster care by court order. On further appeal, the court determined that such a construction of the statute was more restrictive than provided by § 40-7-4. No explanation was given for failing to consider that portion of the statute, which recognized that placement may be made without a court order. The court did not know whether the appellate court merely overlooked the additional language of the statute or whether the additional words were deleted in an effort to see a result in the case more acceptable to the reviewer. Under either circumstance, the court of appeals erred in reversing on that ground. The case was remanded because the court had not been asked to consider the constitutional arguments that were raised and affirmance of the trial court's decision by the court would leave the mother's claims unheard.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the court of appeals was reversed, and the cause was remanded for consideration of the arguments raised by counsel for the State and the mother on an expedited basis.

State v. Amador


No. 13787


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


98 N.M. 270; 1982-NMSC-083; 648 P.2d 309; 1982 N.M. LEXIS 2871; 33 A.L.R.4th 656



July 13, 1982 


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF LEA COUNTY, C. Fincher Neal, District Judge



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant bondsman appealed a decision by the District Court of Lea County (New Mexico), which entered an order forfeiting the entire amount of the bail bond posted on a criminal defendant's behalf, after that defendant failed to appear for trial.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was notified of his trial date, but the bondsman was not. Defendant failed to appear because he was incarcerated in another state. The bondsman first learned of defendant's failure to appear when he was served with an order to show cause. The bondsman contended that the forfeiture should have been set aside because he had a due process right to receive personal notice of defendant's trial date, and that the lower court abused its discretion in refusing to set aside the forfeiture. The court ruled that the lower court abused its discretion. The court held that the bondsman had no right to receive personal notice of defendant's trial date under the due process clause because the procedures were adequate to protect his rights where he was not obligated to produce defendant for trial, but was merely obligated to pay the penalty for his failure to appear. The court concluded that the lower court abused it discretion in forfeiting the entire amount of bail because it was unjust to do so when the bondsman's efforts were thwarted by the actions of another sovereign.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the forfeiture and remanded for further proceedings.

State v. Lucero


No. 13922


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


98 N.M. 204; 1982-NMSC-069; 647 P.2d 406; 1982 N.M. LEXIS 2862



June 24, 1982 


PRIOR HISTORY: ORIGINAL PROCEEDING ON CERTIORARI, (FRANK ALLEN, Trial Judge)



DISPOSITION: Court of Appeals reversed and conviction reinstated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state sought review of a judgment of the Court of Appeals (New Mexico), which held that New Mexico's child abuse statute, N.M. Stat. Ann. § 30-6-1(C) (Cum. Supp. 1981), was constitutional but reversed defendant's conviction thereunder on the ground that the trial court excluded testimony by a defense witness on the issue of duress.


OVERVIEW: During her trial, defendant testified that she knew her boyfriend was physically abusing her son, but that she could not contact the police or get help for her son because her boyfriend threatened to inflict more harm on her and her son if she did so. At trial, out of the jury's presence, a psychologist testified that defendant acted under duress in not seeking help for her son because of her fear of her boyfriend, but the trial court ruled that this testimony was inadmissible because defendant's intent was immaterial to the charge of child abuse. The appellate court reversed defendant's conviction on the ground that the exclusion of this testimony was improper. The court affirmed the appellate court's finding that the child abuse statute was constitutional but reversed with respect to its finding on the duress issue and reinstated defendant's conviction. The court held that § 30-6-1(C) was a strict liability statute, thus, it did not require an intent, duress was not a defense to the crime, and the psychologist's testimony was properly excluded.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the appellate court's judgment that New Mexico's child abuse statute was constitutional, but reversed the appellate court's decision on the duress issue and reinstated defendant's conviction for child abuse.

151 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Wells v. County of Valencia


No. 13856


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


98 N.M. 3; 1982-NMSC-048; 644 P.2d 517; 1982 N.M. LEXIS 2838



April 13, 1982 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied May 7, 1982.


PRIOR HISTORY: CERTIFICATION FROM UNITED STATES DISTRICT COURT, CIV-80-0153 C



DISPOSITION: In those cases where tort damages will constitute a portion of the damages for deprivation of a constitutional right, general principles against double recovery will prevail.

IT IS SO ORDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In plaintiff inmate's claim against defendants, county and individuals, under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 and the New Mexico Tort Claims Act (Act), N.M. Stat. Ann. §§ 41-4-1 to 41-4-29 (1978) (Orig. Pamph. & Cum. Supp. 1981), filed in the United States District Court for the District of New Mexico, the question of whether the Act prohibited the inmate from bringing both claims was certified for consideration.


OVERVIEW: The inmate brought a claim against defendants for cruel and unusual punishment under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 and for personal injuries under the Act. The federal district court certified the question of whether the Act prohibited the inmate from burning the action under the Act when he also brought an action under 42 U.S.C.S. § 42. The court held that the Act did not prohibit the inmate from bringing an action for damages under the Act when he also pursued, by reason of the same occurrence, an action against the same government under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983. The court cited the Supremacy Clause, which barred a legislature from enacting a law that would have had the effect of depriving the inmate of his rights secured by the United States Constitution, and presumed that the legislature enacted the statute within the bounds of the Constitution. The court then construed the Act's language narrowly to mean that a tort was separate and distinct from a constitutional deprivation, which could have been remedied in a jurisdiction other than New Mexico, and that the legislature did not intend to condition it waiver of immunity on the inmate's forbearance of his federal rights.


OUTCOME: The court, in answering a certified question, held that the Act did not prohibit the inmate from bringing an action for damages under the Act where he also pursued, by reason of the same occurrence, an action against the same government under § 1983.

Terry v. N.M. State Highway Comm'n


No. 13886, 14141


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


98 N.M. 119; 1982-NMSC-047; 645 P.2d 1375; 1982 N.M. LEXIS 2837



April 12, 1982 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied June 7, 1982.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF SANTA FE COUNTY, Lorenzo F. Garcia, District Judge



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part and affirmed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff personal representatives appealed from a judgment of the District Court of Santa Fe County (New Mexico), which granted summary judgment in favor of defendants, engineer and contractor, on the ground that the personal representatives' wrongful death suits alleging negligent design and construction of a highway were time barred by N.M. Stat. Ann. § 37-1-27.


OVERVIEW: The personal representatives' decedents were killed in a one-car accident that occurred on a curve that was built as part of a highway construction project designed by the engineer and built by the contractor. The accident happened nine years and nine months after construction, and the suits were filed within two years of the accident. The trial court granted summary judgment to defendants on grounds that they were time barred. Reversing as to the engineer, the court held that because the cause of action arose three months before the expiration of the statute of repose, holding the personal representatives to such an abbreviated period was unreasonable and the statute of limitations for personal injuries under N.M. Stat. Ann. § 37-1-8 was the applicable period. The court held that as the personal representatives failed to produce any evidence contrary to the contractor's evidence that it merely carried out reasonable plans given to him, the court affirmed summary judgment for the contractor.


OUTCOME: The reversed the grant of summary judgment for the engineer, and affirmed the grant of summary judgment for the contractor in the personal representatives' claims arising from their decedents' deaths on a highway curve.

 

153 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State v. Sanchez


No. 14015


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


97 N.M. 521; 1982-NMSC-032; 641 P.2d 1068; 1982 N.M. LEXIS 2832



March 4, 1982 


PRIOR HISTORY: ORIGINAL PROCEEDING ON CERTIORARI



DISPOSITION: Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of trafficking in heroin for the second time. The trial court refused to sentence defendant to life imprisonment as called for in N.M. Stat. Ann. § 54-11-20(B)(2) (1975) of the Controlled Substance Act, and sentenced defendant as a first offender on the basis that § 54-11-20(B)(2) imposed cruel and unusual punishment. The Court of Appeals (New Mexico) reversed the decision of the trial court. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: At the sentencing hearing, the trial judge commented that defendant's latest conviction was based on evidence that the quantity of heroin was very small and was only one-tenth of one-percent in purity. He announced that he would not order a life sentence under such circumstances. The Court of Appeals held that the Controlled Substance Act was constitutionally sound and that a life sentence need not be imposed because the court had the authority to suspend or defer the sentence. On further appeal, the court noted that the crime was not designated as a first, second, third, or fourth degree felony but was designated only as "a felony." The penalty provisions for the offense were included in § 54-11-20B(2), which defined the crime. Under § 54-11-20B(2) and N.M. Stat. Ann. § 40A-29-11(A) (1953), the punishment could be either a fine or a life sentence. The legislature did not establish the crime as a first-degree felony and did not make a life sentence mandatory. Defendant was not convicted of a capital crime or first-degree felony, so the trial court had the authority to defer or suspend the sentence under N.M. Stat. Ann. § 31-20-3 (1981). A remand for resentencing was necessary.


OUTCOME: The decision of the Court of Appeals was affirmed. The cause was remanded to the trial court for resentencing of defendant.

On appeal, the protestants argued that §§ 3-21-15 through 3-21-26 were unconstitutional and that the petition in support of the district lacked sufficient signatures of registered electors as required by N.M. Stat. Ann. § 3-21-18(B). In reversing, the court found that the testimony of a former precinct worker was sufficient to deduct certain voters from the number of electors in the district but that there was an issue as to whether an increased number of voters appearing in an updated registration list after the petition was filed were electors in the district at the time of filing. The court declined to address the constitutional issue because the decision did not require it.

Tex. Nat'l Theatres, Inc. v. City of Albuquerque


No. 13463


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


97 N.M. 282; 1982-NMSC-004; 639 P.2d 569; 1982 N.M. LEXIS 2793



January 6, 1982 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied January 20, 1982.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF BERNALILLO COUNTY, William F. Riordan, Ditrict Judge



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff theater appealed the decision of the District Court of Bernalillo County (New Mexico), which granted a permanent injunction prohibiting it from operating as an "adult theater" until such time as it was granted a special use permit by defendant city in a proceeding concerning certain "special use" provisions of the Albuquerque, N.M., Comprehensive City Zoning Code.


OVERVIEW: A theater, as originally zoned, operated with no restrictions on the movies shown. Subsequently, the Albuquerque, N.M., Adult Entertainment Facilities Ordinance, No. 26-1977 (1977) was passed, which regulated adult theaters as special uses. The trial court found that the theater was a nonconforming structure because it showed adult movies, however, it was permitted to continue operation because the nonconforming use existed before the amendment. The theater abandoned its non-conforming use status when it did not use the theater to show adult movies for a continuous period of one year or more, as provided in Albuquerque, N.M., Comprehensive City Zoning Code § 40(D)(1)(i).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision, which granted an injunction prohibiting the theater from operating as an adult theater until it was granted a special use permit by the city.

Mechem v. City of Santa Fe


No. 13503


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


96 N.M. 668; 1981-NMSC-104; 634 P.2d 690; 1981 N.M. LEXIS 2408



October 5, 1981 


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF SANTA FE COUNTY, BRUCE E. KAUFMAN, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owners challenged the District Court of Santa Fe County (New Mexico) judgment in favor of appellee city in an action to enjoin enforcement of a restriction imposed by a special exception of the city board of adjustment. The property owners alleged that the zoning restriction was ultra vires, N.M. Stat. Ann. §§ 3-21-1, 3-21-8 (1978). The city raised the statute of limitations, N.M. Stat. Ann. § 3-21-9, laches, and unclean hands.


OVERVIEW: The property owners initiated an action against the city, seeking declaratory and injunctive relief from a restriction imposed in a special exception by the city's board of adjustment. The special exception granted the right to operate a tennis club, but required that the right end with any change in ownership. The trial court rendered judgment in favor of the city and the property owners appealed, asserting that the restriction was unconstitutional and void because it was ultra vires. The court held that the statute of limitations, N.M. Stat. Ann. § 3-21-9, did not bar the action because the property owners could collaterally attack the restriction as beyond the scope of the city's statutory authority. It found no basis for either defense of unclean hands or laches. On the merits, the court found that it was not within the proper function of the zoning authority, as provided in N.M. Stat. Ann. §§ 3-21-1, 3-21-8, to condition an exception to the use of real property upon personal rights of ownership rather than use. Although there was no express restriction, the effect of the condition stated in the exception and variance was to do just that, and thus, it was unenforceable.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment in favor of the city and directed the trial court to enter judgment for the property owners in a dispute concerning the enforceability of a special exception to zoning.

Lower Valley Water & Sanitation Dist. v. Public Serv. Co. (In re Lower Valley Water & Sanitation Dist.)

The court remanded the case for further findings under the Water and Sanitation District Act.

State v. Mabry


No. 13146


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


96 N.M. 317; 1981-NMSC-067; 630 P.2d 269; 1981 N.M. LEXIS 2367



July 2, 1981 


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF BERNALILLO COUNTY, Gene E. Franchini, District Judge



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the District Court of Bernalillo County (New Mexico), which convicted defendant of first-degree murder and sentenced him to life imprisonment as mandated by N.M. Stat. Ann. § 31-18-3(A) (1978).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of first-degree murder and sentenced to life imprisonment. On appeal the court affirmed, holding that: (1) the mandatory sentencing under N.M. Stat. Ann. §§ 31-18-3, 31-20-3 (1978) did not violate the doctrine of separation of powers contained in N.M. Const. art. III, § 1 because the legislature had the power establish penalties for criminal behavior and had the right to regulate or restrict the circumstances in which courts could suspend sentences in order to ensure the efficacy of criminal penalties; (2) the trial court did not abuse its discretion in submitting the question of defendant's competency to stand trial to the jury because the uncontroverted testimony established that he had the capacity to understand the nature and object of the proceedings and his condition in reference to the proceedings, and to cooperate with defense counsel in preparing a rational defense; and (3) defendant was not entitled to a new trial in light of newly-discovered evidence because the "newly-discovered" evidence was not discovered since the trial and there was no indication that the evidence would have changed the result.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment convicting defendant of first-degree murder and sentencing him to life imprisonment.

N.M. State Bd. of Educ. v. Bd. of Educ.


No. 13237, 13238


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


95 N.M. 588; 1981-NMSC-031; 624 P.2d 530; 1981 N.M. LEXIS 2267



February 25, 1981 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: February 25, 1981


PRIOR HISTORY: ORIGINAL PROCEEDINGS ON CERTIORARI
Board of Educ. v. Bryant, 95 N.M. 620, 624 P.2d 1017, 1980 N.M. App. LEXIS 920 (N.M. Ct. App., 1980)



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, a teacher and the New Mexico State Board of Education, sought review of a decision from the New Mexico Court of Appeals, which reversed an administrative order that had reinstated the teacher's employment with respondent, a local school district.


OVERVIEW: The teacher, who was tenured, was terminated on grounds of nepotism after her father was elected as a member of the local school board. The court held that N.M. Stat. Ann. § 22-5-6 (1978), which prohibited school districts from employing relatives of school board members, applied only to the initial hiring decision. There was no reason to suspect nepotism in the continued employment of a tenured teacher whose competency had been established by years of service, merely because a family member was elected to the school board at some time during the teacher's career. Moreover, N.M. Stat. Ann. §§ 22-10-15, 22-10-17 provided that the refusal to reemploy a tenured teacher or discharge of a certified employee during the contract period had to be based on good and just cause. Accordingly, the teacher was entitled to reinstatement.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the appellate decision and upheld the administrative ruling in favor of the teacher.

 

160 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State v. Aguilar


No. 13169


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


95 N.M. 578; 1981-NMSC-027; 624 P.2d 520; 1981 N.M. LEXIS 2253



February 23, 1981 


PRIOR HISTORY: ORIGINAL PROCEEDING ON CERTIORARI



DISPOSITION: Dismissal reversed, appeal reinstated and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of aggravated assault with a deadly weapon. The trial court ruled that the mandatory incarceration provision of the firearm enhancement statute, N.M. Stat. Ann. § 31-18-16 (1980), was unconstitutional as a violation of the doctrine of separation of powers. The State appealed defendant's sentence. The court of appeals dismissed the appeal on the ground that the State had no right to an appeal. Certiorari was granted.


OVERVIEW: The State acknowledges that it has no statutory right to an appeal under N.M. Stat. Ann. § 39-3-3. However, the State correctly contended that it had a constitutional right to an appeal under N.M. Const. art. VI, § 2. The court held that the State was an "aggrieved party" under the circumstances of the case, with an absolute right to appellate review of that ruling. The holding was limited to the facts of the case and the court cautioned that the State did not have an absolute right to appeal in every situation in which it may feel "aggrieved" by a trial court's ruling. The court's decision was founded upon the State's strong interest in the enforcement of its statutes.


OUTCOME: The dismissal of the State's appeal by the court of appeals was reversed. The State's appeal was reinstated and the cause was remanded to the court of appeals for consideration of the merits of the appeal.

 

161 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State v. Archibeque


No. 12905


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


95 N.M. 411; 1981-NMSC-010; 622 P.2d 1031; 1981 N.M. LEXIS 2248



January 26, 1981 


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF BERNALILLO COUNTY, Joseph F. Baca, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of commercial burglary and sentenced to one to five years in the penitentiary. After he had begun serving this sentence, the State filed a supplemental information charging defendant as an habitual offender, based on four prior felony convictions, and defendant was convicted. The District Court of Bernalillo County (New Mexico) vacated the sentence on the principal offense and imposed a life sentence. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: In regard to the double jeopardy issue raised by defendant, the court cited its own prior decision in an unrelated case, and the addition support of a recent United States Supreme Court decision, in its determination that the habitual offender proceeding was merely a sentencing procedure and, hence, did not involve double jeopardy. On the second issue, the court held that the life sentence that was imposed did not constitute cruel and unusual punishment. The court relied on another United States Supreme Court case in pointing out that the length of the sentence actually imposed was purely a matter of legislative prerogative. Absent a compelling reason, which was not found to be present in the case, the court recognized that the judiciary should not impose its own views concerning the appropriate punishment for crimes.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court.

 

162 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Taxation & Revenue Dep't v. F.W. Woolworth Co.


No. 12876


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


95 N.M. 519; 1981-NMSC-008; 624 P.2d 28; 1981 N.M. LEXIS 2245



January 19, 1981 


PRIOR HISTORY: ORIGINAL PROCEEDING ON CERTIORARI



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner Taxation and Revenue Department of the State of New Mexico (department) challenged the judgment of the Court of Appeals (New Mexico), which reversed the department's assessment of additional corporate income taxes on respondent taxpayer. The department assessed additional taxes because the taxpayer did not add "gross-up" into its state taxable income and deducted cash stock dividends paid to it by its foreign subsidiaries.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer, which sold general merchandise throughout the United States, claimed that the inclusion in gross income of $ 25 million for foreign income taxes paid by its foreign subsidiaries and reported as dividend income on its federal income tax return in order to claim a credit under I.R.C. §§ 78, 901-908, was inequitable; that cash stock dividends paid to it by its subsidiaries were not business income under the Uniform Division of Income for Tax Purposes Act, § 7-4-1 to -21 (1978); that the department's allocation violated the taxpayer's due process rights; and that the department should have modified the apportionment formula. The court reversed the court of appeals' judgment because: (1) the state's piggy-back method for determining taxable income by reference to federal law, N.M. Stat. Ann. § 7-2-2(S) (1978), was constitutional, unambiguous, and not subject to statutory construction; (2) the department's finding that the dividends were business income was supported by substantial evidence, N.M. Stat. Ann. § 7-1-25 (Repl. Pamp. 1979); (3) the court found no due process violation; and (4) the taxpayer failed to prove what modifications of the formula were needed.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the court of appeals and entered judgment for the department that the taxpayer owed additional corporate income taxes due to its failure to include the "gross-up" and cash stock dividends paid to it by its foreign subsidiaries in its state taxable income.

 

163 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Nall v. Baca


No. 12916


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


95 N.M. 783; 1980-NMSC-138; 626 P.2d 1280; 1980 N.M. LEXIS 2762



December 22, 1980 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied January 21, 1981.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF SANTA FE COUNTY, BRUCE E. KAUFMAN, District Judge



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, bar owner and dancer, challenged the judgment of the District Court of Santa Fe County (New Mexico), which denied their request for a declaratory judgment to declare an indecent dancing statute, N.M. Stat. Ann. § 30-9-14.1 (Cum. Supp. 1980), unconstitutional and for injunctive relief.


OVERVIEW: The bar owner was cited by agents of the state liquor director because he employed the dancer to dance nude in his club, a licensed liquor establishment, in violation of § 30-9-14.1. The court held that the prohibition against nude dancing in a licensed liquor establishment by the statute did not violate the free speech provision of N.M. Const. art. II, § 17. The broad powers of the states to regulate the sale of liquor, conferred by U.S. Const. amend. XXI, outweighed any U.S. Const. amend. I interest in nude dancing, and a state could therefore ban such dancing as a part of its liquor license program. The court stated that the statute was severable with regard to its prohibition against indecent dancing in a "public place," because the portion relating to indecent dancing in a licensed liquor establishment was enforceable only by the Director of the Department of Alcoholic Beverage Control through suspension or revocation of the liquor license. The portion prohibiting indecent dancing in any "public place" was enforceable by other law enforcement officials through arrest and prosecution for a misdemeanor.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the district court that the statute prohibiting nude dancing in a licensed liquor establishment did not violate the New Mexico Constitution.

Mowrer v. Rusk

SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO

October 22, 1980 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: October 23, 1980
