CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff judges brought suit against defendants mayor, chief administrative officer, city council, and the city (city), seeking a declaration that they had authority over court employees and could present budgets to the council without executive branch interference. The District Court of Bernalillo County (New Mexico) entered judgment for the judges concerning the employees and for the city on the budget issue. Both parties appealed.


OVERVIEW: The court determined that the legislative enactment, creating the metropolitan court, did not moot the issues presented. The court found § 3-1-13 of the Revised Ordinances of the City of Albuquerque (1974) was unconstitutional as violative of N.M Const. art. III. The court held that the trial court erred in ruling that the discharge of municipal court employees was subject to the merit ordinance of the City of Albuquerque. Furthermore, any municipal ordinance or any portion of any municipal charter, or any statute that required that the judiciary first submit its requested budget to the mayor or any part of the executive branch of government prior to submitting the same to the legislative branch of government was unconstitutional as violative of N.M. Const. Art. III.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's determination that the controversy was not moot, reversed the trial court's ruling concerning the employees, and reversed the trial court's judgment in regards to the budget.

State v. Larson


No. 12721


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


94 N.M. 795; 1980-NMSC-106; 617 P.2d 1310; 1980 N.M. LEXIS 2734



October 17, 1980 


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF BERNALILLO COUNTY, Joseph F. Baca.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the District Court for Bernalillo County (New Mexico), which convicted him of one count of first-degree and two counts of second-degree criminal sexual penetration in violation of N.M. Stat. Ann. § 30-9-11 (1978).


OVERVIEW: Defendant sexually assaulted his 13 year old stepdaughter and his 15 year old sister-in-law. His wife reported the offense to the police and gave police consent to search their home. Among other evidence the police seized numerous photographs, some depicting defendant's sexual activities with the children. In affirming defendant's convictions, the court first held that § 30-9-11 was not unconstitutionally vague for failing to define "penetration" or describe what was unlawful penetration. The court held that no person of ordinary intelligence would not understand which type of conduct was proscribed. The court next held that the wife's consent to search was all that was needed to search the house and that her motivation in consenting was irrelevant. The court then found no error in the prosecutor's reference to pictures other than those admitted at trial, or in the prosecutor's reference to guns found in the home. Finally the court held that N.M. Stat. Ann., R. Crim. P. 47(a) did not vest in defendant a right of absence from trial, and found no error in the denial of his motion to be excused.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions of criminal sexual penetration.

SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO

State v. James


No. 12742


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


94 N.M. 604; 1980-NMSC-082; 614 P.2d 16; 1980 N.M. LEXIS 2703



July 23, 1980 


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF CHAVES COUNTY, PAUL SNEAD, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order of the District Court of Chaves County (New Mexico), which convicted him of conspiracy to commit armed robbery and armed robbery and sentenced him as an habitual offender to two concurrent life sentences.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted and sentenced for conspiracy to commit armed robbery and armed robbery. At the same time, the State filed a supplemental information alleging defendant to be an habitual offender, pursuant to N.M Stat. Ann. § 31-18-5(C). Four felony convictions, one of which was the consolidation of two federal convictions, were found valid. The underlying prison terms were vacated and two concurrent lifetime sentences were imposed. Defendant alleged that § 31-18-5 was unconstitutionally in violation of double jeopardy, that his right to a speedy trial was violated, and that three of the convictions used for enhancement purposes were unusable. The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence, holding that because the habitual offender proceeding was a sentencing procedure and not a trial of an offense, there was no double jeopardy, that because the extensions granted by the trial court were proper, defendant's right to a speedy trial was not violated, and that defendant's prior convictions were properly considered by the trial court in enhancing defendant's sentence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence.

 

168 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Montoya v. O'Toole


No. 12577


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


94 N.M. 303; 1980-NMSC-045; 610 P.2d 190; 1980 N.M. LEXIS 2675



April 10, 1980 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied May 15, 1980.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF BERNALILLO COUNTY WILLIAM R. RIORDAN, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the District Court of Bernalillo County (New Mexico), which denied his petition for writ of prohibition, alleging an unlawful delegation of power under the New Mexico Constitution and a violation of the notice requirement under the due process clause of the United States Constitution. Defendant was charged with a violation of the Controlled Substances Act for possession of the controlled substance, valium.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that to allow the Board of Pharmacy to schedule drugs, resulting in the attachment of differing criminal penalties for the possession of scheduled drugs, was an unconstitutional delegation of authority under the N.M. Const. art. III, § 1. The court disagreed. The legislature could lawfully delegate authority to an administrative agency when that authority was restricted by specific legislative standards. N.M. Stat. Ann. § 30-31-3 did not violate the delegation strictures of the New Mexico Constitution. The legislature established strict guidelines for the Board of Pharmacy to follow in determining a substance's potential for abuse. The standards for the scheduling of dangerous drugs were clear and the duties of the Board were definite. The legislative scheme for designating and scheduling potentially abused drugs allowed the Board of Pharmacy only minimal discretion in its fact-finding function and no discretion in enacting substantive law. The Board's expertise in this field was crucial and its vigilance in dealing with new and dangerous drugs was necessary.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Appelman v. Beach


No. 12199


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


94 N.M. 237; 1980-NMSC-041; 608 P.2d 1119; 1980 N.M. LEXIS 2657



March 21, 1980 


PRIOR HISTORY: IN THE DISTRICT COURT OF BERNALILLO COUNTY, Gerald R. Cole, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a county and its officials, and appellee taxpayer challenged an order of the District Court of Bernalillo County (New Mexico), which held in the taxpayer's action for a property tax refund or for damages for excess taxes and a reduced valuation that N.M. Stat. Ann. § 7-36-17 (1978) was unconstitutional and ordered the county to adequately fund the property reappraisal program under which the taxpayer's realty was reappraised.


OVERVIEW: Appellants alleged that the legislative repeal of N.M. Stat. Ann. § 7-36-17 (1978) rendered the declaration that that statute was unconstitutional moot and the taxpayer argued that her remedy was improper. The court affirmed the district court's judgment, concluding that the legislative action rendered appellants' argument moot and that the taxpayer was not entitled to any damages because the taxes that she paid did not exceed the limit for which the law allowed. The court reasoned that having the county raise the value of the property that the taxpayer claimed was too low to the same level as the amount that she was paying was a valid remedy due to the compliance with N.M. Stat. Ann. § 7-36-15 (1978) as to the reappraisal of the taxpayer's realty at its fair market value and because the assessment was not for more than the law provided. The court also noted that the taxpayer did not claim any fraud nor intentional discrimination as to the manner in which the reassessment program was conducted or the decision to discontinue it due to a lack of resources and that the record did not indicate any well-defined and established scheme of discrimination or fraudulent action.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment in the taxpayer's tax protest action against appellants that the tax statute was unconstitutional and that the county was required to provide adequate funding to complete the property reappraisal program under which the taxpayer's property was reappraised.

Pedrazza v. Sid Fleming Contractor, Inc.


No. 12389


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


94 N.M. 59; 1980-NMSC-018; 607 P.2d 597; 1980 N.M. LEXIS 2656



February 25, 1980

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff mother, on behalf of her children who were residents of the Republic of Mexico, sought review of a judgment from the District Court of Dona Ana County (New Mexico), which dismissed plaintiffs' claim for benefits under the New Mexico Workmen's Compensation Act on the ground that the children were precluded from recovery by N.M. Stat. Ann. § 52-1-52 (1978).


OVERVIEW: The children's father was killed in an accident while employed by defendant employer. The trial court dismissed the complaint because N.M. Stat. Ann. § 52-1-52 prohibited compensation for dependents who were not residents of the United States. The court affirmed the judgment, rejecting plaintiffs' contention that § 52-1-52 violated the due process and equal protection clauses of the state and federal constitutions. The court found no law stating that workmen's compensation was ranked as a fundamental right within the constitutional framework. The court also found that the New Mexico legislature conferred no due process property right upon plaintiffs that the trial court could have violated by dismissing plaintiffs' suit. Additionally, the court concluded that plaintiffs, as residents of the Republic of Mexico, were beyond the protective reach of the equal protection clause and outside of the court's ability to help their cause on constitutional grounds. Therefore, the court determined that plaintiffs' non-resident alien status prevented them from recovering death benefits under the Act.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

In re A Motion for a Subpoena Duces Tecum to Issue to the Custodian of the Records of the Governor's Organized Crime Prevention Comm'n


No. 12818


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


94 N.M. 1; 1980-NMSC-010; 606 P.2d 539; 1980 N.M. LEXIS 2636



January 28, 1980 


PRIOR HISTORY: ORIGINAL PROCEEDING



DISPOSITION: IT IS SO ORDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The action was commenced as an original proceeding in the New Mexico Supreme Court through the filing of a Motion for Issuance of a Subpoena Duces Tecum to the Governor's Organized Crime Prevention Commission. The questions on review were whether N.M. Stat. Ann. § 29-9-8(B)(1978) was constitutional and which court would have jurisdiction to entertain the motion.


OVERVIEW: The parties were asked to submit briefs on the constitutionality of N.M. Stat. Ann. § 29-9-8(B)(1978) in light of the provisions of N.M. Const. art. VII, §§ 2 and 3. The parties were also asked what court, if any, had jurisdiction to rule on the motion for issuance of a subpoena duces tecum to the Commission if the statute was constitutional. On review, the court determined that the last sentence in § 29-9-8(B) was severable but that the remainder of the Organized Crime Act (Act) remained in full force and effect. The court found that under the court's power of superintending control, and in this particular case, the district courts were authorized and directed, upon proper application for a subpoena duces tecum under N.M. Stat. Ann. R. Civ. P. 45 (1978), to hear and determine whether the records, reports and files of the Commission could be subpoenaed. If the district court ordered that a subpoena duces tecum be issued, the district court was directed to hold an in camera hearing to determine which records, reports and files of the Commission should be produced.


OUTCOME: The district courts were authorized and directed, upon proper application for a subpoena duces tecum, to hear and determine whether the records, reports and files of the Governor's Organized Crime Prevention Commission could be subpoenaed, and if so, upon what conditions.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the District Court of Curry County (New Mexico), which convicted and sentenced him to life as a four-time felony offender under the Habitual Offender Statute, N.M. Stat. § 31-18-5.


OVERVIEW: The trial court convicted defendant and sentenced him to life as a four-time felony offender under the Habitual Offender Statute, N.M. Stat. § 31-18-5. On appeal, the court determined that the evidence and findings in the case could sustain defendant's sentence only as a three-time felony offender, but not as a four-time felony offender. On the other hand, if no new trial was had, the court found that the findings of the jury supported a sentence against defendant as a three-time felony offender.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was reversed and remanded for further proceedings.

Stuckey's Stores, Inc. v. O'Cheskey


No. 11946


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


93 N.M. 312; 1979-NMSC-060; 600 P.2d 258; 1979 N.M. LEXIS 1242; 13 ERC (BNA) 1673



August 6, 1979 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied September 11, 1979.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF SANTA FE COUNTY, Santiago E. Campos, District Judge



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant advertiser sought review of a judgment of the District Court of Santa Fe County (New Mexico), which, after a jury trial, found the New Mexico Highway Beautification Act, N.M. Stat. Ann. §§ 66-12-1 to 14, was a constitutional exercise of police power and did not deny the advertiser due process of law or freedom of speech.


OVERVIEW: The advertiser brought an action against the state highway administrator after the state passed the New Mexico Highway Beautification Act (Act), N.M. Stat. Ann. §§ 66-12-1 to 14, restricting outdoor advertising structures. On review, the court affirmed in part but required some compensation for some signs that were removed. The court held that the Act did not regulate the advertising on the basis of its content nor did it completely prevent the dissemination of the same information by alternative means. The Act restricted commercial, rather than political or ideological, speech. Thus, the Act met the three-pronged test used to determine whether a time, place, and manner restriction was valid. The Act's restrictions on advertisers' exercise of their freedom of speech was justified without reference to the content of the regulated speech. None of the Act's stated purposes, promotion of public safety, health, welfare, convenience and enjoyment of public travel, protection of public investment in public highways, and preservation and enhancement of the scenic beauty of lands bordering the public highways, were related to a particular message of such signs. N.M. Stat. Ann. § 67-12-3.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the district court, in part, in its finding that the New Mexico Highway Beautification Act was a legitimate exercise of the state's police power but reversed in part and remanded where some of the signs were not subject to removal without just compensation.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner optometrist appealed a decision from the District Court of Santa Fe County (New Mexico), which affirmed respondent New Mexico Board of Examiners in Optometry's (board) revocation of the optometrist's license to practice after denying his motions to disqualify first one member of the board for bias, then denying his motions to disqualify the entire board and to dismiss the proceedings.


OVERVIEW: Upon receipt of a complaint of sexual advances against patients, in violation of N.M. Stat. Ann. § 61-2-8(B), the board brought disciplinary proceedings against the optometrist. Ernest W. Hahn, Inc. v. County Assessor


No. 12030


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


92 N.M. 609; 1978-NMSC-094; 592 P.2d 965; 1978 N.M. LEXIS 989



December 11, 1978 



DISPOSITION:  Reversed and remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayers sought review of a judgment of the Court of Appeals (New Mexico) that affirmed a judgment of a county valuation protest board that, on remand, denied the taxpayer's protest of notices of valuation of the taxpayer's property that were received from respondent county assessor.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers protested notices of valuation received from the assessor. After judgment in favor of the assessor and remand, the protests were denied. On further appeal, the court reversed, holding that the appeal was not barred by the doctrine of res judicata. Because the taxpayers' properties were reappraised every year, while over 90 percent of the land in the county had not been subjected to even a single reappraisal, the court concluded that the reappraisal was done in a systematically discriminatory manner. The taxpayers were singled out for selective enforcement of tax laws. Because of the absence of any systematic and definite plan for reappraisal of all lands, the assessment violated N.M. Const. art. VIII, § 1 and N.M. Const. art. II, § 18. The court found that the taxpayers were entitled to a reduction in their assessment to a level that would achieve the practical uniformity required by the constitution. The cause was remanded to the valuation protest board to determine the proper ratio to achieve practical uniformity.


OUTCOME: The decision of the Court of Appeals was reversed and the cause was remanded.

Torres v. Village of Capitan


No. 11567


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


92 N.M. 64; 1978-NMSC-065; 582 P.2d 1277; 1978 N.M. LEXIS 956



August 9, 1978 



DISPOSITION:  Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, owners of an area to be annexed, appealed the denial by the Lincoln County District Court (New Mexico), of their motion for summary judgment against defendants, village and village trustees, in an action seeking to invalidate an annexation of contiguous land by the village. The district court entered judgment on a stipulated record in favor of the village.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs brought an action against defendants seeking to invalidate an annexation of contiguous land. The district court entered judgment on a stipulated record in favor of the village. The court affirmed, holding that res judicata did not apply because the subject matter of the prior and current suits was not simply the land involved, but the two different attempts to annex the same land. The court held that the judge's holding in the first case that N.M. Stat. Ann. § 14-7-17 (1953) was unconstitutional, was a conclusion purely of law, and was not collaterally binding on the judge in a second case between the same parties or privies. The court held that the village was not collaterally estopped to assert that § 14-7-17 was constitutional in the second suit. Because § 14-7-17 did not involve elections and did not infringe upon the fundamental right to vote, the court applied minimum scrutiny and held that discrimination or inequality would not be set aside if any state of facts were reasonably conceived to justify it. The court found that apportionment of taxes was a rational basis for the annexation and that § 14-7-17 was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed and held the judgment of the district court, which denied plaintiffs motion for summary judgment in their action regarding the annexation of contiguous land.

 

179 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Humana of N.M., Inc. v. Bd. of County Comm'rs


No. 11599


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


92 N.M. 34; 1978-NMSC-036; 582 P.2d 806; 1978 N.M. LEXIS 950



May 9, 1978 



DISPOSITION:  Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff hospital brought a declaratory judgment action against defendant board of county commissioners for a determination of the rights and responsibilities of the hospital and the board under the Indigent Hospital Claims Act (Act), N.M. Stat. Ann. §§ 13-2-12 et seq. (Repl. 1976). The trial court (New Mexico) found that N.M. Stat. Ann. § 13-2-15(B) (Repl. 1976) violated N. M. Const. art. IX, § 14. The hospital appealed.


OVERVIEW: The hospital's dispute with the board revolved around the board's alleged failure to pay indigent claims as required by the Act. The trial court determined that the portion of the Act that provided for counties to pay hospital claims for "indigent patients" as defined by the Act violated N.M. Const. art. IX, § 14 and that the definition of "indigent patient" was vague and overbroad. Reversing the trial court's judgment, the court found that contemporaneous construction of § 14 was proper because the term "poor" in 1912 may have meant penniless, but in 1978 had to include persons on welfare who barely eked out an existence. Thus, the court held that the legislature's definition of "indigent patient" in N.M. Stat. Ann. § 13-2-15(B) was not unconstitutional under N.M. Const. art. IX, § 14, nor was it vague or overbroad.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment, which found the statutory definition of "indigent patient" unconstitutional, and remanded for further proceedings.

 

180 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Governor's Organized Crime Prevention Comm'n v. Jaramillo (In re Investigation No. 2 of the Governor&apos;s Organized Crime Prevention Comm')


No. 11635


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


91 N.M. 516; 1978-NMSC-022; 577 P.2d 414; 1978 N.M. LEXIS 919



March 21, 1978 



DISPOSITION:  Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant State Liquor Director challenged an order from the trial court (New Mexico), which denied the Director's motion to quash a subpoena duces tecum issued by appellee Governor's Organized Crime Prevention Commission pursuant to the Organized Crime Act, N.M. Stat. § 39-1-1 et seq., in an investigation to determine whether the liquor industry had been infiltrated by organized crime. The Director argued that the Act was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The Commission issued a subpoena duces tecum for bank records covering loans and accounts belonging to the Director, pursuant to the Organized Crime Act, N.M. Stat. § 39-1-1 et seq. The Commission was conducting an investigation to determine whether the liquor industry had been infiltrated by organized crime. The Director filed a motion to quash the subpoena, which was denied. The Director appealed and contended that U.S. Const. amends. IV, XIV, required a showing of probable cause before business records could be subpoenaed. The court affirmed the judgment and held that the Commission was an investigatory rather than an accusatory body and that its subpoenas were administrative and not subject to search and seizure protections of the Fourth Amendment. The trial court properly determined that the subpoena was sufficiently limited in scope and that the material sought was relevant. The court rejected the Director's argument that the Act was unconstitutionally vague. The Act was not penal and not amenable to a claim of vagueness. The court also held that the Act did not violate N.M. Const. art. IV, § 16, because the word "racketeering" was not required to appear in the title.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

181 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Kepler v. Covarrubia


No. 11637


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


91 N.M. 443; 1978-NMSC-019; 575 P.2d 952; 1978 N.M. LEXIS 906



March 15, 1978 



DISPOSITION:  Remanded with instructions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landowner challenged a judgment from the trial court (New Mexico), granting abatement of rent to appellee resident. The landowner contended that N.M. Stat. Ann. § 70-7-27 B (1975) was unconstitutionally vague and that the tenant had failed to give notice of any breach.


OVERVIEW: The landowner sought recovery of unpaid rent, and the resident sought damages and abatement. The trial court found that the landowner had actual notice of the deficiencies claimed, absent any evidence of written notice. The resident did not appear and testify, and the only testimony was that of the landowner that he did not receive written notice. The landowner requested a finding of fact that the resident did not serve any written notice as required by § 70-7-29, and the trial court did not make such findings. On appeal the court held that the trial court erred by not making such a finding and reversed the judgment. Because N.M. Stat. Ann. § 70-7-29 (1975) required written notice for abatement of rent, the trial court had erred. The court rejected the landowner's claim that N.M. Stat. Ann. § 70-7-27 B (1975) was unconstitutionally vague, reasoning that because the statute distinguished between willful acts as opposed to conditions beyond his control, and defined what damages could be recovered, the statute was sufficiently clear to meet the test of constitutionality.


OUTCOME: The court remanded the case with directions that the judgment be reversed.

 

182 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State v. Favela


No. 11822


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


91 N.M. 476; 1978-NMSC-010; 576 P.2d 282; 1978 N.M. LEXIS 908



February 17, 1978 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied March 28, 1978.



DISPOSITION: Trial court's denial of motion to dismiss affirmed; cause remanded for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On its own motion, the court issued a writ of certiorari to review a decision of the Court of Appeals (New Mexico), which reversed a trial court decision denying defendant's motion to dismiss the indictment and charge for contributing to the delinquency of a minor under N.M. Stat. Ann. § 40A-6-3.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, a female adult, was charged with contributing to the delinquency of a minor, in violation of N.M. Stat. Ann. §40A-6-3, by reason of sexual intercourse with a fifteen year old boy, who allegedly consented to the act. The trial court denied defendant's motion to dismiss the indictment and she took an interlocutory appeal. The Court of Appeals reversed. The court, on its own motion issued a writ of certiorari under authority of N.M. Const. art. 6, § 3. The court found that the appellate court erroneously determined that the definition section of the Children's Code, N.M. Stat. Ann. §13-14-3, and N.M. Stat. Ann. § 40A-6-3 had to be construed together. The court of appeals noted that the juvenile did not commit a delinquent act. The court held that § 13-14-3 applied only to children less than 18 years of age and was intended to protect children from the consequences of their own acts, so longs as it was consistent with protection of the public interest. It established a system of treatment for children who have committed delinquent acts or were neglected. Conversely, N.M. Stat. Ann. § 40A-6-3 applied to adults and was designed to protect kids from harmful adult conduct.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment and remanded for further proceedings.

 

183 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Bird v. Apodaca


No. 11707


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


91 N.M. 279; 1977-NMSC-110; 573 P.2d 213; 1977 N.M. LEXIS 1117



December 28, 1977 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied January 10, 1978.



DISPOSITION: Therefore, we hold that the petitioner is not subject to the transfer provisions of § 5-4-3, supra, and a writ of mandamus will issue ordering respondent to cease, desist and refrain from removing or transferring petitioner Bird or from interfering with the petitioner's performance of his duties as State Highway Engineer contrary to the laws of the State of New Mexico.

IT IS SO ORDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner State Highway Engineer (engineer) brought a mandamus proceeding seeking an order directing respondent governor to refrain from transferring the engineer. The governor sought to transfer the engineer to the State Parks and Recreation Commission under N.M. Stat. Ann. § 5-4-3 (1953). The engineer argued that the governor lacked the power to effect the transfer and that he was not subject to § 5-4-3.


OVERVIEW: The governor argued that mandamus was not the proper remedy because the issue to be resolved was based solely upon the judgment and discretion of the executive officer, and mandamus could not lie to interfere with the exercise of discretion. The governor argued that the relief requested was actually a matter for a writ or prohibition or injunction, and prohibition could not lie against a state officer. The court held that the threshold question was whether mandamus was the proper remedy and whether the court was the proper place in which to bring the action. The court held that the petition was properly styled mandamus, and the requested relief was within the scope of the mandamus remedy. The court held that the engineer was being deprived of the duties, responsibilities, and authority he was given by law when he was properly appointed to his position. Thus, the court found it apparent that no plain, speedy, or adequate remedy, other than mandamus, existed whereby his rights could be protected. The court held that § 5-4-3 did not apply to the engineer.


OUTCOME: The court held that the engineer was not subject to transfer and that a writ of mandamus would issue ordering the governor to cease, desist, and refrain from removing or transferring the engineer or from interfering with the performance of his duties.

 

184 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Keiderling v. Sanchez


Nos. 11518, 11519, 11631, 11679, 11683


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


91 N.M. 198; 1977-NMSC-103; 572 P.2d 545; 1977 N.M. LEXIS 1109



December 14, 1977 



DISPOSITION:  Application for writ of prohibition denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner applied for a writ of prohibition directed to respondent, a judge of the Second Judicial District Court (New Mexico) for failure to honor an attempted disqualification, pursuant to N.M. Stat. Ann. § 21-5-8 (Inter. Supp. 1976-1977), as amended by 1977 N.M. Laws, ch. 165, § 2.


OVERVIEW: The disqualification statute, N.M. Stat. Ann. § 21-5-8 (Inter. Supp. 1976-1977), had been amended in 1977 N.M. Laws, ch. 165, § 2, to provide, in § 21-5-8(B), that litigants before the Second Judicial District Court had the right to disqualify three judges, while under § 21-5-8(A) litigants in other districts had the right to disqualify only one. On review, the court denied petitioner's application for a writ of prohibition against the judge. The court found that the ultimate effect of § 21-5-8 was that different rights accrued to the class of litigants in district courts, depending upon where cases were filed, without regard to changing conditions that might develop in the future. The court thus held that § 21-5-8 was a special law, which was prohibited under N.M. Const. art. IV, § 24. The court ruled that petitioner had not shown that a general law could not have been enacted which gave ever member of the class the same status as litigants in the second district. The court applied its holding only to N.M. Stat. Ann. § 21-5-8(B), which it found to be severable.


OUTCOME: The court denied the writ of prohibition.

 

185 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Nat'l Adver. Co. v. State ex rel. N.M. State Highway Comm'n


No. 11147


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


91 N.M. 191; 1977-NMSC-101; 571 P.2d 1194; 1977 N.M. LEXIS 1108



December 8, 1977 



DISPOSITION:  Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The District Court, Tenth Judicial District (New Mexico) entered summary judgment for defendants, the state, the state highway commission, and the state highway department, in a declaratory judgment action commenced by plaintiff sign company (company) seeking, inter alia, compensation for the value of their signs removed pursuant to the State Highway Beautification Act (act). The company appealed.


OVERVIEW: The sign company had contended that if their signs were not compensable under the act, then the act was unconstitutional as applied to them. The trial court found that the signs erected by the company could have only been compensable if they fell within one of the exceptions provided for in N.M. Stat. Ann. § 55-11-4 and that its signs failed to conform to any of those exceptions. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment in a memorandum opinion filed earlier. When both parties petitioned for rehearing, the court substituted this opinion for the memorandum opinion. The court affirmed. The court found that the act was constitutional (1) because property was subject to the fair exercise of the state's police power; and (2) reasonable regulations, enacted for the benefit of the public health, safety, or general welfare, were not unconstitutional. The court further found that the state was not equitably estopped from denying compensation to the company for the removal of its signs because the evidence showed that the company recognized language on certain permits stating that the permits could be revoked at any time and the signs removed at the owners' expense.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment for the state. The court, in its opinion replacing a prior memorandum opinion, stated that the act was constitutional and that the state was not equitably estopped from denying the company compensation for removal of its signs, pursuant to the act.

State v. Corp. of Abiquiu Tierra Amarilla Land Grant


No. 10939


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


91 N.M. 187; 1977-NMSC-100; 571 P.2d 1190; 1977 N.M. LEXIS 1107



December 7, 1977 



DISPOSITION:  Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a corporation and certain of its officers, sought review of a judgment from the trial court (New Mexico), which found defendants in contempt of court due to violations of an injunction obtained by appellee State restraining defendants from performing certain acts which were in contravention of the rights of plaintiff record owners of lands within the Tierra Amarilla Land Grant.


OVERVIEW: Defendants claimed title to the lands based on the Treaty of Guadalupe-Hidalgo and certain hijuelas stemming from the treaty. Defendants contended that the injunction was void for being vague and overbroad and that there was no substantial evidence to support the trial court's finding that defendants were in contempt of court for violating the injunction. The court affirmed the decision, finding that defendants were not found in contempt of court for asserting protected rights. Instead, defendants were found to have completely disregarded a court order that prohibited them from interfering with plaintiffs' quiet enjoyment. The court determined that the injunction set forth the proscribed acts in language that was neither vague nor uncertain. It was capable of being read and understood by persons of common intelligence. Finally, the court found that the trial court's findings in support of its contempt order were supported by substantial evidence because the evidence relied upon by the trial court in making its findings was relevant, probative, and sufficient to satisfy a reasonable mind of its truth. Thus, the conclusions reached were reasonable and not based on conjecture.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision.

Espanola Hous. Auth. v. Atencio


No. 11514


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


90 N.M. 787; 1977-NMSC-074; 568 P.2d 1233; 1977 N.M. LEXIS 1081



September 12, 1977 



DISPOSITION:  Decision of Court of Appeals reversed and order of District Court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, a city, a housing authority, and a manufacturer, sought certiorari review of a decision entered in the Court of Appeals (New Mexico), which reversed a district court judgment in respondents' personal injury action and found that N.M. Stat. Ann. § 23-1-23 was unconstitutional on equal protection grounds. Respondents included an injured minor and those suing on her behalf.


OVERVIEW: The minor was allegedly injured on a merry-go-round owned by the city's housing authority. The suit to recover for her injuries was brought nearly three years later. The city and housing authority asserted the affirmative defense of statute of limitations. The district court dismissed the case, and the minor appealed, challenging the constitutionality of N.M. Stat. Ann. § 23-1-23. The minor asserted that N.M. Stat. Ann. § 23-1-23 and its one-year statute of limitation denied the victims of municipal torts equal protection because it was inconsistent with N.M. Stat. Ann. § 23-1-8, which had a three-year limitation period against private tortfeasors. The court of appeals reversed and found that the statute was unconstitutional. On review, the court stressed that, if the one-time limitations for filing in the statute were applicable, the proceedings were properly terminated. The court held that there was a rational basis for limiting the time period in which suit could be brought against the city because the it narrowed exposure for determining insurance rates, the city was limited in its ability to raise taxes and funds, and the city had a greater need to know what claims it faced.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the court of appeals and affirmed the district court's order dismissing the complaint.

 

188 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Schanefelt v. Paradiso (In re Will of Brooks)


No. 10312


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


90 N.M. 760; 1977-NMSC-072; 568 P.2d 596; 1977 N.M. LEXIS 1079



September 7, 1977 



DISPOSITION:  Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On remand from the United States Supreme Court, the court reviewed a judgment of the district court, which sat in probate as provided by law and found that appellant heir did not have standing to challenge a will pursuant to N.M. Stat. Ann. § 30-2-13 (1953). By her will, the testator bequeathed and devised all of her estate to appellee, a stranger, who was not an heir.


OVERVIEW: The heir, who was the daughter of the brother of the testator's deceased husband, sought to contest the testator's last will and testament. The will bequeathed the testator's entire estate to the stranger. The district court granted judgment in the stranger's favor. The court affirmed, but the U.S. Supreme Court remanded the case to the court for further consideration. Thereafter, the court reversed and remanded. The heir claimed that she was an interested person who had a right to challenge the will under § 30-2-13. She further claimed that under a literal reading of N.M. Stat. Ann. §§ 29-1-13, 29-1-14 and 29-1-15, heirs of a predeceased husband were discriminated against on the basis of gender. The court found that there was no constitutional violation. The court held that although the language of N.M. Stat. Ann. § 29-1-13 was phrased exclusively in terms of the male intestate, the case law indicated that the statute applied equally to a spouse of either sex who died intestate and without issue. Thus, the heirs of a predeceased male spouse were not excluded from the unified scheme. The heir had the right to challenge the will.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded.

Southwest Distrib. Co. v. Olympia Brewing Co.

SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO

June 27, 1977 



DISPOSITION:  Reversed and remanded.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant supplier sought review of the judgment of the trial court (New Mexico) that permanently enjoined the supplier from terminating a distribution agreement with appellee distributor.


OVERVIEW: The distributor had an informal oral agreement with the supplier's predecessor that it was to have been a distributor of a particular type of beer in the New Mexico market. After the supplier purchased the assets of the predecessor, it terminated the relationship with the distributor, and the distributor commenced an action seeking an injunction requiring the supplier to supply and sell beer to the distributor for resale throughout New Mexico. The trial court granted the injunction, and the court reversed and remanded. The court held that the distributor had no vested property right in the distribution agreement and that the supplier had not assumed the obligations of the agreement when it purchased the assets.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the judgment enjoining the supplier from terminating a distribution agreement with the distributor.

 

190 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Santa Fe v. Velarde


Nos. 11084, 11091


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


90 N.M. 444; 1977-NMSC-040; 564 P.2d 1326; 1977 N.M. LEXIS 1048



May 23, 1977 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied June 8, 1977.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded with instructions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant applicants challenged a judgment from the Santa Fe County District Court (New Mexico), which granted appellee city's motion for summary judgment on the grounds of res judicata and collateral estoppel predicated on an order dismissing a previous case with prejudice. The city, in its corporate and proprietary capacities, had brought suit against the applicants to quiet title to certain property.


OVERVIEW: In the first case, the applicant claimed to own in fee simple and have actual possession of certain lands, and sought a quitclaim deed from the city, which filed a motion to dismiss challenging the trial court's jurisdiction, the applicant's standing, the claim's sufficiency, and lack of an indispensable party. The trial court entered an order dismissing the complaint with prejudice unless the applicant, within 20 days, amended and sought mandamus or quiet title. Although both cases involved some or all of the same land, the applicant was plaintiff in the first case and defendant in the second and the dismissal was with prejudice, such factors did not meet the test to apply res judicata or collateral estoppel by judgment. The court held that the applicant's chance to amend his pleadings did not make the causes of action identical. The court pointed out that the rule that a prior final decision determined not only what was in issue but also what might have been in issue contemplated existing identical causes of action and not what the causes of action might have been after theoretical amendments to the pleadings which were never made. The judgment was reversed and remanded.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the trial court's judgment with instructions to overrule the city's motion for summary judgment against the applicants for a quitclaim deed and to proceed with the case.

 

191 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Mt. States Tel. & Tel. Co. v. N.M. State Corp. Comm'n


No. 10983


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


90 N.M. 325; 1977-NMSC-032; 563 P.2d 588; 1977 N.M. LEXIS 1039



April 20, 1977 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied May 11, 1977.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded with instructions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner telephone and telegraph company sought review of a judgment from respondent state corporation commission (New Mexico), which denied a petition for an even-percentage increase in rates or for the commission to fix reasonable rates. The telephone company sought an increase in revenues in an action opposed by intervenor retail association.


OVERVIEW: The state corporation commission entered an order that the telephone company was entitled to a 12 percent rate of return on its average book equity, and the company filed proposed rates based on the order. The retail association intervened, and the commission refused to approve the proposed rates. On review, the court reversed and ordered the cause remanded. The court held that the state commission did not have a constitutional duty to provide the revue based on its prior order and was not required by N.M. Const. art. 11, § 8 to adjust the schedule of rates within six months. The court also held, however, that the denial of the motion to allow the new rates to take effect during the period was violative of U.S. Const. amend. XIV and N.M. Const. art. 2, § 20 prohibiting public confiscation of private property without just compensation. The court further stated that the commission erred in holding that the company did not satisfy its burden of proof that the proposed rates were just and reasonable. The court directed the state commission to fix a permanent schedule of rates and held that it was required to consider the most recent data in establishing the rate base period.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the judgment of the state corporation commission, which denied the telephone and telegraph company's petition for an even-percentage increase in rates or for the state commission to fix reasonable rates in the action opposed by the retail association.

 

192 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Navajo Freight Lines, Inc. v. Baldonado


No. 11268


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


90 N.M. 264; 1977-NMSC-025; 562 P.2d 497; 1977 N.M. LEXIS 1032



April 6, 1977 



DISPOSITION:  Decision of Court of Appeals reversed and cause remanded to district court for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, truck owner and operator, sought review of an order from the Court of Appeals (New Mexico), which affirmed the trial court's dismissal of their third-party complaint against respondent driver. The dismissal was based on the New Mexico guest statute.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff individual was injured in an automobile and truck accident. He was a passenger in the driver's car. He filed suit against the petitioners for his injuries. They filed a third-party complaint against the driver for contribution and property damage, and the operator also sought damages for personal injuries. The third-party complaint was based on the theory that the New Mexico guest statute was no longer applicable because it had been declared unconstitutional by the New Mexico Supreme Court. The trial court held that the guest statute did apply and dismissed the third-party complaint. Upon review, the court reversed. The Supreme Court had declared its decision was given a modified prospectivity. The court found that the decision applied to all civil actions in which the complaint was filed after the Supreme Court's decision. The individual filed his action after the decision was handed down. Thus, the guest statute was not applicable. The petitioners' claims for property damage and personal injuries were properly joined because they arose out of the same operative facts as the individual's claims.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the dismissal of petitioners' third-party complaint for property damage and personal injuries. The court found that the parties were properly joined and remanded the action for further proceedings.

 

193 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State v. Cessna Int'l Fin. Corp. (In re One Cessna Aircraft)


No. 11026


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


90 N.M. 40; 1977-NMSC-007; 559 P.2d 417; 1977 N.M. LEXIS 1122



January 28, 1977 



DISPOSITION:  Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, an owner of an airplane, a secured creditor finance company and an alleged secured party, challenged an order from the trial court (New Mexico), which entered judgment in favor of respondent, the State, and allowed the State to seize the airplane free and clear of the interest of any party pursuant to the forfeiture provisions of the Controlled Substances Act, N.M. Stat. Ann. § 54-11-33 et seq. (Supp. 1975).


OVERVIEW: An airplane was found containing 580 pounds of marijuana. Appellant owner of the aircraft claimed due process violations and the finance company and the alleged secured creditor claimed security interests in the plane. The State seized the plane and sought a foreclosure and a declaration that the State was entitled to the plane free and clear of the interest of any party. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment as to the owner of the aircraft and the alleged secured creditor, but reversed as to the finance company. The claimed constitutional errors of appellant owner were without merit. The statute provided for a hearing within 30 days of the seizure, which was sufficient to satisfy due process standards. There was also substantial evidence to support the trial court's finding of probable cause for the search and seizure. However, the finance company admitted in its answer and introduced documentary and testamentary evidence of its security interest. The court held that the forfeiture of a vehicle under the Act was subject to the security interests of an innocent third party; therefore, the trial court erred in not recognizing the finance company's security interest.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment as to appellants, the owner of the aircraft and an alleged secured creditor. However, the court reversed the judgment as to appellant finance company.

 

194 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State v. Valenzuela


No. 10674


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


90 N.M. 25; 1976-NMSC-079; 559 P.2d 402; 1976 N.M. LEXIS 865



December 6, 1976 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied December 27, 1976.



DISPOSITION: Ordered in accordance with opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment of the District Court of Chaves County (New Mexico), entered after a jury trial, that convicted him of murder in the first degree for the killing of his wife. He was sentenced to death and his motion for a new trial was denied.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, an itinerant farm worker, shot his wife. The court affirmed the guilty verdict but reversed the death sentence, holding that because of recent United States Supreme Court decisions, the penalty to be imposed was life imprisonment. No jury determination of defendant's competency was required because the trial court correctly found that he was competent. Defendant's motion to suppress certain statements was properly denied because Miranda warnings were properly given. Admission of photographs of the deceased was not an abuse of discretion. Defendant's counsel was not prevented from using the word "malice" in his closing argument. The Uniform Jury Instructions-Criminal were properly used even though the information was filed before the date on which their use became mandatory. Defendant's objection to a combined instruction on intoxication and diminished responsibility was not preserved. N.M. Stat. Ann. § 40A-2-1 (1972) was not unconstitutional because the distinction between first and second degree murder was clearly drawn. The trial court did not err in refusing to instruct the jury on insanity because defendant did not establish that he suffered from a mental disease.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the verdict that found defendant guilty, but it reversed the judgment and sentence of the trial court imposing the death penalty. The action was remanded for the purpose of sentencing defendant to life imprisonment.

 

195 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State v. Hicks


No. 10475


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


89 N.M. 568; 1976-NMSC-069; 555 P.2d 689; 1976 N.M. LEXIS 841



October 26, 1976 



DISPOSITION:  Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision from the District Court of Bernalillo County (New Mexico), which convicted him of first degree murder and sentenced him to death under the mandatory provisions of N.M. Stat. Ann. § 40A-2902 (Supp. 1975). The defendant contended that the trial court committed various errors including imposition of the death penalty and failure to suppress the defendant's statements.


OVERVIEW: The defendant was charged with murdering a man who was found in the defendant's motel room beaten, tied, gagged, and strangled with an electric cord. While under arrest in Arizona on unrelated charges, the defendant was questioned by New Mexico police. He admitted to meeting the victim at a bar, inviting him to his motel room, fighting, tying and gagging him. The defendant was indicted on an "open" charge of murder. At trial, the defendant filed a motion to suppress his admissions. The trial court denied the motion. The defendant was convicted of first degree murder and sentenced to death. On appeal, the court reversed the trial court's decision. The court held that: (1) the penalty to be imposed for a first degree felony was life imprisonment; (2) before the defendant could be convicted of felony murder, he was entitled to be given notice of the precise felony with which he was being charged; (3) a jury instruction was incomplete and constituted error where it permitted jury to find guilt of first degree murder based upon implied malice; but (4) the defendant's admissions were admissible where his statements were taken two days after his arrest after being warned of his rights.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the trial court, which convicted the defendant of first degree murder and sentenced him to death. The court remanded the case for a new trial.

 

196 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Eastham v. Public Emples. Ret. Ass'n Bd.


No. 10322


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


89 N.M. 399; 1976-NMSC-046; 553 P.2d 679; 1976 N.M. LEXIS 818



August 23, 1976 



DISPOSITION:  Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff members sought review of the judgment from the District Court of Santa Fe County (New Mexico) that found in favor of defendant former legislators in the members' action seeking to declare the Legislative Retirement Act unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The members, claiming membership in the Public Employees' Retirement Association under the Legislative Retirement Act, N.M. Stat. Ann. § 5-5-6.1 (1953), sought to declare the Legislative Retirement Act unconstitutional. The trial court found that the members lacked standing and that certain indispensable parties were not joined as defendants. In affirming, the court held that the trial court was correct in holding that procedural due process required notice to other members of the class whose rights would be affected. The court further held that the members had no standing to file the action as potential retirees under the program, nor did they have standing as citizens and taxpayers. Accordingly, the action was properly dismissed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment from the trial court that found in favor of the former legislators in the members' action to declare the Legislative Retirement Act unconstitutional.

 

197 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State v. Rondeau


Nos. 10273, 10262


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


89 N.M. 408; 1976-NMSC-044; 553 P.2d 688; 1976 N.M. LEXIS 820



August 20, 1976 



DISPOSITION:  Convictions affirmed; imposition of death penalty reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, one and two, sought review of their convictions in the District Court of Bernalillo County (New Mexico) of the charges of first degree murder and robbery while armed with a deadly weapon. After appellants' review was docketed, the case was remanded to the trial court for consideration of their motion for a new trial based on newly discovered evidence. The trial court denied their motion.


OVERVIEW: Appellants challenged their convictions in the trial court of the charges of first degree murder and robbery while armed with a deadly weapon, and asserted that their death sentences under N.M. Stat. Ann. § 40A-29-2 (Supp. 1975) constituted cruel and unusual punishment. The court affirmed appellants' convictions, but remanded for resentencing. The court found that mandatory death sentences that left neither the trial court nor jury with the discretion to impose lesser sentences violated the U.S. Const. amend. VIII prohibition against cruel and unusual punishment. The court determined that the legislature's enactment of N.M. Stat. Ann. § 40A-29-2 (Supp. 1975) was an impermissible response to the capriciousness that previously existed in the imposition of the death penalty. The court held that the former statutes were revived because their revival would not run contrary to the legislature's intent to punish the crimes for which appellants were convicted. The court noted that the revived § 40-29-2 left the recommendation of life imprisonment or death to the unbridled discretion of the jury. The court held that substantial evidence supported their convictions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellants' conviction because there was sufficient evidence to support their convictions, but remanded the case for resentencing because the death penalty statute was declared to have been unconstitutional.

 

198 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Ammerman v. Hubbard Broad., Inc.


No. 10937


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


89 N.M. 307; 1976-NMSC-031; 551 P.2d 1354; 1976 N.M. LEXIS 812



June 29, 1976 



DISPOSITION:  Appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant broadcasters sought review of a decision of a trial court (New Mexico), which ordered them, pursuant to N.M. Stat. Ann. § 20-1-12.1, to disclose the names of all of their claimed confidential informants and to produce all information they received from their such informants to plaintiff slandered individuals. The individuals sought to have the appeal dismissed on the ground that N.M. Stat. Ann. § 20-1-12.1(C) was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The individuals sought recovery for alleged slanderous radio broadcasts, news reports, or newscasts. The privilege claimed by the broadcasters under N.M. Stat. Ann. § 20-1-12.1(A) directly conflicted with N.M. R. Evid. 501 and the review procedures provided by N.M. Stat. Ann. § 20-1-12.1(C), pursuant to which the broadcasters' appeal was taken, were inconsistent with the rules for appellate procedure. Dismissing the appeal, the court held that the privilege against disclosure created by the legislature in N.M. Stat. Ann. § 20-1-12.1(A) was not available in a judicial proceeding. The court reasoned that a privilege was a rule of evidence and that the legislature lacked power to prescribe by statute rules of evidence and procedure as such power was constitutionally vested exclusively in the court. The court also found that the review provided for in N.M. Stat. Ann. § 20-1-12.1(C) was unconstitutional because the legislature had no power to substitute a de novo hearing for an appeal from a judgment or order of the district court, and had no power to fix the time within which an appeal was heard by the court.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the broadcasters' appeal of the decision ordering them to disclose their confidential informants to the allegedly slandered individuals.

 

199 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State v. DeSantos


No. 10478


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


89 N.M. 458; 1976-NMSC-034; 553 P.2d 1265; 1976 N.M. LEXIS 825



June 29, 1976 


PRIOR HISTORY: See also 89 N.M. 351, 552 P.2d 787.



DISPOSITION: Conviction of unlawfully taking a vehicle affirmed, conviction of first-degree murder reversed and remanded for a new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the trial court (New Mexico), which convicted him of first-degree murder and unlawful taking of vehicle.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that the evidence was not sufficient to convict him. The trial court instructed the jury on four separate theories of first-degree murder: (1) willful, deliberate and premeditated murder; (2) felony murder; (3) murder by any act greatly dangerous to the lives of others, indicating a depraved mind regardless of human life; and (4) murder from a deliberate and premeditated design unlawfully and maliciously to effect the death of any human being. Upon review, the court found that the evidence, including the concealment of the body and defendant's flight after the crime, justified an instruction under N.M. Stat. Ann. § 40A-2-1(A)(1) on premeditated and deliberate murder. However, there was no evidence that showed defendant raped the victim, there was no evidence that defendant committed an act that was dangerous to more than one person, and there was no evidence that defendant intended to kill anyone other than the victim. Thus, there was not sufficient evidence to justify the jury instructions on the remaining theories of murder. Defendant was denied a fair trial because of the confusion caused by the jury instructions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for the unlawful taking of a vehicle, but it reversed his conviction for first-degree murder and remanded the cause to the trial court for a new trial.

 

200 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Serna v. Hodges


Nos. 10187, 10194


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


89 N.M. 351; 1976-NMSC-033; 552 P.2d 787; 1976 N.M. LEXIS 817



June 29, 1976 


PRIOR HISTORY: See also 89 N.M.   ,    P.2d   .



DISPOSITION: Writs made permanent.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent district judge in three separate criminal actions held that N.M. Stat. Ann. § 40A-29-2 (Supp. 1975) was unconstitutional. Pursuant to N.M. Const. art. VI, § 3, petitioner district attorney successfully sought alternative writs of prohibition to preclude respondent from proceeding in the criminal cases. Petitioner now sought to have the writs of prohibition made permanent by the exercise of the court's power of superintending control.


OVERVIEW: The consolidated cases raised the question whether the New Mexico death penalty statute, §40A-29-2, was unconstitutional under the Eighth Amendment to the Constitution of the United States or under N.M. Const. art. II, § 18. In the underlying criminal actions, respondent held by memorandum opinion that § 40A-29-2 was unconstitutional under a United States Supreme Court case, that the law prior to 1973 would apply, and that, therefore, the maximum penalty if defendants in the criminal cases were convicted of first degree murder would be life imprisonment. Petitioner alleged there was a conflict in the New Mexico judicial districts as to whether or not the death penalty as written by the legislature in 1973 was constitutional, that several persons in other judicial districts have been convicted of first degree murder and sentenced to death, and that allowing the ruling of respondent to stand would result in the rendering of unequal justice. The court held that the statute did not violate either the Eighth Amendment or N.M. Const. art. II, § 18. The procedures imposing the death penalty provided by N.M. Stat. Ann. § 40A-29-2 did not offend the constitutional provisions.


OUTCOME: The court made the alternative writs permanent.
